The Validity Dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Fuduli Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a fuduli marriage in dual capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on the validity of a marriage contracted by a fuduli in dual capacity, and analyse the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa rules the marriage valid without permission; Sahibayn require permission because the absolute command is customarily restricted to a compatible match.

While the prohibition of dual capacity is agreed upon, what happens if such a marriage is nonetheless performed? This lesson dives into the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The disagreement turns on whether an absolute command (mulaq) is taken literally or restricted by custom (urf). Understanding this is key to appreciating the methodology of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage is valid (nāfidh) immediately without need for permission. The contract takes effect from the moment it is made.
2
State the ruling of Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the marriage is not valid unless the principal (the one who gave the absolute command) gives permission. It is suspended (mawquf) on permission.
3
Identify the proof of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa takes the absolute command literally: if someone says 'marry me' without specifying, the agent has full authority, and any marriage contracted is valid.
4
Identify the proof of Sahibayn
Sahibayn argue that the absolute command is customarily understood to be restricted to marriage with a compatible match (kuf'). Since a fuduli may not ensure compatibility, the contract is not valid without the principal's approval.
5
Note the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the couple becomes husband and wife immediately. Under Sahibayn, they must wait; if permission is denied, the marriage is invalid.
The muftā bihi according to later authorities is the view of Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الولي والكفؤ
ه أو ولياً من جانب ووكيلاً من جانب. ولا يجوز أن يكون الواحد فضولياً كما إذا كان: أصيلاً وفضولياً، أو ولياً من جانب وفضولياً من جانب، أو وكيلاً من جانب وفضولياً من جانب، أو فضولياً من الجانبين. (وصح) أي نفذ من غير توقف، وهذا عنده، وقالا: لا يصح إلا إذا أجازه الآمر؛ لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف، وهو التزويج بالكفؤ.
Chapter of the Guardian and Compatibility. This: or a guardian from one side and an agent from the other. It is not permissible for one person to be a volunteer, such as when he is: a principal and a volunteer, or a guardian from one side and a volunteer from the other, or an agent from one side and a volunteer from the other, or a volunteer from both sides. (And it is valid) meaning it takes effect without delay, and this is according to him (Abu Hanifa), and they (the two) said: it is not valid unless the one who commanded gives permission, because the absolute (word) is understood according to custom, which is marriage to a compatible match.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a marriage when one person acts in a dual capacity, such as being both the principal and the fuduli (voluntary agent) or guardian and fuduli, etc. The text first states that it is not permissible for a single person to act as a fuduli in these combinations. Then it addresses the ruling if such a marriage is contracted: According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage is valid (nāfidh) without requiring subsequent permission, because the authority to contract marriage is effective from the moment of the contract. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Sahibayn) hold that it is not valid unless the principal (the one who had the right to contract) gives permission afterward. Their reasoning is that when an absolute command is given, it is customarily understood to be restricted to what is conventional—i.e., marriage to a compatible match. The passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn statement 'wa saḥḥa' (and it is valid).

Key Terms
فضولي (fudūlī): A person who acts on behalf of another without prior permission, i.e., a volunteer agent.
كفؤ (kuf'): Compatibility between spouses in matters of lineage, profession, religion, etc., considered for the wife's side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis for Sahibayn's ruling that the marriage is not valid unless the principal permits?
A) The absolute command is literal.
B) The absolute command is customarily restricted to marriage with a compatible match.
C) The marriage is forbidden.
D) The contract is defective.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a fuduli marriage in dual capacity is disputed: Abu Hanifa deems it valid immediately, while Sahibayn require the principal's permission, based on the interpretation of absolute commands.

Agent Marrying a Slave Woman: The Absolute vs. Custom
Dispute on validity of marriage by absolute agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute regarding an agent marrying a slave woman and explain the basis for each position.

Core Idea
An agent told to marry a 'woman' – absolute wording gives freedom; custom restricts.

This lesson examines a case where an absolute agency to marry a woman leads to a dispute within the Hanafi school. Abu Hanifa holds the marriage valid based on the literal absolute wording, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule it invalid using istihsan, considering custom and compatibility. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply usul principles in agency contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa: the marriage is valid because the agent followed the absolute wording of the authorization.
The authorization is absolute (muṭlaq) – no restriction to free women.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold the marriage invalid unless the principal permits it.
They rely on istihsan, not strict analogy.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the reasoning: custom restricts 'woman' to free women; also, compatibility (kafa'ah) is a right of the woman.
Istihsan here overrides the literal absolute because of custom and need.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Note that Abu Hanifa adheres to the literal absolute; he does not accept custom as a restrictor without evidence.
The dispute hinges on whether 'absolute' in agency is truly unrestricted.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa the marriage is valid; according to the Sahibayn it is invalid unless the principal approves.
Later Hanafi authorities (Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi) preferred the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text

نكاح أمة زوجها مَن أُمر بنكاح امرأة لأمره. وله : إن لفظ التوكيل مطلق، والمطلق يجر على إطلاقه، وقولهما: استحسان، واختاره أبو الليث والطحاوي، ودلّت المسألة على اعتبار الكفاءة من جانب المرأة عندهما. كذا في «الهداية» وشروحها.
The marriage of a slave woman married by someone who was commanded to marry a woman for his command. And he (Abu Hanifa) said: Indeed, the wording of agency is absolute, and the absolute is taken according to its absoluteness. And their (the two's) statement is istihsan. And Abu al-Layth and al-Tahawi chose (their view). And this issue indicates the consideration of compatibility from the woman's side according to them. Thus in al-Hidayah and its commentaries.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a free man authorizes an agent to marry a woman (without specifying free or slave). The agent then marries a slave woman belonging to someone else. According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage is valid because the authorization is absolute, and the absolute must be given effect as it is. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, however, rule it invalid using istihsan (juristic preference), reasoning that custom restricts 'woman' to free women, and also because compatibility (kafa'ah) is a consideration for the wife. Abu al-Layth and al-Tahawi preferred the view of the two. This passage also highlights that Sahibayn consider kafa'ah from the woman's side as a factor in determining the validity. The passage is an expansion (sharh) on the original matn statement.

Key Terms
أمة (amah): A female slave.
مطلق (muṭlaq): An absolute, unrestricted term in the context of agency.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference—a method of reasoning that prefers a ruling due to custom, need, or equity over strict analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Wakeel Marrying a Slave-Girl: Absolute Agency vs. Istihsan
Exposition of ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on a wakeel marrying a slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wakeel marrying a slave-girl when ordered to marry a woman, explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the principle that absolute agency is carried upon its absoluteness unless custom (urf) intervenes.

Core Idea
An absolute agency permits marrying a slave-girl; the Sahibayn use istihsan to restrict 'woman' to free women.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the scope of absolute agency in marriage contracts. When a wakeel is ordered simply to 'marry a woman' and he marries a slave-girl, does the contract hold? Abu Hanifa says yes—the absolute wording must be upheld. The two companions say no—custom dictates that 'woman' implies a free woman. We will analyze their proofs, the practical consequence, and the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a wakeel marrying a slave-girl to his principal who ordered him to marry a woman (without specification). The dispute is whether this marriage is valid or invalid.
The wakeel followed the literal wording, but the Sahibayn consider custom (urf) as a restricting factor.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds the marriage is valid (sahih). His proof: the wording of the agency is absolute (mutlaq), and the absolute must be carried upon its absoluteness (al-mutlaq yujra 'ala itlaqihi). Since 'woman' linguistically includes both free and slave, the wakeel has not violated his mandate.
This is a direct application of a Hanafi usul principle regarding absolute expressions.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold the marriage is invalid. Their proof: istihsan (juristic preference). Custom (urf) indicates that when someone says 'marry a woman', a free woman is intended. They restrict the absolute wording based on prevalent practice.
Istihsan here is a form of qiyas khafi—a hidden analogy that departs from the literal meaning due to custom.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi and al-Tahawi chose Abu Hanifa's view. Thus the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that the marriage is valid.
Even though the Sahibayn's view is weaker in fatwa, it remains a legitimate position within the school, based on istihsan.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if a wakeel marries a slave-girl, the marriage is valid per Abu Hanifa, invalid per Sahibayn. In practice, fatwa is given according to Abu Hanifa, so the marriage is upheld.
Also, the dispute highlights the role of 'urf in restricting absolute expressions in Hanafi methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نكاح أمة زوجها مَن أُمر بنكاح امرأة لأمره نكاح أمةٍ زوجها مَن أُمِرَ بنكاح امرأة) وله : إن لفظ التوكيل مطلق ، والمطلقُ يجر على إطلاقه، وقولهما: استحسان، واختاره أبو الليث والطحاوي ، ودلّت المسألة على اعتبار الكفاءة من جانب المرأة عندهما. كذا في «الهداية»، وشروحها. [١] قوله : أمة ؛ يشمل المكاتبة وأم الولد، وكذا يصح إنكاحه بالعمياء ومقطوعة اليدين، أو مفلوجة، أو مجنونة، أو صغيرة لا تجامع ؛ لإطلاق التوكيل كذا في «الفتح»، زاد في «البحر»: أو كتابية أو من حلف بطلاقها، أو آلى منها، أو في عدة الموكل ، أو بغبن فاحش في المهر بنكاح امرأة). (٢) قوله : بنكاح امرأة ؛ أي مطلقة غير معينة، فإن أمره بنكاح معينة أو بحرة، أو بأمة فخالف، أو أمرته المرأة بتزويجها ولم تعين فزوجها من غير كفء، أو وكله رجل بتزويج امرأة مطلقاً فزوجه بنته الصغيرة لا يصح النكاح في هذه الصور اتفاقاً ؛ لوجود المخالفة، أو التهمة، أو انتفاء الكفاءة المعتبرة .اتفاقا كذا في «الدر المختار) ، و«حواشیه». A slave-girl married by someone who was ordered to marry a woman for his order (the marriage of a slave-girl by one ordered to marry a woman) — And for him (Abu Hanifa): Indeed, the wording of the agency is absolute, and the absolute is carried upon its absoluteness. And their statement (of the two companions): istihsan. And Abu al-Layth and al-Tahawi chose (Abu Hanifa's view). And the issue indicates the consideration of compatibility from the woman's side according to them. Likewise in al-Hidayah and its commentaries. [1] His statement: 'a slave-girl' includes the mukatabah and umm walad, and similarly his marrying a blind woman, one with hands cut off, paralyzed, insane, or a minor who does not engage in intercourse is valid because of the absolute agency. Likewise in al-Fath; al-Bahr added: or a kitabiyyah, or one who he swore divorce upon her, or he made ila' from her, or in the iddah of the principal, or with a gross dower disparity in the marriage of a woman). (2) His statement: 'by marriage of a woman' means an absolute, unspecified woman. For if he ordered him to marry a specified woman, or a free woman, or a slave-girl, and he violated, or the woman ordered him to marry her and he married her to a non-match, or a man appointed him to marry a woman absolutely and he married his minor daughter to him, the marriage is not valid in these cases by agreement due to violation, suspicion, or absence of considered compatibility. Similarly in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its glosses. [3] His statement: 'for his order' means any order after he was free. And restricting the issue to the commander, as in al-Hidayah, is incidental, following what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Muhammad from Ya'qub from Abu Hanifa: concerning a commander from the Quraysh commanders: he ordered me to marry a woman, so I married a slave-girl belonging to someone else to him; he said: it is valid. Abu Hanifa set the issue for himself out of humility, making himself the commanded one. The ruling does not differ whether the principal is a commander or not, Quraysh or not, as long as he is free. He only restricted with 'a slave-girl belonging to someone else' because if he married his own slave-girl, it is not valid by consensus due to suspicion. Mentioned in Jami' Qadi Khan. Likewise in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage. The matn states that if a man is appointed as a wakeel to marry a woman, and he marries a slave-girl to him instead, the ruling: According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage is valid because the wording of the agency is absolute (mutlaq), and the absolute must be taken literally. The wakeel has followed the order exactly, as 'woman' includes both free and slave. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it invalid based on istihsan (juristic preference): custom dictates that when a person is ordered to marry a woman, a free woman is intended. Abu al-Layth and al-Tahawi chose Abu Hanifa's view. The text then clarifies that 'a slave-girl' includes mukatabah, umm walad, etc., and it is also valid to marry a blind, disabled, insane, or minor girl due to the absolute agency. The exception is if the agency is specified (e.g., a particular woman or a free woman), or if the wakeel marries his own slave-girl, which is invalid by consensus due to suspicion. The note on 'for his order' explains that the issue is not restricted to commanders; it applies to any free principal. The example of a Quraysh commander is due to humility of Abu Hanifa. The key takeaway: absolute agency permits marrying a slave-girl unless specified otherwise; compatibility (kafa'ah) is considered from the woman's side according to the two companions.

Key Terms
التوكيل (al-tawkīl): Agency; the act of appointing someone to act on one's behalf. Here, it is absolute (mutlaq) without specification.
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) based on custom or necessity. Here, the two companions use istihsan to restrict the absolute agency.
الكفاءة (al-kafā'ah): Compatibility in marriage; here, the two companions consider it from the woman's side, meaning the woman must be compatible to the man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An absolute agency in marriage is taken literally; the Sahibayn's istihsan based on custom is overruled by the mufta bihi, which upholds the absolute wording.

The Binding Authority of Father and Grandfather in Marrying Minors with Gross Dower Disparity
Explanation of guardians' authority in minor marriage with gross dower disparity and internal Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the father/grandfather marrying a minor with gross dower disparity or to a non-match, explain why it is binding, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the minor's option after puberty.

Core Idea
Father/grandfather's absolute authority: their marriage of a minor is binding even with gross dower disparity; no option after puberty.

In this passage, we examine the specific authority of the father and grandfather (in the absence of the father) to marry a minor with a gross dower disparity (ghabn fāḥish) or to a non-match. The matn declares that such a marriage is valid and binding (lāzim), and the minor has no right to annul it after puberty. However, this ruling is not without internal debate: the two companions (Sahibayn) dissent, granting the minor the option (khiyār). Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi approach to guardianship (wilāyah) and the balance between authority and protection.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Abu Hanifa holds the father/grandfather's marriage of a minor with gross dower disparity or to a non-match is valid and binding (sahih lazim). The minor has no right of annulment after puberty (no khiyar al-bulugh).
This is the position presented in the matn.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: they hold that such a marriage gives the minor the right to annul upon reaching puberty.
The text states 'khilāfan lahumā' (contrary to the two).
3
Follow the rival's implied proof
The Sahibayn's objection is based on potential harm to the minor: a gross dower disparity or marriage to a non-match could be detrimental, so the minor should have the option to annul.
The text does not elaborate but this is the logical basis.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that the father and grandfather possess 'complete opinion and perfect compassion' (wāfirā al-ra’y kāmilā al-shafaqa). Their decisions are inherently in the minor's best interest, so no option is needed. However, if they are known for bad judgment, the marriage is invalid by consensus.
The text mentions the exception: if they are known for bad choice, it is invalid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the minor cannot annul the marriage; under the Sahibayn, the minor can annul. The mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) is Abu Hanifa's view, but the Sahibayn's view is acknowledged.
This difference affects real-life cases where a minor wants to dissolve the marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب الولي والكفؤ وإنكاح الأب والجد عند عدم الأب الصغير والصغيرة بغبن فاحش بالمهر، أو من غير كفؤ لا لغيرهما) : أي لا يصح لغيرِ الأب والجد إنكاحُ الصغير والصغيرة بغبن فاحش في المهر، أو من غير كفؤ اتفاقاً، وجواز إنكاحهما للآبِ والجد بالغبن الفاحش، أو من غير كفؤ مذهب أبي حنيفة الله خلافاً لهما : أي لو فعل الأب أو الجد عند عدم الأب لا يكون للصغير والصغيرة حق الفسخ بعــد البلوغ [١]قوله : وإنكاح ؛ عطف على قوله : (نكاح أمة» : أي صح إنكاح الأب الصغير أو الصغيرة، وكذا إنكاح الجد عند عدم الأب بغبن فاحش في المهر بالزيادة في جانبه والنقصان في جانبها. والمراد بالغبن الفاحش : ما لا يتغابن الناس بمثله. فهذا النكاح صحيح لازم حتى لا يكون لهما الخيار بعد البلوغ ؛ لأنهما وافرا الرأي كاملا الشفقة فيلزم انكاحهما بأي وجه كان نعم ؛ إن كانا معروفين بسوء الاختيار فسقاً ومجانةً لا يصح اتفاقاً. وكذا يلزم إنكاح المولى الصغير أو الصغيرة المرقوقين حتى لو اعتقهما بعد ذلك ، ثم بلغا لا يثبت لهما خيار البلوغ لكمال ولاية المولى. [٢]قوله : لا لغيرهما ؛ ظاهره : أنه لو زوَّجَ غير الأب والجد : كالأخ مثلاً الصغير بامرأة أدنى منه لا يجوز، وخدشه الشَّرنبلالي بما مرَّ أن الكفاءة لا تعتبر في حق الرجل. وأجيب عنه : بأن معنى عدم اعتبار الكفاءة هاهنا أن الرجل لو زَوَّج نفسه من امرأة دنية ليس للولي حق الاعتراض، فأما إنكاح الولي الصغير بغير الكفء فلا يجوز. (۱) غبن فاحش : إذا جاوزت الزيادة ما يُعتادُ مثله. ينظر : ((المصباح»(ص٤٦٤).
The Book of Marriage, Chapter of Guardian and Compatibility. And (the marriage conducted by) the father and grandfather in the absence of the father of a minor boy and minor girl with a gross dower disparity, or to a non-match, is not (valid) for others besides them (i.e., it is not valid for other guardians). That is, it is not valid for anyone other than the father and grandfather to marry the minor boy and girl with gross dower disparity or to a non-match by agreement. And the permissibility of both (father and grandfather) marrying with gross dower disparity or to a non-match is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Sahibayn). That is, if the father or grandfather (in the absence of the father) does so, the minor boy and girl have no right of annulment after puberty. [1] His statement: 'And (the marriage conducted by) the father' is conjoined to his statement: 'marriage of a slave-girl.' That is, the marriage by the father of a minor boy or minor girl, and similarly by the grandfather in the absence of the father, with gross dower disparity (excess from his side, deficiency from her side) is valid. The meaning of gross dower disparity is what people do not ordinarily tolerate. So this marriage is valid and binding such that they have no option after puberty, because they (father/grandfather) are perfect in opinion and complete in compassion, so their marriage is binding in any manner. However, if they are known for bad choice (due to wickedness and foolishness), it is not valid by agreement. Similarly, the marriage of the master of a minor slave boy or minor slave girl is binding; even if he afterwards frees them and they reach puberty, they do not have the option of puberty due to the complete guardianship of the master. [2] His statement: 'not for others besides them': its apparent meaning is that if someone other than the father and grandfather, like the brother, marries a minor to a woman lower than him, it is not valid. And al-Shurunbulali noted a discrepancy with what has passed that compatibility is not considered in the right of the man. It was answered: the meaning of non-consideration of compatibility here is that if a man marries himself to a lowly woman, the guardian has no right to object; however, the guardian marrying a minor to a non-match is not valid. (1) Gross dower disparity: when the excess exceeds what is customary. Look at al-Misbah, p. 464.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage. The matn states that the father and grandfather (in the absence of the father) have the authority to marry a minor (boy or girl) with a gross dower disparity or to a non-match, and this marriage is binding. Other guardians (like the brother) cannot do so by agreement. Abu Hanifa holds that the father/grandfather's marriage is binding (lazim) and the minor has no option to annul after puberty. The two companions (Sahibayn) disagree: they would grant the minor the right of annulment (khiyar al-bulugh) in such cases. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is that the father and grandfather have complete opinion and compassion, so their decisions are binding. However, if they are known for bad judgment or immorality, their marriage is not valid by consensus. Similarly, the master's marriage of his minor slaves is binding. The gross dower disparity is defined as what people do not ordinarily tolerate. The text also clarifies that compatibility (kafa'ah) is not considered from the man's side when he marries himself, but for a guardian marrying a minor, it is considered because the minor cannot object.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fāḥish): Gross dower disparity; defined as a deviation in dower beyond what people ordinarily tolerate.
الولي (al-walī): Guardian; here specifically the father and grandfather who have full authority to marry minors.
الخيار (al-khiyār): Option; here, the option to annul the marriage after attaining puberty (khiyar al-bulugh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the marriage is harmful to him.
B) No, because the grandfather has complete guardianship and the marriage is binding.
C) Only if the grandfather was drunk.
D) Yes, if the dower was too low.

Key Takeaway
The father and grandfather's marriage of a minor with gross dower disparity is binding because of their complete authority; the Sahibayn's dissent highlights the tension between authority and protection.

Marriage of Minors by Father or Grandfather with Ghubn Fahish or Non-Kuf'
Ruling on validity and binding nature of marriage of minors by father/grandfather despite defects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity and binding nature of a marriage of a minor by the father or grandfather with a gross discrepancy in the mahr or to a non-compatible spouse, and explain why this authority is exclusive to these guardians.

Core Idea
Father and grandfather may marry a minor even with gross mahr discrepancy or to a non-kuf' spouse; the marriage is binding with no option of puberty.

This passage from the chapter on guardianship and compatibility addresses the special authority of the father and grandfather over the marriage of minors. It clarifies that while other guardians cannot make such contracts with defects, the father and grandfather's decision is binding due to their presumed complete opinion and compassion, unless they are known for poor judgment. The passage also highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds the marriage is binding, while the Sahibayn disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their authority
Recognize that the ruling applies specifically to the father and grandfather (in the absence of the father). Other guardians like brothers do not have this authority. Note the text says 'لا لغيرهما' (not for others besides them).
The father and grandfather are considered to have complete opinion (وافرا الرأي) and perfect compassion (كاملا الشفقة).
2
Identify the defects
The two defects discussed are ghubn fahish (gross discrepancy in mahr) and non-kuf' (incompatibility of the spouse). Determine whether these defects are present in the scenario.
Ghubn fahish is defined as 'what people do not overlook in transactions' – a significant deviation from the customary mahr.
3
State the ruling for father/grandfather
If the father or grandfather marries the minor with either defect, the marriage is valid and binding (sahih lazim). The minor has no right of annulment (khiyar al-bulugh) after puberty.
This is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, as identified in the text.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: they hold that such a marriage is not binding, and the minor retains the right to annul. Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The text says 'خلافاً لهما' (contrary to the two), indicating the majority position in the school is Abu Hanifa's.
5
Apply the exception
If the father or grandfather is known for bad choice due to transgression (fisq) or foolishness (majanah), then the marriage is not valid by consensus – even for them.
This exception underscores that the authority is conditional on trustworthiness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب الولي والكفؤ

وإنكاح الأب والجد عند عدم الأب الصغير والصغيرة بغبن فاحش بالمهر، أو من غير كفؤ لا لغيرهما

أي إن وُكِّلَ أن يزوجه امرأةً فزوجه أمةً صح خلافاً لهما.

(وإنكاح الأب والجد عند عدم الأب الصغيرَ والصَّغيرةَ بغبن فاحش (۱) بالمهر، أو من غير كفؤ لا لغيرهما) : أي لا يصح لغيرِ الأب والجد إنكاحُ الصغير والصغيرة بغبن فاحش في المهر، أو من غير كفؤ اتفاقاً، وجواز إنكاحهما للآبِ والجد بالغبن الفاحش، أو من غير كفؤ مذهب أبي حنيفة الله خلافاً لهما : أي لو فعل الأب أو الجد عند عدم الأب لا يكون للصغير والصغيرة حق الفسخ بعــد البلوغ

[١]قوله : وإنكاح ؛ عطف على قوله : (نكاح أمة» : أي صح إنكاح الأب الصغير أو الصغيرة، وكذا إنكاح الجد عند عدم الأب بغبن فاحش في المهر بالزيادة في جانبه والنقصان في جانبها.
والمراد بالغبن الفاحش : ما لا يتغابن الناس بمثله.
فهذا النكاح صحيح لازم حتى لا يكون لهما الخيار بعد البلوغ ؛ لأنهما وافرا الرأي كاملا الشفقة فيلزم انكاحهما بأي وجه كان نعم ؛ إن كانا معروفين بسوء الاختيار فسقاً ومجانةً لا يصح اتفاقاً.
وكذا يلزم إنكاح المولى الصغير أو الصغيرة المرقوقين حتى لو اعتقهما بعد ذلك ،
ثم بلغا لا يثبت لهما خيار البلوغ لكمال ولاية المولى.
[٢]قوله : لا لغيرهما ؛ ظاهره : أنه لو زوَّجَ غير الأب والجد : كالأخ مثلاً الصغير بامرأة أدنى منه لا يجوز، وخدشه الشَّرنبلالي بما مرَّ أن الكفاءة لا تعتبر في حق الرجل. وأجيب عنه : بأن معنى عدم اعتبار الكفاءة هاهنا أن الرجل لو زَوَّج نفسه من امرأة دنية ليس للولي حق الاعتراض، فأما إنكاح الولي الصغير بغير الكفء فلا يجوز.
(۱) غبن فاحش : إذا جاوزت الزيادة ما يُعتادُ مثله. ينظر : ((المصباح»(ص٤٦٤).
The book of marriage. The chapter of the guardian and compatibility. And the marriage of the father and the grandfather, in the absence of the father, of the minor boy and minor girl with a gross discrepancy in the dower, or from a non-compatible man, is not valid for others besides them. That is, if he is appointed to marry a woman to him and he marries him to a slave woman, it is valid, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). (And the marriage of the father and grandfather, in the absence of the father, of the minor boy and minor girl with a gross discrepancy in the dower, or from a non-compatible man, is not valid for others besides them): That is, it is invalid for other than the father and grandfather to marry the minor boy or girl with a gross discrepancy in the dower or from a non-compatible man, by consensus. And the permissibility of their marriage by the father and grandfather with a gross discrepancy or from a non-compatible man is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Meaning, if the father or grandfather (in the absence of the father) does so, the minor boy or girl has no right of annulment after puberty. [1] His saying: 'And the marriage' is conjuncted to his saying 'marriage of a slave woman': that is, the marriage of the father of the minor boy or girl is valid, and likewise the marriage of the grandfather in the absence of the father with a gross discrepancy in the dower by increase on his side or decrease on her side. And what is meant by gross discrepancy is that which people do not overlook in transactions. So this marriage is valid and binding such that they have no option after puberty, because they (father and grandfather) are complete in opinion and perfect in compassion, so their marriage is binding in whatever manner. Yes, if they are known for bad choice due to transgression and foolishness, it is not valid by consensus. Likewise, the marriage of the master of a minor male or female slave is binding, such that even if he frees them afterwards and they reach puberty, they have no option of puberty due to the completeness of the master's authority. [2] His saying: 'not for others besides them'; its apparent meaning is that if someone other than the father and grandfather marries a minor boy to a woman inferior to him, it is not permissible. Al-Sharnablali challenged this with what has passed that compatibility is not considered with respect to the man. And it was answered: that the meaning of non-consideration of compatibility here is that if a man marries himself to a low-born woman, the guardian has no right to object; but as for the guardian marrying a minor to a non-compatible man, it is not permissible. (1) Gross discrepancy: when the excess exceeds what is customary. See al-Misbah p.464.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the marriage of minors (saghir or saghirah) by their father or grandfather. The text states that the father and grandfather (in the absence of the father) may marry a minor with a gross discrepancy (ghubn fahish) in the mahr or to a non-compatible (ghayr kuf') spouse, and such a marriage is valid and binding. However, this right is exclusive to the father and grandfather; others (like brothers) do not have this authority. The passage also mentions the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that such a marriage is valid and binding, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. The commentary clarifies that the marriage is valid because the father and grandfather are considered to have complete opinion (waafir al-ra'y) and perfect compassion (kaamil al-shafaqa). It also notes that if the father or grandfather are known for bad choice (su' al-ikhtiyar) due to fisq or foolishness, then the marriage is not valid by consensus. The commentary also discusses the master's authority over minor slaves. The sub-commentary addresses a point by al-Sharnablali about kafa'ah not being considered for the man, but clarifies that this refers to the man marrying himself, not the guardian marrying a minor girl to a non-kuf'.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghubn fahish): A gross discrepancy in the mahr (dower) that people would not overlook in transactions. Specifically defined as an increase beyond what is customary.
كفء (kuf'): Compatibility or suitability in marriage, especially lineage, religion, profession, etc. Here, non-kuf' means the spouse is not considered socially equivalent.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage; in this context, the right of the minor after puberty to annul the marriage if married by someone other than father or grandfather with ghubn or non-kuf'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a father marries his minor daughter to a non-compatible man (ghayr kuf') with a gross discrepancy in the mahr?
A) The marriage is invalid and must be annulled immediately.
B) The marriage is valid and binding; the daughter has no option of puberty.
C) The marriage is valid only if the daughter consents after puberty.
D) The marriage is valid but the daughter has the option to annul it after puberty.

Key Takeaway
The father or grandfather's marriage of a minor with ghubn fahish or to a non-kuf' spouse is valid and binding, and the minor has no option of puberty.

Nikah — Marriage

Marriage of Minors by Non-Father Guardians: Absolute Invalidity Refined
Critical refinement of a misinterpretation in the sharh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a marriage being merely non-binding (mawquf) and absolutely invalid (batil) in the case of a minor married by a guardian other than the father/grandfather with ghubn fahish or to a non-kuf', and state the correct Hanafi ruling with its evidence.

Core Idea
A minor's marriage by a non-father guardian with gross disparity is absolutely invalid, not merely reversible.

The matn of al-Hidayah states that a minor married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather has the right to annul after puberty. This phrasing might suggest the marriage is valid but not binding. However, the super-commentator here exposes a critical error: the reliable Hanafi position is that such a marriage is absolutely invalid (batil) from the outset. This lesson unpacks the debate, the evidence, and the authoritative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting views
Note the two positions: (1) The commentator whose sharh is being refined, who implied the marriage is valid but non-binding. (2) The super-commentator and the majority of reliable books, who hold the marriage is absolutely invalid.
The error is termed 'wahm' (illusion) by al-Taftazani and Ibn al-Kamal.
2
Locate the key evidence from the reliable books
Examine the quotation from al-Muhit, stating consensus that a guardian other than the father/grandfather cannot increase or decrease the dower to a degree that people would not overlook. Also note the fatwa of Abu al-Layth rejecting ratification.
Consensus (ijma') is a primary proof.
3
Analyze the response of the later commentators
Some later scholars (e.g., al-Qahistani) cited transmissions that seemed to allow validity. The super-commentator (Ibn Abidin) rebuts these as weak and contrary to the established madhhab.
Ibn Abidin emphasizes that a statement by 'some' does not constitute a reliable transmission from the Imams.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The authoritative ruling is that the marriage is batil (invalid) and cannot become valid even with subsequent consent. This is based on zahir al-riwayah and the weight of early authorities.
Hanafi position: hukm = batil, not mawquf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن فعل غيرُهما ، فلهما أن يفسخا بعد البلوغ).

[١] قوله : فلهما أن يفسخا ... الخ ؛ فيه بحث ذكره التفتازاني في «التلويح (۲) وابن الكمال (۳) : وهو أن هذا يقتضي أن يصح إنكاح غير الأب والجد الصغير أو الصغيرة من غير الكفء أو بغبن فاحش، ولا يكون لازماً مع أنه لا يصح مطلقاً لا لازماً ولا موقوفاً ، صرح به في عامة الكتب المعتبرة ، فهذا وهم من الشارح له منشؤه حمل الصحة في المتن في مسألة إنكاح الأب والجد على الملزوم.
وتوجيه النفي الواقع في قوله : لا لغيرهما على نفي اللزوم فقط : ، وهو ما في المعتبرات ، قال في «المحيط»: أجمعوا على أن غيرها لو زاد أو نقص بحيث لا يتغابن الناس بمثله لا يجوز النكاح ، ولو زوج غيرهما من غير الكفء لا روايــة فـيـه عـن أصحابنا، وقال الفضلي : على قياس مسألة التقصير في المهر ينبغي أن لا يجوز بلا خلاف.
وفي فتاوي أبي الليث»: إن زوج غيرهما صغيرة من غير كفء، ثم أدركت فأجازت لم يجز ؛ لأن نكاح هؤلاء من غير الكفء لا يجوز. وأجاب عنه القهستاني (٤) وغيرُه : بأن صحة إنكاح غيرهما بالغبن الفاحش نقلها (۱) وَهَّمَ التفتازاني في «التلويح»(٢ : ٣٦٨ - ٣٦٩) ، وابن كمال في «الاصلاح»(ق٤٤ /ب)، والحصكفي في (الدر المختار (۲) : (٣٠٦ صدر الشريعة في قوله : فلهما أن يفسخا بعد البلوغ، بأنه إن كان المزوج غير الأب والجد لا يصح من غير كفؤ أو بغبن فاحش أصلا. وأجاب عن قولهم القهستاني في جامع الرموز (۱) : (۲۷۹)، وشيخ زاده في مجمع الأنهر» (۱ : : ٣٤٦) : في «الجواهر) : ويصح تزويج غيرهما بغبن فاحش، كما قال بعضهم . وفي «الجوامع وبغير كفء على ما قال بعضهم، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز. وهذا يدل على وجود الرواية لا على عدمها كما لا يخفى فلا وجه لرد صاحب «الإصلاح»، و«التلويح». ورد قولهما ابن عابدين في رد المحتار) (۲) : (٣٠٦ : وفيه نظر؛ فإن ما كان قولاً لبعض لا يلزم أن يكون فيه رواية عن أئمة المذهب ولا سيما إذا كان قولاً ضعيفاً مخالفاً لما في المشايخ مشاهير كتب المذهب المعتمدة.
And if someone other than them (father/grandfather) does so, then they (the minors) may annul after puberty. [1] His saying: 'then they may annul after puberty...' contains a discussion mentioned by al-Taftazani in al-Talwih and Ibn al-Kamal: that this implies that the marriage of a minor by other than the father and grandfather with a non-compatible man or with gross discrepancy is valid but not binding, whereas it is not valid at all, neither binding nor suspended, as stated in generally reliable books. So this is a mistake by the commentator, arising from his taking 'validity' in the text concerning the father and grandfather as meaning binding. And the interpretation of the negation in his saying 'not for others besides them' as only negation of binding nature is what is in the reliable books. He said in al-Muhit: They agreed that if others increase or decrease to an extent that people do not overlook, the marriage is not permissible. And if others marry (a minor) to a non-compatible man, there is no transmission (riwaya) from our companions. Al-Fadli said: By analogy to the issue of deficiency in the dower, it should be impermissible without dispute. And in the Fatawa of Abu al-Layth: If someone else marries a minor girl to a non-compatible man, then she reaches maturity and ratifies it, it is not valid, because the marriage of such a person to a non-compatible man is not permissible. Al-Qahistani and others responded that the validity of marriage by others with gross discrepancy has been transmitted. Al-Taftazani and Ibn al-Kamal considered the statement of Sadr al-Shari'a as mistaken: that if the one who contracts the marriage is other than father/grandfather, it is not valid at all from a non-compatible or with gross discrepancy. Al-Qahistani in Jami' al-Rumuz and Shaykh Zada in Majma' al-Anhur responded: In al-Jawahir: it is valid for others to marry with gross discrepancy, as some said. And in al-Jawami': and with non-compatible as some said, but the correct is that it is not permissible. This indicates the existence of a transmission, not its absence, so there is no ground for rejecting by the author of al-Islah and al-Talwih. Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar rejected their statement: There is consideration; what is a statement of some does not necessarily imply a transmission from the imams of the madhhab, especially if it is a weak statement contrary to what is in the well-known reliable books of the madhhab.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the super-commentator on the earlier sharh. It addresses the statement in the matn: 'If someone other than the father and grandfather marries the minor, then they (the minors) may annul after puberty.' This phrasing suggests that such a marriage is valid but not binding, which contradicts the well-known position in the madhhab that such a marriage is absolutely invalid (not valid at all). The super-commentator notes that al-Taftazani and Ibn al-Kamal pointed out this error. The correct view, as stated in al-Muhit and other reliable texts, is that if someone other than the father or grandfather marries a minor with a gross discrepancy in the dower or to a non-compatible spouse, the marriage is impermissible by consensus. There is even a fatwa from Abu al-Layth rejecting the validity of such a marriage even if the minor ratifies it after puberty. Some later scholars like al-Qahistani attempted to rescue the earlier commentator by citing transmissions that some allowed validity, but the super-commentator (likely Ibn Abidin) rejects this, stating that such isolated weak reports do not constitute a reliable transmission from the founding imams. Thus, the authoritative ruling is that a marriage of a minor by a guardian other than the father or grandfather with ghubn fahish or to a non-kuf' is absolutely invalid (batil), not merely non-binding.

Key Terms
وهم (wahm): Mistake or illusion; the super-commentator uses it to indicate an error by the earlier commentator in understanding the matn.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a marriage that is not immediately binding but depends on subsequent approval by the minor after puberty.
غبن فاحش (ghubn fahish): Gross discrepancy; a significant inequality in the dower that people would not normally overlook in similar transactions.
كفء (kuf'): Compatibility; the marital partner should be equal in lineage, religion, wealth, and profession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the super-commentator's conclusion regarding the marriage of a minor by a non-father/grandfather guardian with ghubn fahish?
A) The marriage is valid but the minor can annul after puberty.
B) The marriage is invalid (batil) and cannot become valid even with consent.
C) The marriage is valid if the minor consents after puberty.
D) The marriage is suspended (mawquf) until the minor decides.

Key Takeaway
Marriage of a minor by a guardian other than the father or grandfather, when accompanied by ghubn fahish or non-kuf', is absolutely invalid (batil), not merely voidable, and later consent does not cure it.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Marriage by Non-Father/Jud Guardians
Critical refinement of the correct ruling on marriage by non-father/grandfather guardians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position that a marriage by a non-father/grandfather guardian with ghubn fahish or non-kuf' is batil ab initio, and explain the intra-school ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A marriage by a non-father/grandfather guardian with ghubn fahish or non-kuf' is batil ab initio—not merely revocable.

This passage corrects a common misunderstanding of the matn's statement that the minor has the right to annul after puberty. Some thought this implies the marriage was valid but revocable. The correct Hanafi position, as emphasized by al-Taftazani and Ibn al-Kamal, is that such marriages are absolutely void from the start when there is a gross deficiency in dower or incompatibility. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the intra-school dissent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested element
The issue is whether a marriage contracted by a guardian other than the father or grandfather (ghayr al-ab wa al-jadd) is valid (sahih) when there is ghubn fahish or non-kuf'. The majority says it is batil; a minority says it is valid but not binding.
2
Follow the majority evidence
The majority relies on consensus (ijma) as reported in al-Muhit, stating that such marriages are not valid (la yajuz). There is no transmission (riwayah) from the companions for the contrary.
Consensus is a strong dalil in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the minority argument
The minority, cited in al-Jawahir and al-Jawami', holds that such marriages are valid (sahih) but not binding (ghayr lazim), by analogy with the father/grandfather's authority.
The minority argues by analogy (qiyas) to the case of the father/grandfather.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response is that the analogy fails because the father/grandfather have full wilayah (wilaya jami'ah), while others have limited authority. The majority texts explicitly negate validity, so the minority transmission is weak.
The concept of wilaya jami'ah is key to the rebuttal.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is absolute invalidity. The minor's right to annul in the matn refers to the case of father/grandfather, not others. The sharh's interpretation is an error.
Al-Marghinani and later authorities affirm the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : فلهما أن يفسخا ... الخ ؛ فيه بحث ذكره التفتازاني في «التلويح» وابن الكمال : وهو أن هذا يقتضي أن يصح إنكاح غير الأب والجد الصغير أو الصغيرة من غير الكفء أو بغبن فاحش، ولا يكون لازماً مع أنه لا يصح مطلقاً لا لازماً ولا موقوفاً ، صرح به في عامة الكتب المعتبرة ، فهذا وهم من الشارح له منشؤه حمل الصحة في المتن في مسألة إنكاح الأب والجد على الملزوم.

وتوجيه النفي الواقع في قوله : لا لغيرهما على نفي اللزوم فقط : ، وهو ما في المعتبرات ، قال في «المحيط»: أجمعوا على أن غيرها لو زاد أو نقص بحيث لا يتغابن الناس بمثله لا يجوز النكاح ، ولو زوج غيرهما من غير الكفء لا روايــة فـيـه عـن أصحابنا، وقال الفضلي : على قياس مسألة التقصير في المهر ينبغي أن لا يجوز بلا خلاف.
وفي فتاوي أبي الليث»: إن زوج غيرهما صغيرة من غير كفء، ثم أدركت فأجازت لم يجز ؛ لأن نكاح هؤلاء من غير الكفء لا يجوز. وأجاب عنه القهستاني وغيرُه : بأن صحة إنكاح غيرهما بالغبن الفاحش نقلها
(۱) وَهَّمَ التفتازاني في «التلويح»(٢ : ٣٦٨ - ٣٦٩) ، وابن كمال في «الاصلاح»(ق٤٤ /ب)، والحصكفي في (الدر المختار (۲) : (٣٠٦ صدر الشريعة في قوله : فلهما أن يفسخا بعد البلوغ، بأنه إن كان المزوج غير الأب والجد لا يصح من غير كفؤ أو بغبن فاحش أصلا. وأجاب عن قولهم القهستاني في جامع الرموز (۱) : (۲۷۹)، وشيخ زاده في مجمع الأنهر» (۱ : : ٣٤٦) : في «الجواهر) : ويصح تزويج غيرهما بغبن فاحش، كما قال بعضهم . وفي «الجوامع وبغير كفء على ما قال بعضهم، والصحيح أنه لا يجوز. وهذا يدل على وجود الرواية لا على عدمها كما لا يخفى فلا وجه لرد صاحب «الإصلاح»، و«التلويح». ورد قولهما ابن عابدين في رد المحتار) (۲) : (٣٠٦ : وفيه نظر؛ فإن ما كان قولاً لبعض لا يلزم أن يكون فيه رواية عن أئمة المذهب ولا سيما إذا كان قولاً ضعيفاً مخالفاً لما في المشايخ مشاهير كتب المذهب المعتمدة.
His statement: 'they have the right to annul after puberty' ... etc.; there is a discussion mentioned by al-Taftazani in al-Talwih and Ibn al-Kamal: that this implies that the marriage of a minor boy or a minor girl by someone other than the father or grandfather—when it is not with a compatible match or with a gross deficiency—is valid (sahih) but not binding (lazim), whereas [according to the correct view] it is not valid at all, neither binding nor suspended. This is clearly stated in the generally relied-upon books. So this is an error on the part of the commentator, originating from his interpreting 'validity' in the text in the case of the father/grandfather as meaning [the marriage is] binding. Contrary to that, and the interpretation of the negation occurring in his statement 'not for others' as denoting only non-bindingness, which is [found] in the reliable works. He said in al-Muhit: 'They have agreed that if someone other than them increases or decreases to such an extent that people would not overlook the like of it, the marriage is not valid; and if someone other than them marries [a minor] to a non-compatible match, there is no transmission about it from our companions.' And al-Fadli said: 'By analogy with the issue of deficiency in the dower, it should not be valid without dispute.' And in the Fatawa of Abu al-Layth: 'If someone other than them marries a minor girl to a non-compatible match, then she reaches puberty and consents, it is not valid, because the marriage of such [guardians] to a non-compatible match is not valid.' And al-Qahistani and others answered [the critic] that the validity of marriage by others with a gross deficiency is transmitted (1) Al-Taftazani in al-Talwih, Ibn Kamal in al-Islah, and al-Haskafi in al-Durr al-Mukhtar criticized Sadr al-Shari'a in his statement 'they have the right to annul after puberty', saying that if the one marrying is other than the father and grandfather, it is not valid at all when there is non-kafa'a or gross deficiency. They answered their statement [by citing] al-Qahistani in Jami' al-Rumuz and Shaykh Zada in Majma' al-Anhur: 'In al-Jawahir: the marriage of others with a gross deficiency is valid, as some said. And in al-Jawami': and with non-kafa'a according to what some said, and the correct view is that it is not valid. This indicates the existence of a transmission, not its non-existence, as is clear, so there is no basis for rejecting [the view] of the author of al-Islah and al-Talwih.' Their statement was refuted by Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar: 'There is consideration in it: for what is a statement of some [scholars] does not necessarily entail a transmission from the imams of the school, especially if it is a weak statement opposing what is in the books relied upon by the prominent [scholars].'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a critical note (hashiya) on the Sharh al-Wiqaya. The original matn stated that if a guardian other than the father or grandfather marries off a minor, the minor has the right to annul upon reaching puberty. The sharh interpreted this to mean that such a marriage is valid (sahih) but not binding (lazim). The commentator argues this is a misunderstanding (wahm). He cites al-Taftazani and Ibn al-Kamal, who point out that the correct Hanafi position is that such a marriage is absolutely invalid (batil) when there is a gross deficiency in dower (ghubn fahish) or inequality of status (ghayr kuf'). This is clearly stated in all reliable books. The attempted justification that the matn's negation (la) refers only to non-bindingness is rejected. The footnote discusses a minority transmission that such marriages are valid but revocable, but the majority opinion, as recorded in al-Muhit and other authoritative works, is that they are invalid from the outset. The text also mentions a fatwa of Abu al-Layth and a response by al-Qahistani, but Ibn Abidin refutes the minority view, affirming that the relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is absolute invalidity.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghubn fahish): Gross deficiency in mahr relative to the woman's like, such that people would not overlook it in commercial dealings.
كفء (kuf'): Equality in lineage, religiosity, profession, and other factors considered relevant for marital compatibility.
ولاية (wilayah): Guardianship authority to contract marriage on behalf of a minor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, if a guardian other than the father or grandfather marries a minor girl to a non-compatible man with a grossly deficient dower, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is valid but she may annul it upon puberty.
B) The marriage is invalid from the start (batil).
C) The marriage is suspended on her consent.
D) The marriage is valid and binding.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi position is that a marriage by a non-father/grandfather guardian, when there is a gross deficiency in dower or inequality of status, is absolutely invalid (batil) and cannot become valid by subsequent consent.

Invalidity of Marrying Two Women in One Contract by an Agent
Ruling on invalidity of marrying two women in a single contract when only one was commanded

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent marries two women in one contract and explain why it is invalid, distinguishing between absolute invalidity and non-binding interpretations.

Core Idea
Marrying two women in one contract when ordered to marry one is absolutely invalid for both.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario in Hanafi marriage law: a principal instructs his agent to marry him one woman, but the agent marries two women in a single contract. The classical texts rule that such a marriage is invalid, but there is a debate whether this means it is void (batil) or merely non-binding (ghayr lazim). The passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya clarifies that the correct view is absolute invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties
Recognize the principal (commanding a marriage), the agent (ma'mur), and the two women. The agent was told to marry one woman but married two in a single contract.
The key is that the agent exceeded his authority.
2
State the ruling as per the matn
The matn says: 'There is no marriage of one of the two women.' The commentator confirms both marriages are invalid.
Invalid means batil, not merely non-binding, according to the commentator.
3
Understand the reasoning
The invalidity arises because (a) the agent violated the command, (b) uncertainty (jahalah) as to which woman was intended, and (c) no basis to prioritize one over the other.
The three possibilities are all blocked.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Hidaya interprets the invalidity as non-binding (luzum), but the commentator rejects this and holds absolute invalidity (batil).
The commentator's view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا نكاح واحدة من اثنين زوجَهُما المأمور بواحدة" للآمر) : أي إن أمر آخر أن يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين بعقد واحد لا يصح نكاح كل واحدة منهما ، أما إذا زوج بعقدين فالأوّلُ صحيح دون الثاني. في «الجواهر» عن بعضهم، وبغير كفء نقلها في «الجامع» عن بعضهم، وهذا يدل على وجود الرواية، وفيه : أنه قول غير معتبر، والأصح بطلان إنكاح غيرهما بغبن فاحش ، ومن غير كفء من أصله، كما ذكره في «الكافي» وغيره.
فحمل كلام المصنف على قوله : ضعيف بعيد عن الشارح ، والحق أن
النفي في المتن محمول على نفي الصحة مطلقاً لا على نفي اللزوم.
[١) قوله ؛ ولا نكاح ؛ أي لا يصح نكاح واحدة من اثنتين فيما إذ أمره رجل بتزويج واحد، فتزوج المأمور اثنتين بعقد واحد ، والمراد من عدم الصحة عدم اللزوم، كما عبر عنه في «الهداية» (۱) ؛ وذلك لأنه لا وجه لتنفيذها للمخالفة ولا للتنفيذ في إحداهما غير معينة للجهالة، ولا للتنفيذ في إحداهما معينة لعدم الأولوية، فتعين

('There is no marriage of one of two women whom the agent married for one') meaning: if a man ordered another to marry him a woman, but he married two women with one contract, the marriage of each of them is not valid. However, if he married with two contracts, the first is valid and the second is not. In al-Jawahir from some, and for non-kafa' it is transmitted in al-Jami' from some, and this indicates the existence of a transmission. In it: that it is an unreliable statement, and the most correct is the nullity of marriage by others with gross deficiency and with non-kafa' from its origin, as mentioned in al-Kafi and others. Therefore, interpreting the author's statement as [the sharh does] is weak and far from the commentator, and the truth is that the negation in the text is taken as negation of validity absolutely, not negation of bindingness. (1) His statement: 'and there is no marriage'; meaning: the marriage of one of two women is not valid when a man ordered him to marry one, and the agent married two with one contract. What is meant by invalid is non-binding, as expressed in al-Hidaya; because there is no way to execute it due to violation [of command], nor to execute one unspecified because of uncertainty, nor to execute one specific because there is no priority, so invalidity is determined. (2) His statement: 'for one'; meaning unspecified, related to the agent; i.e., the one who was ordered to marry one woman. If he ordered him to marry two women in one contract and he married one, it is valid. Similarly, if he ordered him to marry a specific woman and he married another along with her in one contract, it is valid. As in al-Binaya.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling from the matn. The original text states: 'There is no marriage of one of two women whom an agent married when only one was commissioned.' The commentator clarifies: If a man orders his agent to marry him a woman, but the agent marries two women in a single contract, the marriage to each woman is invalid. If he marries them in two separate contracts, the first is valid and the second is invalid. The commentator then discusses the rationale: there is no way to execute either contract because of conflict with the command; if we try to choose one, it is unknown which was intended (jahalah), and if we arbitrarily pick one, there is no priority. Therefore, both are void. The passage also notes an alternative interpretation from al-Hidaya that 'invalid' here means 'non-binding' (luzum), but the commentator favors absolute invalidity because the contract violates the principal's instruction. The commentary concludes by clarifying that if the agent marries one woman correctly, that marriage is valid.

Key Terms
مأمور (ma'mur): An agent who is commanded by another (the principal) to contract a marriage.
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty regarding which of the two women was intended for marriage in the single contract.
لزوم (luzum): Binding nature of a contract; here some interpret 'invalid' as meaning 'non-binding' rather than void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator of 'Umda al-Ri'aya, what is the ruling when an agent marries two women in a single contract after being ordered to marry one?
A) The marriage is valid but non-binding.
B) Both marriages are absolutely invalid.
C) The marriage to the first woman is valid, the second invalid.
D) The marriage is valid if the women are of equal status.

Key Takeaway
When an agent marries two women in one contract contrary to the principal's command, both marriages are absolutely invalid due to violation of authority and uncertainty.

Agent Exceeds Authority: Marrying Two When Ordered One
Commentary on ruling when agent exceeds marriage authorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent marries two women while authorized one, and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) for the invalidity.

Core Idea
Exceeding agency in marriage invalidates the contract — both marriages are batil in one contract.

When you authorize someone to marry you to a single woman, and they marry you to two women in one contract, what happens? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that neither marriage is valid, based on the agent's violation and the impossibility of validly executing either. We'll explore the reasoning behind this rule and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the agent marrying two women in a single contract when authorized only one. The Hanafi ruling: both marriages are batil (invalid).
If two separate contracts are used, the first is sahih, the second batil.
2
Trace the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The text gives three reasons: executing both violates the mandate; executing one unspecified is impossible due to uncertainty (jahalah); executing one specified lacks preference (la awlawiyyah). All three are impossible, so invalidity is the only outcome.
This is a logical analysis, not a textual proof.
3
Distinguish the scenario with two separate contracts
If the agent marries in two separate contracts, the first is valid because it fits within authorization; the second is due to a new action exceeding the mandate.
The ruling hinges on the unity or multiplicity of the contract.
4
Acknowledge the weak alternative narration
Some transmitted a view that the marriage is valid but non-binding (ghayr lazim). However, this narration is considered weak and not relied upon.
The mufta bihi is absolute invalidity.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi
The operative position (mufta bihi) is that both marriages are batil in a single contract, consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.
This ruling is authoritative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١) قوله ؛ ولا نكاح ؛ أي لا يصح نكاح واحدة من اثنتين فيما إذ أمره رجل بتزويج واحد، فتزوج المأمور اثنتين بعقد واحد ، والمراد من عدم الصحة عدم اللزوم، كما عبر عنه في «الهداية» (۱) ؛ وذلك لأنه لا وجه لتنفيذها للمخالفة ولا للتنفيذ في إحداهما غير معينة للجهالة، ولا للتنفيذ في إحداهما معينة لعدم الأولوية، فتعين التفريق. There is no marriage of one of two women whom the agent married when he was ordered [to marry] one. Explanation: If he ordered someone to marry him a woman, and he married two women in one contract, the marriage of each of them is not valid. But if he married with two contracts, the first is valid, not the second. From al-Jawahir: from some [scholars], and regarding a non-compatible [match] transmitted in al-Jami' from some, indicating that there is a narration. But it is an unreliable statement; the correct view is that the marriage of other than them is invalid due to gross disadvantage [ghubn fahish], and from a non-compatible [marriage] from its origin, as mentioned in al-Kafi and others. So the author's statement is weak and far from the commentator; the truth is that the negation in the matn is absolute negation of validity, not negation of binding. [1] His statement: wa la nikaah: meaning that the marriage of one of two women is not valid when a man ordered him to marry one, and the agent married two in one contract. The meaning of invalidity is non-binding, as expressed in al-Hidayah. This is because there is no way to execute both due to violation, nor to execute one unspecified due to ignorance, nor to execute one specified due to lack of preference, thus (the only option is) separation. [2] His statement: bi-wahidah: meaning unspecified, relating to the agent; i.e., the one ordered to marry one. If he ordered (him to marry) two in one contract and he married one, it is permissible. Similarly, if he ordered (him to marry) one specific woman and he married her together with another in one contract, it is permissible. As in al-Binayah.

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a man appoints an agent to marry him one woman, but the agent marries two women. The ruling is that if the agent marries both in a single contract, neither marriage is valid (batil). If he marries them in separate contracts, the first marriage is valid and the second is invalid. The reasoning is that executing both would violate the mandate; executing one without specification is impossible due to uncertainty; executing one with specification lacks priority. The text also mentions a weak narration suggesting the marriage is valid but non-binding, but the relied-upon position is absolute invalidity. The commentator clarifies that the negation in the matn refers to negation of validity (sihha), not just binding (luzum).

Key Terms
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person appointed as agent to perform the marriage contract on behalf of another.

A) Both marriages are valid

C) Both are invalid
D) The agent chooses which is valid

Key Takeaway
When an agent exceeds his marriage mandate by contracting two unions in one contract, both are invalid (batil) due to the impossibility of partial enforcement.

The Hanafi Definition of Mahr and the Shafi'i Dispute
Definition of mahr, Shafi'i dissent, and refutation of a story.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mahr, explain why teaching Quran is not valid as mahr, and respond to the Shafi'i argument using the story of Adam.

Core Idea
Hanafi mahr must be property—teaching Quran transfers reward but is not a legal equivalent of property.

This passage opens the chapter on mahr (dower) with a clear Hanafi definition: mahr is property (mal) given to the wife in exchange for the right to marital intimacy. However, the Shafi'i school holds that non-property benefits like teaching the Quran also qualify. The author then addresses a potential objection from a story about Adam and Hawwa, providing a Hanafi response that upholds the property requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of mahr
Find the definition given in the text: mahr is the property brought from husband to wife as compensation for the benefits of her sexual organ. Note the key term 'mal' (property).
The arabic phrase is 'عبارة عمَّا يساقُ إلى الزوجة من الزوج عوضاً لمنافع بضعها'.
2
Contrast the Shafi'i position
The text states that al-Shafi'i does not require mahr to be property; teaching the Quran and similar acts are sufficient. Understand the difference: for Shafi'is, any benefit with value can be mahr.
The Shafi'i view is based on a broader interpretation of 'value', including non-tangible benefits.
3
Analyse the Adam story objection and the Hanafi response
Ibn al-Jawzi's story says Adam gave salat as mahr, which seems to contradict the property condition. The Hanafi response explains that if the action is performed with the intention of it being mahr, the reward transfers to the wife by analogy to a hired reciter. This is an exception, not a general rule.
The response does not overrule the general principle; it shows that the reward of deeds can become property through intention, but the default is physical property.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
For Hanafis, if a marriage is contracted with teaching Quran as mahr, the marriage is valid but the wife receives mahr al-mithl (fair dower), not the teaching. For Shafi'is, the teaching itself is valid and fulfils the mahr obligation.
The practical difference lies in what the wife can claim if the teaching is not performed or if the marriage ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المهر [1] قوله : باب المهر ؛ أي هذا باب في بيان أحكام المهر وما يتعلق به، وهو بالفتح عبارة عمَّا يساقُ إلى الزوجة من الزوج عوضاً لمنافع بضعها ، وهو . عندنا لا بد أن يكون مالاً أو ما في حكمه. مهراً. وعند الشافعي له : لا يشترط كونه مالاً ، بل تعليم القرآن ونحوه أيضاً يصلح مهراً. فإن قلت : ذكر ابن الجوزي ) في كتابه «سلوة الأحزان»: إن آدم على نبينا وعليه الصلوة والسلام لازم القرب من حواء، وطلبت منه المهر، فقال: يا رب وماذا أعطيها ، قال : يا آدم صلّ على حبيبي . الله عشرين مرة ففعل، وفي رواية : قال الله : حين أراد القرب لا حتى تعطي مهرها. محمد بن عبد ا ومن المعلوم أن فائدة الصلاة ترجع إلى آدم ، فكيف صح جعله مهراً؟ قلت : يمكن أنه لما أوقعها على قصد كونه مهراً أشبه ذلك ما لو استؤجر شخص لقراءة القرآن ،ونحوه، فأتى به على قصد كونه للمستأجر ، وقد صرحوا فيه بأن ثوابه للمستأجر، وعليه فثواب صلاته لحواء ؛ لكونه في مقابلة المهر. كذا في حاشيتي «المواهب اللدنية» لعلي الشبراملسي المصري، وتلميذه محمد بن عبد الباقي الزرقاني" (۲)
Chapter of Mahr. [1] His statement: Chapter of Mahr: i.e., this is a chapter explaining the rulings of mahr and what pertains to it. Mahr (with fathah) is the term for what is brought forward from the husband to the wife as compensation for the benefits of her sexual organ. According to us [Hanafis], it must be property or its legal equivalent. According to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him): it is not required to be property; rather, teaching the Quran and the like also suffices as mahr. If you say: Ibn al-Jawzi mentioned in his book 'Sulwah al-Ahzan' that Adam (peace be upon him and our Prophet) sought closeness to Hawwa, and she asked him for mahr. He said: 'O Lord, what should I give her?' He said: 'O Adam, send blessings upon my beloved [Muhammad] twenty times,' so he did. In another narration: Allah said when he wanted to approach: 'Not until you give her mahr.' Muhammad ibn Abd...[?] And it is known that the benefit of the salat returns to Adam, so how can it be made mahr? I say: It is possible that when he performed it with the intent of it being mahr, it resembles a person hired to recite Quran, who then recites it with the intent that its reward belongs to the employer, and they have explicitly stated that its reward is for the employer. Thus, the reward of his salat is for Hawwa, as it is in exchange for mahr. This is mentioned in the two hashiyas of al-Mawahib al-Ladunniyyah by Ali al-Shabramallisi al-Misri and his student Muhammad ibn Abd al-Baqi al-Zarqani.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on mahr (dower). The Hanafi definition is given: mahr is property (mal) or its legal equivalent brought from the husband to the wife in exchange for the right to marital intimacy. The text then notes the Shafi'i view that mahr need not be property; teaching the Quran and similar acts are also valid as mahr. A story from Ibn al-Jawzi about Adam and Hawwa is presented as a possible objection: Adam taught Hawwa salat as mahr. The commentator refutes this by explaining that if the salat is performed with the explicit intention of it being mahr, its reward is transferred to the wife, analogous to a hired reciter. Thus, the story does not contradict the Hanafi condition that mahr be property, because the reward of deeds can be considered property in a metaphorical sense. The Hanafi position remains that mahr must be tangible property or its legal equivalent.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): Property given from husband to wife as compensation for the right to marital intimacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a valid form of mahr?
A) Gold coins
B) Teaching Quran
C) A house
D) A horse

Key Takeaway
Hanafi mahr must be property; teaching Quran is not valid as mahr, but the marriage remains valid with mahr al-mithl.
