Mahr Must Be Property: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Definition of mahr and establishing the Hanafi condition of monetary value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for mahr (that it must be property), explain why the Shafi'i proof from the Adam and Hawwa story is weak, and apply the Quranic verse 4:24 as evidence.

Core Idea
Mahr must be property; non-material benefits like teaching Qur'an are invalid according to Hanafi law.

This lesson explores the foundational Hanafi ruling on mahr (dower): it must be property (mal) or something treated as property. The Shafi'i school disagrees and permits non-material mahr. We will examine the Hanafi proof from Quran 4:24 and critique the Shafi'i reliance on a story about Prophet Adam. By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi position is firmly rooted in the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Define mahr linguistically and legally
Read the first few lines. Mahr is property given by the husband to the wife in exchange for the right to sexual intimacy (manafi' al-bud'). Note that Hanafis require mahr to be property (mal) or what is in its ruling.
This definition uses the term 'iwad (compensation) highlighting the contractual nature of marriage.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i allows non-property mahr, such as teaching Qur'an. Their primary evidence is the story of Adam and Hawwa where mahr was sending blessings upon the Prophet. The commentator presents this story to later refute it.
The story is from Ibn al-Jawzi's work; Shafi'is consider it valid proof because it appears in Islamic literature.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The commentator gives two responses: (1) Intention can transfer the reward of blessings to the wife, similar to hiring someone to recite Qur'an. (2) More decisively, rulings of previous religions are not binding if contradicted by our own law. Since Quran 4:24 explicitly mentions 'wealth', the Shafi'i proof is overridden.
The second response is the stronger one; it invokes the principle that earlier prophetic laws are abrogated by explicit Quranic text.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof: Quran 4:24 and the preposition 'ba'
Allah says: '...that you seek with your wealth...' (bi-amwalikum). The Hanafis argue that the preposition 'ba' (with) indicates attachment (ba al-ilṣāq) — meaning the act of seeking marriage must be accompanied by wealth. This establishes that mahr must be property.
This is a linguistic argument from usul al-fiqh: the word 'ba' here is considered to convey accompaniment, making wealth a necessary condition.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In the Hanafi school, a marriage contracted for a non-material mahr (e.g., teaching a surah) is either invalid (batil) or requires payment of mahr al-mithl. In the Shafi'i school, such a marriage is valid with that mahr.
This difference has real-world implications for marriage contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المهر
قوله : باب المهر ؛ أي هذا باب في بيان أحكام المهر وما يتعلق به، وهو بالفتح عبارة عمَّا يساقُ إلى الزوجة من الزوج عوضاً لمنافع بضعها ، وهو عندنا لا بد أن يكون مالاً أو ما في حكمه.
وعند الشافعي له : لا يشترط كونه مالاً ، بل تعليم القرآن ونحوه أيضاً يصلح مهراً.
فإن قلت : ذكر ابن الجوزي ) في كتابه «سلوة الأحزان»: إن آدم على نبينا وعليه الصلوة والسلام لازم القرب من حواء، وطلبت منه المهر، فقال: يا رب وماذا أعطيها ، قال : يا آدم صلّ على حبيبي . الله عشرين مرة ففعل، وفي رواية : قال الله : حين أراد القرب لا حتى تعطي مهرها.
ومن المعلوم أن فائدة الصلاة ترجع إلى آدم ، فكيف صح جعله مهراً؟
قلت : يمكن أنه لما أوقعها على قصد كونه مهراً أشبه ذلك ما لو استؤجر شخص لقراءة القرآن ،ونحوه، فأتى به على قصد كونه للمستأجر ، وقد صرحوا فيه بأن ثوابه للمستأجر، وعليه فثواب صلاته لحواء ؛ لكونه في مقابلة المهر. كذا في حاشيتي «المواهب اللدنية» لعلي الشبراملسي المصري، وتلميذه محمد بن عبد الباقي الزرقاني.
وهاهنا جواب آخر وهو أنه يمكن أن يكون المهر ثواب الصلاة، ويكون مقصود الله له من قوله : صلّ على حبيبي أن يصلي عليه ويهب ثوابه لحواء، فكان المهر شيئاً حاصلاً من آدم لحواء. وقد استدلت الشافعية بهذه القصة على أن المهر قد يكون غير المال أيضاً، وهو استدلال ضعيف، فإن الأحكام الواقعة في الأديان السابقة إذا قصت في القرآن والحديث إنما تكون حجّةً إذا لم يرد في شرعنا ما يخالف ذلك، فإن ورد فلا.
وقد ورد فيما نحن فيه وهـو قـوله بعد ذكر المحرمات : ﴿ وَأُحِلَّ لَكُم مَّا وَرَاءَ ذَالِكُمْ أَن تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ تُحْصِنِينَ ) (١) ، فإنّ الله ما أحل الابتغاء ملصقاً بالأموال ؛ إذ الباء موضوعة للإلصاق، فدل ذلك على أنه لا يخلو الابتغاء، وهوا العقد ويأتي الجواب عن بقية استدلالات الشافعية.
Chapter of Mahr
His statement: Chapter of Mahr; that is, this is a chapter explaining the rulings of mahr and what pertains to it. Mahr (with fatha) is a term for what is given from the husband to the wife as compensation for the benefits of her vulva. According to us, it must be property or what is in its ruling.
According to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him: It is not a condition that it be property; rather, teaching the Qur'an and the like also suffice as mahr.
If you say: Ibn al-Jawzi mentioned in his book 'Salwat al-Ahzan' that Adam, peace be upon him, desired intimacy with Hawwa, and she asked him for mahr. He said: O Lord, what shall I give her? Allah said: O Adam, send blessings upon My beloved twenty times, and he did. In another narration: Allah said when he desired intimacy: Not until you give her mahr.
It is known that the benefit of the blessings returns to Adam, so how could it be valid to make it mahr?
I say: It is possible that when he performed it with the intention of it being mahr, it resembles the case where a person is hired to recite the Qur'an and the like, and he performs it with the intention of it being for the hirer, and they have stated clearly that its reward is for the hirer. Accordingly, the reward of his blessings is for Hawwa because it is in exchange for the mahr. This is in the hashya of 'al-Mawahib al-Ladunniyya' by Ali al-Shabaramlisi al-Misri and his student Muhammad ibn Abd al-Baqi al-Zurqani.
And here is another answer: It is possible that the mahr is the reward of the blessings, and Allah's intention to him from His statement 'Send blessings upon My beloved' was that he should send blessings and gift its reward to Hawwa, so the mahr was something obtained from Adam for Hawwa. The Shafi'is have used this story as evidence that mahr may sometimes be non-property, and it is weak evidence. For the rulings of previous religions when narrated in the Qur'an and Hadith are only evidence if nothing contrary appears in our Law; if it does, then they are not.
And contrary has appeared in our subject, which is His statement after mentioning prohibitions: 'And lawful to you are what is beyond that, that you seek with your wealth, guarding chastity' [4:24]. Indeed, Allah did not make seeking lawful except attached to wealth, because the preposition 'ba' is for attachment. This indicates that seeking, which is the contract, is never free of wealth. And the answer to the remaining Shafi'i evidences will follow.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on mahr (dower) from a Hanafi commentary. The author first defines mahr linguistically and legally: it is property given by the husband to the wife in exchange for the right to sexual intimacy (manafi' al-bud'). The Hanafi position is that mahr must be property (mal) or something that is treated as property in law. This excludes non-material things like teaching the Qur'an. The Shafi'i school, however, permits non-material mahr, such as teaching Qur'anic verses. The commentator then addresses a potential objection based on a story narrated by Ibn al-Jawzi about Prophet Adam and Hawwa, where Adam's mahr was sending blessings upon the Prophet. The Shafi'is use this as evidence that mahr need not be property. The commentator gives two responses: first, that if the blessings are performed with the intention of being mahr, their reward can be transferred to the wife, similar to hiring someone to recite the Qur'an where the reward goes to the hirer. Second, and more decisively, the stories of previous religions are not binding in our law if contradicted by our own texts. The Quranic verse (4:24) explicitly conditions seeking marriage 'with your wealth' (bi-amwalikum), which the Hanafis interpret through the Arabic preposition 'ba' as indicating attachment—thus the act of marriage must be accompanied by wealth. This refutes the Shafi'i view. The commentary ends by noting that further refutations will follow.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): Property given from husband to wife in exchange for the benefits of her vulva (sexual intimacy).
البضع (al-bud'): The vulva or female genitalia; legally, the right to sexual intimacy.
عوض (iwad): Compensation or consideration; in marriage, the mahr is the iwad for the woman's right to intimacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It must be a specific gold coin.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mahr must be property (mal) or its legal equivalent; non-material benefits are not valid as mahr, and any such contract requires payment of mahr al-mithl.

Minimum Mahr: Ten Dirhams with Hadith Evidence
Establishing the minimum mahr as ten dirhams with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for minimum mahr, explain the hadith evidence and its strengthening, and reconcile the apparent conflict with the iron ring hadith.

Core Idea
Minimum mahr is ten dirhams based on a hadith strengthened to hasan, reconciled with the iron ring hadith by applying each to different contexts.

In Hanafi fiqh, mahr (dower) is an obligatory payment to the wife, but what is the minimum amount? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the minimum is ten dirhams, the primary hadith evidence, and how the school resolves an apparent contradiction with the well-known hadith mentioning a ring of iron. Understanding this ruling requires analyzing hadith strength and contextual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
The matn states: 'Its minimum is ten dirhams.' This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. Note that the marriage is still valid if less is stipulated, but the wife is entitled to proper mahr (mahr al-mithl).
The minimum is a condition for the specified mahr, not for the validity of the marriage itself.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The proof is a marfu' hadith from Jabir: 'Do not marry women except to equals... and no mahr less than ten dirhams.' Identify the chain: it includes Mubashshir ibn Ubayd, considered weak by al-Daraqutni.
Weakness does not automatically reject the hadith; it can be elevated.
3
Assess the hadith's strength
Al-Bayhaqi narrated the same meaning through multiple weak chains. These chains strengthen each other, raising the hadith to the rank of hasan, which is sufficient for legal evidence. This is the Hanafi method of dealing with weak narrations when corroborated.
The principle: multiple weak chains can strengthen to hasan li ghayrihi.
4
Address the counter-dalil
The opposing hadith (Bukhari, Muslim) reports the Prophet telling a man to 'Seek even a ring of iron' as mahr. This seems to contradict the ten-dirham minimum. Understand the objection and prepare for reconciliation.
This hadith is stronger in transmission but different in context.
5
Apply the reconciliation
Al-Qari resolves the conflict: the ten-dirham hadith refers to the minimum specified mahr (whether deferred or immediate), while the iron ring hadith refers to customary validation of the marriage (i.e., any token suffices to make the marriage valid in custom). Thus, both are applied in different scenarios.
The Hanafi ruling stands: the specified mahr cannot be less than ten dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[ ۱ ] قوله : أقله ؛ أي أقل المهر ؛ أي الذي لا يجوز أدنى منه. [٢] قوله : دراهم ؛ أي مقدار عشرة دراهم سواء كانت فضة خالصة، أو مضروباً ، أو ذهباً، أو متاعاً مقدراً به.

(2) :

Its minimum is ten dirhams: this is according to us.
[1] His statement: Its minimum; meaning the minimum of mahr; i.e., what is not permissible to go below. [2] His statement: Dirhams; meaning the amount of ten dirhams, whether they are pure silver, or minted, or gold, or goods estimated by it.
[3] His statement: This is according to us; meaning the specification of the minimum as ten dirhams is our school due to traditions that have come concerning that. From Jabir marfu': 'Do not marry women except to equals, and do not give them in marriage except through guardians, and no mahr less than ten dirhams.' In its chain is Mubashshir ibn Ubayd. al-Daraqutni said after he narrated it...
(Reference to al-Daraqutni's Sunan, al-Sunan al-Sughra, al-Mu'jam al-Awsat, Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir, etc. It is opposed by what the two Shaykhs narrated concerning the woman who offered herself: 'Seek even if a ring of iron.' al-Qari said: The opposition is repelled by carrying the first hadith on the minimum named mahr deferred and immediate, and the second on customary registration. The first is supported by what al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan al-Kubra from weak chains, but they strengthen each other regarding Jabir, so it rises to the rank of hasan, and it is sufficient as evidence. In I'la' al-Sunan: Ibn Hajar and the author of Sharh al-Sunnah declared it hasan. See: al-Asrar al-Marfu'a, Zafr al-Amani, Kashf al-Khafa'.)
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum amount of mahr in Hanafi law. The matn states 'its minimum is ten dirhams'. The commentator explains that 'its minimum' means the lowest permissible amount, and 'dirhams' refers to ten silver dirhams or equivalent value in gold or goods. This is the Hanafi school's position (madhhabuna). The proof is a hadith from Jabir: 'Do not marry women except to equals... and no mahr less than ten dirhams.' The commentator acknowledges that the chain includes Mubashshir ibn Ubayd, whom al-Daraqutni criticized, but al-Bayhaqi's narrations from multiple weak chains strengthen each other to the level of hasan, which is sufficient for legal evidence. A potential objection is raised from the well-known hadith in Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet told a man: 'Seek even a ring of iron' as mahr. The commentator (citing al-Qari) resolves this: the hadith of ten dirhams refers to the minimum specified mahr (in deferred or immediate payment), while the hadith of the iron ring refers to customary validation of a marriage (not fixing a minimum). Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands: any mahr less than ten dirhams is not valid.

Key Terms
أقله (aqalluhu): The minimum amount of mahr, below which it is not permissible.
الدرهم (al-dirham): A silver coin; the standard of measurement for mahr minimum.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr determined by the wife's social status and the mahr of her female relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes a minimum mahr of ten dirhams based on a hadith strengthened to hasan, and reconciles the iron ring hadith by applying it to customary validation, not the specified mahr.

The Minimum Mahr: Hanafi Ruling and Proofs
Commentary on the minimum mahr ruling with hadith criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum mahr, identify the Quranic and hadith evidence, and explain the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The minimum mahr is ten dirhams; specifying less invalidates the stipulation, not the marriage.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the Hanafi position that the minimum specified mahr must be ten dirhams. The author presents the Quranic verse from Surah an-Nisa as the primary proof, then evaluates hadith evidence that supports the ruling despite weak chains. The Shafi'i counter-argument is also addressed and refuted, clarifying the madhhab's reliance on textual and cumulative evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the legal rule: the minimum specified mahr is ten dirhams; if less is stipulated, the stipulation is void and the wife receives mahr al-mithl.
The contract itself remains valid.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
Examine verse an-Nisa:24, focusing on the letter ba' in 'bi-amwalikum' which indicates attachment of marriage to wealth, implying mahr must be of monetary value.
This refutes the idea that mahr can be non-monetary.
3
Evaluate the hadith evidence
Assess the hadith from Jabir: 'No mahr below ten dirhams.' Note the weak chain (Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd) and the objection of critics, then consider the argument that multiple weak chains strengthen it to hasan level.
Also consider the mawquf hadith from Ali.
4
Examine the Shafi'i counter-argument and Hanafi response
Review the Shafi'i proofs: story of Adam and Hawwa', the 'iron ring' hadith, and the principle of freedom of agreement. Then follow the Hanafi refutation: previous laws abrogated, the 'iron ring' refers to customary gift not specified mahr, and the lack of textual basis for no minimum.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the stipulated mahr is enforceable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر
أقله عشرة دراهم
أقله عشرة دراهم: هذا عندنا
وهاهنا جواب آخر وهو أنه يمكن أن يكون المهر ثواب الصلاة، ويكون مقصود الله له من قوله: صل على حبيبي أن يصلي عليه ويهب ثوابه لحواء، فكان المهر شيئاً حاصلاً من آدم لحواء. وقد استدلت الشافعية بهذه القصة على أن المهر قد يكون غير المال أيضاً، وهو استدلال ضعيف، فإن الأحكام الواقعة في الأديان السابقة إذا قصت في القرآن والحديث إنما تكون حجةً إذا لم يرد في شرعنا ما يخالف ذلك، فإن ورد فلا.
وقد ورد فيما نحن فيه وهو قوله بعد ذكر المحرمات: ﴿ وَأُحِلَّ لَكُم مَّا وَرَاءَ ذَالِكُمْ أَن تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ مُحْصِنِينَ ﴾ (النساء: 24)، فإن الله ما أحل الابتغاء ملصقاً بالأموال؛ إذ الباء موضوعة للإلصاق، فدل ذلك على أنه لا يخلو الابتغاء وهو العقد عن المال، ويأتي الجواب عن بقية استدلالات الشافعية.
قوله: أقله؛ أي أقل المهر؛ أي الذي لا يجوز أدنى منه. قوله: دراهم؛ أي مقدار عشرة دراهم سواء كانت فضة خالصة، أو مضروباً، أو ذهباً، أو متاعاً مقدراً به. قوله: هذا عندنا؛ أي تعيين الأقل بعشرة دراهم مذهبنا لأحاديث وردت بذلك، فعن جابر مرفوعاً: «لا تنكحوا النساء إلا الأكفاء، ولا يزوجهن إلا الأولياء، ولا مهر دون عشرة دراهم»، وفي سنده مبشر بن عبيد، قال الدارقطني بعد أن أخرج هذا الحديث: «هو متروك الحديث، أحاديثه لا يتابع عليها». انتهى. ويعارضه ما رواه الشيخان في الواهبة رفعه: «التمس ولو خاتماً من حديد»، قال القاري: وتندفع المعارضة بحمل الأول على أقل مسمى من المهر آجلاً وعاجلاً، والثاني المسجل عرفاً، ويؤيد الأول ما رواه البيهقي في سننه الكبرى من طرق ضعيفة، لكنها يقوي بعضها ببعض عن جابر فيرتقي إلى مرتبة الحسن، وهو كاف في الحجة. وفي «إعلاء السنن»: حسنه ابن حجر وصاحب شرح السنة. ينظر: «الأسرار المرفوعة» (٣٦٨ - ٣٦٩)، و«ظفر الأماني» (١٧٢ - ١٧٤)، و«كشف الخفاء».
وأسند البيهقي وقد أخرجه في «سننه» في كتاب «المعرفة» عن أحمد: أنه قال: أحاديث مبشر بن عبيد موضوعة. انتهى.
وأخرجه أيضاً أبو يعلى الموصلي في «مسنده»، وابن حبان في «كتاب الضعفاء»: وقال: مبشر بن عبيد يروي عن الثقات الموضوعات لا يحل كتب حديثه إلا على جهة التعجب. انتهى.
وأخرجه أيضاً ابن عدي والعقيلي وأعلاه بمبشر.
وأخرج الدارقطني والبيهقي في سننهما عن الشعبي عن علي موقوفاً: «لا تقطع اليد في أقل من عشرة دراهم، ولا يكون المهر أقل من عشرة دراهم»، وفي سنده داود الأودي، وهو ضعيف، وله طرق أخر في سنن الدارقطني، ولا تخلو عن ضعف. وهنا أبحاث:
الأول: إن هذه الأحاديث كلها أسانيدها مجروحة غير قابلة لأن يحتج بها. وأجاب عنه العيني في «البناية»: «بأنه إذا روي الحديث من طرق مفرداتها ضعيفة يصير حسناً، ويحتج به».
أقول: لا يخفى ما فيه، فإن بكثرة الطرق إنما يصير الحديث حسناً إذا كان الضعف فيها يسيراً، فينجبر بالتعدد، لا إذا كانت شديدة الضعف بأن لا يخلو واحد منها عن كذب أو متهم، والأمر فيما نحن فيه كذلك.
Book of Nikah: Chapter of Mahr. Its minimum is ten dirhams. Its minimum is ten dirhams: This is according to us. And here is another answer: that the mahr could be the reward of prayer, and what Allah intended from His saying 'Send blessings on my beloved' is that he [Adam] should send blessings on him and gift its reward to Hawwa', so the mahr was something obtained from Adam for Hawwa'. The Shafi'is have used this story as evidence that mahr can be other than wealth as well, and it is a weak deduction, because rulings that occurred in previous religions when narrated in the Qur'an and Hadith are only a proof if there is nothing in our Shari'ah that contradicts that; if it contradicts, then it is not. And there has come in what we are discussing, and it is His saying after mentioning the prohibited women: {And lawful to you are all beyond those, that you seek with your wealth, being chaste} (an-Nisa: 24), for Allah did not permit seeking unless attached to wealth, because the ba' is for attachment, so that indicates that the seeking, which is the contract, is not free from wealth. And the response to the rest of the Shafi'is' arguments will come. His saying: 'its minimum'; meaning the minimum of the mahr; that is, that which is not permissible to go below. His saying: 'dirhams'; meaning the amount of ten dirhams, whether pure silver, or coined, or gold, or goods valued thereby. His saying: 'this is according to us'; meaning the specification of the minimum as ten dirhams is our madhhab due to hadiths that have come to that effect. Thus from Jabir in marfu' form: 'Do not marry women except to equals, and let none give them in marriage except guardians, and there is no mahr less than ten dirhams.' In its chain is Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd. al-Daraqutni said after he narrated this hadith: 'He is abandoned in hadith; his hadiths are not followed.' End. And it is opposed by what the two Shaykhs narrated regarding the woman who gave herself [in marriage] in marfu' form: 'Seek, even if it be an iron ring.' al-Qari said: The opposition is repelled by interpreting the first as the minimum amount of mahr, deferred and immediate, and the second as the customary [gift] that is recorded. And the first is supported by what al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan al-Kubra from weak chains, but some strengthen others from Jabir, so it rises to the level of hasan, and that is sufficient as evidence. And in I'la' al-Sunan: Ibn Hajar and the author of Sharh al-Sunnah declared it hasan. Look at al-Asrar al-Marfu'ah (368-369), Zafar al-Amani (172-174), and Kashf al-Khafa'. And al-Bayhaqi transmitted, and he had narrated it in his Sunan in Kitab al-Ma'rifah, from Ahmad that he said: The hadiths of Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd are fabricated. End. And it was also narrated by Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili in his Musnad, and Ibn Hibban in Kitab al-Du'afa', who said: Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd narrates fabricated things from trustworthy narrators; it is not permissible to write his hadith except in astonishment. End. And it was also narrated by Ibn 'Adi and al-'Uqayli, and they faulted it due to Mubashshir. And al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi narrated in their Sunan from al-Sha'bi from 'Ali in mawquf form: 'The hand is not cut for less than ten dirhams, and mahr is not less than ten dirhams.' In its chain is Dawud al-Awdi, and he is weak, and it has other chains in Sunan al-Daraqutni, and they are not free from weakness. Here are investigations: The first: That all these hadiths have chains that are wounded, not acceptable as proof. And al-'Ayni responded in al-Binayah: 'That if a hadith is narrated from multiple chains each of which is weak, it becomes hasan and is used as evidence.' I say: What is in it is not hidden, for by multiplicity of chains a hadith only becomes hasan if the weakness is slight, so it is compensated by multiplicity, not when it is severe weakness such that each chain is not free from a liar or an accused [narrator], and the matter in what we are discussing is like that.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah stating the legal ruling that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. The author begins by affirming that this is the Hanafi position. He then addresses a Shafi'i argument that mahr can be non-monetary, citing the story of Adam and Hawwa'. The author refutes this by noting that previous religious rulings are only valid in our Shari'ah if not contradicted; here, the Quranic verse (an-Nisa:24) explicitly links marriage with wealth, as the letter ba' indicates attachment. Thus mahr must involve wealth. Next, the author explains the words of the matn: 'its minimum' means the least permissible amount; 'dirhams' includes any form of wealth equivalent to ten dirhams; and 'this is according to us' refers to the madhhab's reliance on hadith evidence. The primary hadith from Jabir is cited, but its chain includes Mubashshir ibn 'Ubayd, whom critics like al-Daraqutni declare abandoned. The author then presents an opposing hadith about seeking an iron ring, but resolves it by interpreting that as a customary gift, not the specified mahr. He supports the first hadith by noting that despite weak individual chains, the multiplicity raises it to hasan level, as argued by al-Bayhaqi and others. Further criticisms of Mubashshir from Ahmad, Abu Ya'la, and Ibn Hibban are given. Another mawquf hadith from Ali is cited but also weak. The author concludes with a discussion: al-'Ayni argues that multiple weak chains can strengthen a hadith, but the author objects that this only applies if the weakness is slight, not severe as in this case. Thus the hadith evidence is contested, yet the Hanafi ruling stands based on the Quranic verse and the cumulative strength of the hadith.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife as a legal obligation of marriage.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin, here used as a unit of value equivalent to approximately 3 grams of silver or the value of goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a marriage contract specifies a mahr of seven dirhams?
A) The marriage is invalid.
B) The marriage is valid and the wife receives seven dirhams.
C) The marriage is valid, but the specification is void and the wife receives mahr al-mithl.
D) The marriage is valid only if the wife agrees to reduce the mahr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum mahr of ten dirhams is derived from the Quranic indication that mahr must be wealth, supported by hadith evidence that rises to hasan level through multiple chains.

Critique of the Hadith Evidence for Minimum Mahr
Critically examining the hadith evidence for the ten-dirham minimum mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the strength of the hadith evidence for the Hanafi minimum mahr of ten dirhams and identify the author's two main objections.

Core Idea
The ten-dirham minimum mahr relies on a weak hadith that cannot override the Quranic absolute and should be interpreted as negation of perfection.

The Hanafi school holds that the mahr (dower) cannot be less than ten dirhams, citing a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) fixed this minimum. However, this hadith has been criticized as weak, and the school's own principles on using solitary reports and interpreting negation hadiths may be inconsistently applied. In this lesson, we examine the author's critique of the evidence and the two irrefutable objections he raises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on minimum mahr
Recall that the Hanafi school rules it impermissible to specify a mahr less than ten dirhams. If a lesser amount is named, the wife is entitled to the proper mahr (mahr al-mithl).
2
Examine the first objection: weakness of the hadith
The author lists the chains of the key hadith and shows they are weak or fabricated. According to Hanafi usul, a weak solitary report cannot specify the absolute Quranic command 'that you seek with your wealth' (Quran 4:24), which has no minimum.
This is a methodological inconsistency: the school normally requires strong evidence to override the Quran, but here a weak hadith is used.
3
Examine the second objection: interpretation of 'لا' as negation of perfection
The author compares the minimum mahr hadith to other 'لا' hadiths that Hanafis interpret as negating perfection, not essence (e.g., 'لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب'). If the school applies that principle to those hadiths, why not apply it here, allowing a valid marriage with a lesser mahr?
This objection points to a possible inconsistency in the school's hermeneutics.
4
Analyze the author's conclusion
The author states that these two objections are irrefutable, leaving the issue unresolved. Reflect on what this means for the mufta bihi position and for the student's understanding of how fiqh positions are not always settled.

Source Text

وحديث : «النعلين»، وإن صححه التّرْمِذِيُّ فليس بصحيح، فيه : عاصم بن عبيد الله ، قال ابن الجوزي : قال ابن معين : ضعيف لا يحتج به، وقال ابن حبان : فاحش الخطأ فترك.
وحديث: «العلائق» معلول بمحمد بن عبد الرحمن ، قال البخاري : منكر الحديث، ورواه أبو داود في «المراسيل» وفيه : محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى : ضعيف.
وحديث : «الخدري»، فيه : أبو هارون العبدي، قال ابن الجوزي : قال حماد بن زيد : كان كذاباً». انتهى(۱) وأجيب عنه : بأن ما يدلُّ على كون المهر أقل من عشرة دارهم، محمول على المهرِ المعجل، فإنّ العادة . عندهم كانت تعجيل بعض المهر قبل الدخول حتى ذهب بعض العلماء إلى أنه لا يدخلُ حتى يقدم شيئاً ، نُقِلَ ذلك عن ابن عباس وابن عمر والزبيري وقتادة تمسكاً بمنعه «عليّاً حين زوجه فاطمة رضي الله عنها، وأراد أن يدخل عليها عن الدخول حتى يعطي شيئاً). أخرجه النسائي. والمختار الجواز قبله ؛ لحديث عائشة رضي الله عنها : «أمرني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن أُدْخِلَ امرأة على زوجها قبل أن يعطيها شيئاً (۳)، أخرجه أبو داود، والمنع المذكور محمول على الندب. كذا في «الفتح»، وغيره.
أقول : لا يخفي ما فيه، فإن هذا الحملَ إنّما يُسَلِّمُ مع مخالفتِهِ الظواهر إذا ثبت التقدير بدليل معتمد ، وإذ ليس فليس.
الثالث : إن العمل بالحديث المذكور، والقولُ بأنه لا يجوز أقل من عشرة يخالف إطلاق قوله : أَن تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَلِكُم ) ، فإنّه لا تقدير فيه بشيء، وتخصيص إطلاق الكتاب بخبر الآحاد وإن كان صحيحاً لا يجوز عند أصحابنا فما بالك إذا كان ضعيفاً مضعفاً.
وقد استند به أصحابنا في الجواب عن الأحاديث الصحيحة التي دلت على كون المهر غير مال، وهي مروية في «الصحيحين»، واستندت بها الشافعية حيث قالوا : هذه الأحاديث أخبار آحاد مخالفة لظاهر الكتاب فلا يعمل بظاهرها، فمع هذا كيف جاز لأصحابنا العمل بخبر الآحاد مع مخالفته لإطلاق الكتاب؟ هذا ما ظهر لي.
الرابع : وهو أيضاً ما خطر ببالي أن هذا الحديث نظير حديث: «لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب ، وحديث : لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد»، وحديث : «لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله»(۳) وغير ذلك وهي عند أصحابنا محمولة على نفي الكمال لا على نفي الذات. فما بالهم لم يحملوا هذا الحديث على مثل هذا، وهذان الإيرادان مما لا مدفع لهما ، فتأمل لعل الله الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمراً.
The hadith of the sandals, even if at-Tirmidhi authenticated it, is not authentic. In it is 'Asim ibn 'Ubaydullah. Ibn al-Jawzi said: Ibn Ma'in said: weak, not used as evidence. Ibn Hibban said: gross error, so abandoned. The hadith of the hanging things is defective due to Muhammad ibn 'Abd ar-Rahman. Al-Bukhari said: munkar al-hadith. Abu Dawud narrated it in al-Marasil, and in it is Muhammad ibn 'Abd ar-Rahman ibn Abi Layla: weak. The hadith of al-Khudri, in it is Abu Harun al-'Abdi. Ibn al-Jawzi said: Hammad ibn Zayd said: he was a liar. End. And it was answered: that what indicates that the dower is less than ten dirhams is interpreted as the prompt dower, for their custom was to pay some portion of the dower before consummation, to the extent that some scholars held that he should not enter until he gives something. That was transmitted from Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn 'Umar, az-Zubayri, and Qatadah, adhering to the prevention of 'Ali when he married Fatima (may Allah be pleased with her) and wanted to enter upon her, he prevented him from entering until he gives something. An-Nasa'i narrated it. The chosen view is that it is permissible before that, due to the hadith of 'A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered me to bring a woman to her husband before he gave her anything.' Abu Dawud narrated it. And the mentioned prevention is interpreted as recommendation. Thus in al-Fath and others. I say: what is in it is not hidden, for this interpretation is only conceded if it contradicts the apparent meanings when the estimate is established by a reliable proof, and it is not. The third: that acting on the mentioned hadith and saying that less than ten is not allowed contradicts the absolute meaning of His statement 'that you seek with your wealth', for there is no estimate in it. And specifying the absolute of the Book with a solitary hadith, even if authentic, is not allowed according to our companions, so what about when it is weak and weakened? And our companions relied on it in answer to the authentic hadiths that indicated that the dower is not wealth, which are narrated in the two Sahihs. The Shafi'is relied on them where they said: these hadiths are solitary reports opposing the apparent of the Book, so their apparent is not acted upon. So with this, how did our companions allow acting on a solitary report while it opposes the absolute of the Book? This is what appeared to me. The fourth: and it also occurred to me that this hadith is similar to the hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book', and the hadith 'No prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque', and the hadith 'No wudu for one who does not mention Allah's name' and others, which according to our companions are interpreted as negation of perfection, not negation of essence. So why did they not interpret this hadith similarly? These two objections are irrefutable. So reflect, perhaps Allah will bring about something thereafter.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the argument for setting a minimum mahr of ten dirhams. The author first presents the standard Hanafi defense: the hadiths that suggest a lower mahr can be given are interpreted as referring to prompt payment or as merely recommendatory. However, these interpretations are rejected because they contradict the apparent meaning of the Quran and rely on weak hadiths. The author then raises two objections: (1) The hadith setting ten dirhams as a minimum is weak and thus cannot override the absolute Quranic command to seek women with wealth (without specifying an amount). The Hanafi school normally does not allow a solitary hadith to specify the Quran, so using a weak one is even more problematic. This contradicts their own methodology when they reject other solitary hadiths used by the Shafi'is. (2) The hadith on minimum mahr should be interpreted like other negations in the school (e.g., 'no prayer without Fatiha') as negating perfection, not essence. If the school does this for those hadiths, why not for this one? The author concludes these objections are irrefutable, leaving the issue unresolved.

Key Terms
المهر المعجل (al-mahr al-mu'ajjal): The portion of the dower paid promptly before consummation.
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A hadith transmitted by a single or limited chain, not reaching tawatur.
نفي الكمال (nafy al-kamāl): Negation of perfection rather than negation of essence; the action is valid but incomplete.

C) The hadith contradicts the Quranic verse on marriage.
D) The hadith is clear and cannot be reinterpreted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum mahr of ten dirhams rests on a weak hadith, and the school's own usul and hermeneutic principles raise two irrefutable objections against it.

Defending the Minimum Mahr: The Third and Fourth Objections
Refuting two objections to the Hanafi minimum mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two key objections to the Hanafi position on minimum mahr and explain why they challenge Hanafi usul and interpretation.

Core Idea
The Hanafi ruling on mahr faces internal consistency challenges regarding solitary hadith and the principle of nafy al-kamal.

This passage presents two forceful objections raised against the Hanafi position that the minimum mahr must be ten dirhams. The third objection points to a contradiction in usul: the Hanafis reject using solitary hadith to specify the Quran, yet they rely on a solitary (and weak) hadith to set a minimum mahr. The fourth objection argues that the mahr hadith should be interpreted as negating perfection, not essence, similar to other hadiths the Hanafis interpret that way. The author acknowledges these objections as undeniable, leaving the reader to reflect on the tension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on minimum mahr
Recall that the Hanafi school holds that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams; if less is specified, the woman is owed ten dirhams.
This is the established position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the third objection
The objection claims that using a solitary hadith (khabar ahad) to specify the absolute Quranic verse (4:24) contradicts Hanafi usul, and the hadith is weak. Hanafis normally require a mutawatir or mashhur hadith to specify the Quran.
The critic points out that the Hanafis themselves use this argument against Shafi'i hadiths.
3
Understand the fourth objection
The objection analogizes the mahr hadith to other hadiths (e.g., 'no prayer without Fatiha') that Hanafis interpret as negating perfection, asking why they don't interpret the mahr hadith similarly.
This would mean the hadith negates perfect mahr rather than prohibiting mahr below ten dirhams.
4
Analyze the author's response
The author does not offer a full rebuttal; he acknowledges both objections as 'undeniable' (la madafa'a lahu) and leaves them for reflection. This forces the student to think about the methodological tension.
The author might be presenting a self-critique or inviting further research.

Source Text

أقول : لا يخفي ما فيه، فإن هذا الحملَ إنّما يُسَلِّمُ مع مخالفتِهِ الظواهر إذا ثبت التقدير بدليل معتمد ، وإذ ليس فليس.
الثالث : إن العمل بالحديث المذكور، والقولُ بأنه لا يجوز أقل من عشرة يخالف إطلاق قوله : أَن تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَلِكُم ) ، فإنّه لا تقدير فيه بشيء، وتخصيص إطلاق الكتاب بخبر الآحاد وإن كان صحيحاً لا يجوز عند أصحابنا فما بالك إذا كان ضعيفاً مضعفاً.
وقد استند به أصحابنا في الجواب عن الأحاديث الصحيحة التي دلت على كون المهر غير مال، وهي مروية في «الصحيحين»، واستندت بها الشافعية حيث قالوا : هذه الأحاديث أخبار آحاد مخالفة لظاهر الكتاب فلا يعمل بظاهرها، فمع هذا كيف جاز
لأصحابنا العمل بخبر الآحاد مع مخالفته لإطلاق الكتاب؟ هذا ما ظهر لي. الرابع : وهو أيضاً ما خطر ببالي أن هذا الحديث نظير حديث: «لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب ، وحديث : لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد»، وحديث : «لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله»(٣) وغير ذلك وهي عند أصحابنا محمولة على نفي الكمال
لا على نفي الذات. فما بالهم لم يحملوا هذا الحديث على مثل هذا، وهذان الإيرادان مما لا مدفع
لهما ، فتأمل لعل الله الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمراً.
I say: It is not hidden what is in it, for this interpretation is only accepted if it contradicts apparent meanings only when the estimation is established by a reliable proof, and if not, then not. Third: Acting on the mentioned hadith, and the statement that less than ten is not permissible, contradicts the absolute [general] meaning of His statement: 'that you seek [marriage] with your wealth' [4:24] – for there is no estimation in it of anything. And specifying the absolute meaning of the Book by a solitary report, even if authentic, is not permissible according to our companions, so what about when it is weak and weakened? Our companions have relied on it in answering the authentic hadiths that indicate that mahr is not property, and these are narrated in the two Sahihs. The Shafi'is have relied on them saying: These hadiths are solitary reports that contradict the apparent meaning of the Book, so their apparent meaning is not acted upon. So how is it permissible for our companions to act on a solitary report while it contradicts the absolute meaning of the Book? This is what appeared to me. Fourth: And this is also what occurred to me – that this hadith is similar to the hadith: 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' and the hadith: 'No prayer for a neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque' and the hadith: 'No wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah' and others. And these are interpreted by our companions as negation of perfection, not negation of essence. So why did they not interpret this hadith in such a manner? These two objections are undeniable. So reflect, perhaps Allah will bring about something after that.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement wherein the author responds to four objections raised against the Hanafi position that the minimum mahr must be ten dirhams. The first two objections are not fully given here; the text starts from the third and fourth objections. The third objection argues that the Hanafi reliance on a hadith specifying ten dirhams contradicts the general Quranic verse 'seek with your wealth' which does not specify any minimum. Moreover, according to Hanafi usul, a solitary hadith (khabar ahad) cannot specify a general text of the Quran, especially when the hadith in question is weak. The author also notes the inconsistency: the Hanafis use this argument against the Shafi'is who rely on other solitary hadiths regarding mahr, yet the Hanafis themselves use a solitary hadith to set the minimum. The fourth objection analogizes the hadith on mahr to other hadiths (about prayer, wudu) which the Hanafis interpret as negating perfection, not essence; the author asks why they do not similarly interpret the mahr hadith as negating perfect mahr rather than disallowing any mahr below ten. The author leaves these reflections for the reader to ponder.

Key Terms
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-ahad): A hadith transmitted by a limited number of narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
نفي الكمال (nafy al-kamal): Negation of perfection; meaning that an act is valid but incomplete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third objection, what does the Hanafi reliance on a solitary hadith for minimum mahr contradict?
A) The Quranic verse on marriage
B) The Hanafi usul principle that a general Quran text cannot be specified by a solitary hadith
C) The Shafi'i position
D) The authenticity of the hadith

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on minimum mahr faces genuine methodological objections regarding the use of solitary hadith and interpretation of negation, which the commentator acknowledges rather than dismisses.

The Minimum Mahr: When Specification Is Void
Clarifies that if a mahr less than ten dirhams is specified, the full ten are due.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying a mahr below ten dirhams, derive the ruling via qiyas on the nisab of theft, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i and Imam Zafar's views.

Core Idea
A mahr of less than ten dirhams is void; the wife receives ten dirhams instead.

This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi rule that the mahr (dower) in marriage must be at least ten dirhams. If a lower amount is specified, the contract does not fail—rather, the specification is voided and the woman is entitled to the full minimum. We will trace the proof by analogy to the hadd threshold for theft, examine the Shafi'i objection, and also note an internal Hanafi difference with Imam Zafar. The goal is to understand not just the ruling but the legal reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
What does the matn say about a mahr specified at less than ten dirhams? The ruling is that the wife is entitled to ten dirhams, not the lesser amount.
The matn phrase 'تجب هي' refers to the ten dirhams becoming wajib.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The Hanafi school holds that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. If less is named, the named amount is void and the ten are wajib. This is the mufta bihi position.
This ruling applies to the initial specification; if no mahr is named, mahr al-mithl applies.
3
Examine the Primary Proof: Qiyas on Nisab al-Sariqa
The Hanafi proof is qiyas on the nisab (minimum threshold) for theft, which is ten dirhams. The analogy: just as the hand is cut only for stolen goods worth ten dirhams, so too the vulval benefits (buda') must be compensated by at least ten dirhams.
Identify the asl (theft nisab), far' (mahr), illah (significant property compensating a valuable benefit).
4
Consider the Objection and Hanafi Response
The objection: legal measures cannot be set by qiyas or opinion. The response (from al-Babarti): this is not mere opinion; it is deriving a measure from the Lawgiver's own benchmark (the nisab) to give mahr its due significance.
The measure is ta'abbudi but based on a textual indicator.
5
Compare with Opposing Views
The Shafi'i school allows any amount suitable as a price. Imam Zafar (within Hanafi) holds that an invalid specification triggers mahr al-mithl, not the fixed ten. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is clear: in Hanafi fatwa, the woman gets ten dirhams; in Shafi'i, the specified amount stands; in Zafar's view, she gets mahr al-mithl.
The disputed element is the existence and quantum of a minimum.

And it [the mahr] is obligatory [if he specifies less than it] [the ten dirhams], and if he specifies other than that [it is as specified]. (1) As for the Shafi'i, everything that is suitable as a price is suitable as a mahr, whether it is ten dirhams, or less than that, or more. (And it is obligatory if he specifies less than it, and if he specifies other than that.) And it may be argued for our companions by analogy to the threshold for theft: i.e., the amount for which the hand is cut off for theft, and it is ten dirhams according to us. But it is flawed because measures are not established by mere opinion and analogy (2). (2) His statement: 'Everything suitable as a price...' etc.; meaning everything that can be a price in sales, even a dirham or less, is suitable as a mahr. So for him there is no minimum except its suitability as a consideration, just as there is no maximum for mahr by agreement. [2] His statement: 'If he specifies'; from specification, meaning if he mentions at the contract a mahr less than ten, the ten become obligatory, and his specification is void. And in this there is a difference of opinion with Zafar, as he says: mahr al-mithl (proper dower) is obligatory in this case, based on the principle that specification of what is not suitable as a mahr is like no specification. And in the case of no specification, mahr al-mithl is obligatory by agreement, as will come, Allah willing. (On) the Quranic texts about providing compensation for the vulval benefits, an-Nasafi said in his Tafsir (1:219) regarding the previous verse: In it is proof that marriage is only with a mahr, and that it is obligatory even if not specified, and that non-property is not suitable as a mahr, and that little is not suitable as a mahr, since a grain is not customarily considered property. (1) Refer to: at-Tanbih (p. 107), and Hashiyat al-Bujayrimi (3:445), and al-Ghurar al-Bahiyyah (4:182), and others. (2) This is not a matter of determining measures by opinion and analogy; rather, it is consideration of the amount of property that has significance in the eyes of the Noble Lawgiver to apply the summary of legal texts to it. Al-Babarti said in al-‘Inayah (3:320): 'Indeed, mahr is a right of the law in terms of its obligation, acting on His statement: "We know what We have prescribed for them concerning their wives" [33:50]. And that was to show the honor of the place, so it is measured by what has significance, which is ten, by analogy to the threshold for theft, because by it a respectable limb is ruined, so it is more fitting that by it the vulval benefits are owned.'
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn stating: 'And it [the mahr] is obligatory if he specifies less than it [ten dirhams], and if he specifies other than that [the actual specified amount applies, except when less than ten].' The commentary provides the Shafi'i position that any amount suitable as a price is valid. It then discusses the Hanafi proof by analogy to the theft threshold (nisab al-sariqa) of ten dirhams. An objection is raised that legal quantities cannot be set by mere reasoning, but the commentator refutes this by citing al-Babarti that this is not arbitrary but derives from the Lawgiver's consideration of what is significant property. The passage also notes the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf with Imam Zafar, who holds that when an invalid amount is specified, mahr al-mithl (proper dower) applies, not the fixed ten. The commentator concludes by quoting an-Nasafi and al-Babarti to reinforce the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife in marriage.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the amount given to women of similar status (e.g., family, beauty, etc.).
نصاب السرقة (nisab al-sariqa): The minimum value of stolen goods (ten dirhams) required for the application of the hadd punishment for theft.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a mahr specified at less than ten dirhams is void, and the wife automatically receives the minimum of ten dirhams.

Half Dower: Divorce Before Consummation and Valid Seclusion
Commentary explaining the half-dower ruling and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on half dower when divorce occurs before consummation or valid seclusion, and explain why both conditions are necessary.

Core Idea
Half dower is wajib if divorce occurs before either consummation or valid seclusion; both conditions are needed because they are not always coextensive.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that half the prescribed dower becomes obligatory upon divorce before consummation (intercourse) or before valid seclusion (khalwah sahiha). The commentator clarifies why the matn mentions both conditions separately: to cover cases where intercourse occurs without valid seclusion (e.g., during a prohibited time). We will explore the textual proof from the Quran, the definition of valid seclusion, and the logical objection that mentioning both is redundant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act triggers the half-dower obligation? Divorce before consummation or valid seclusion. The ruling is that half the dower becomes wajib (obligatory).
The ruling applies whether the dower is specified or unspecific.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:237, which commands giving half the prescribed dower upon divorce before consummation. The Hanafi school extends this to valid seclusion by analogy, as seclusion is legally considered like intercourse for dower purposes.
The dalil is qati in thubut (Quran) and qati in dalala (explicit command).
3
Understand valid seclusion (khalwah sahiha)
Valid seclusion means the husband and wife are alone in a place where intercourse is physically possible and there is no legal impediment (e.g., fasting Ramadan, ihram). Invalid seclusion occurs when an impediment exists and does not trigger the half-dower rule.
The commentary emphasizes that valid seclusion is distinct from actual intercourse.
4
Analyze the objection and response
An objector claims mentioning both 'before intercourse' and 'before valid seclusion' is redundant because if divorce is before seclusion, it must be before intercourse. The commentator refutes this by noting that intercourse can occur without valid seclusion (e.g., during Ramadan fast), so both conditions must be stated.
This shows the careful legal reasoning (istiqra) in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The mufta bihi position is that half dower becomes wajib upon divorce before consummation OR before valid seclusion. Both are separate conditions; if either is absent, the full dower (or half if consummation occurred) applies.
The preposition 'ba' in 'bi-talaq' indicates accompaniment, not causation, because the obligation arises from the marriage contract, not the divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلاق قبل وطء وخلوة صحت) : أي الخلوة الصحيحة، وسيجيه تفسيرها. فإن قلت : لِمَ لَم يَكْتَف بقولِهِ : قبل خلوة صحت ؛ فإنَّه إذا كان قبل الخلوة الصحيحة، كان قبل الوطء. فَنِصْفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ، والخلوة في حكم الوطء شرعاً في «باب المهـر» وغيره كما سيأتي ذكره إن شاء الله. ويمكن أن يكون ضمير نصفه راجعاً إلى كلِّ من المسمى في المسألة الثانية، والعشرة في الصورة الأولى : أي صورة تسمية الأقل من العشرة، فإنّ المسمى هناك وإن كان أقل؛ لكن هذه التسمية لغو شرعاً، فكأنه صار المسمّى هناك العشرة حكماً، فيجب تنصيفه عند الطلاق قبل الوطء. [1] قوله : بطلاق؛ الباء للمصاحبة لا للسببية؛ لمَّا مرَّ أن الوجوب بنفس العقد، كذا قال الشرنبلالي، ولو قال : بكل فرقة من قبله لكان أولى فيشمل ردّته وزناه وتقبيله ومعانقته لأم امرأته وبنتها قبل الخلوة. كذا في «جامع الرموز». [٢] قوله : قبل وطء؛ لو اكتفى بهذا أو أراد بالوطء أعم من أن يكون حقيقة أو حكماً لكفي، لكنه قصد التوضيح فذكر الخلوة أيضاً. [۳] قوله : أي الخلوة الصحيحة؛ تفسير الحاصل من الموصوف مع الصفة، واحترز به عن الخلوة الفاسدة؛ فإنها ليست في حكم الوطء في «باب المهر» على ما سيأتي. (٤) قوله : لم لم يكتف؛ حاصله : أن ذكر الوطء مع ذكر الخلوة مستدرك، فإن الطلاق إذا كان قبل الخلوة لا بُدَّ أن يكون قبل الوطء؛ لأن الوطء يكون في الخلوة لا في الجلوة، فإذا لم توجد الخلوة لم يوجد الوطء، فكان على المصنف له أن يكتفي على قوله : «خلوة صحت». قلت : لا نُسَلّم، فإنه يمكن أن يكون قبل الخلوة الصحيحة، ولا يكون قبل الوطء بأن وَطِئَ بلا خلوة صحيحة، نحو إن وَطِئَ مع وجود المانع الشرعي كصوم رمضان، ونحوه. [٤] قوله : قلت لا نسلّم؛ أي كون الطلاق قبل الوطء لازماً؛ لكونه قبل الخلوة الصحيحة؛ فلذلك احتيج إلى ذكرها ولم يكتف بأحدهما.
(Divorce before intercourse and valid seclusion): i.e., valid seclusion, and its explanation will come. If you say: Why was it not sufficient with his statement: before valid seclusion? For if it is before valid seclusion, it is before intercourse. Then half of what you prescribed [Qur'an 2:237] and valid seclusion is in the ruling of intercourse legally in the chapter of dower and elsewhere as will come. And it is possible that the pronoun 'half' refers to each of the named in the second case and ten in the first case: i.e., the case of naming less than ten; for the named there even if less, but this naming is void legally, so as if the named becomes ten by operation of law, so half is obligatory upon divorce before intercourse. [1] His statement: 'with divorce'; the ba is for accompaniment not causality; because obligation is by the contract itself, as stated by al-Shurunbulali. And if he said 'with every separation from him' it would be more appropriate to include his apostasy, his zinā, his kissing and embracing the mother of his wife and her daughter before seclusion. As in Jami' al-Rumuz. [2] His statement: 'before intercourse'; if he sufficed with this or intended intercourse to be general, real or constructive, it would suffice, but he intended clarification so he mentioned seclusion as well. [3] His statement: 'i.e., valid seclusion'; interpretation of the composite of described and adjective, and by it he excludes invalid seclusion; for it is not in the ruling of intercourse in the chapter of dower as will come. (4) His statement: 'why was it not sufficient'; its gist: that mentioning intercourse along with seclusion is redundant, because if divorce is before seclusion it must be before intercourse; for intercourse occurs in seclusion not in public, so if seclusion is not present intercourse is not present, so the author could have sufficed with his statement: 'valid seclusion'. I say: we do not accept, for it is possible that it is before valid seclusion but not before intercourse if he had intercourse without valid seclusion, like if he had intercourse while there is a legal impediment such as Ramadan fast and the like. [4] His statement: 'I say we do not accept'; i.e., that divorce before intercourse is necessary because it is before valid seclusion; therefore, it was necessary to mention it and not suffice with one of them.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that if a husband divorces his wife before both consummation (intercourse) and valid seclusion, the wife is entitled to half the dower (based on Quran 2:237). The commentator first clarifies that 'valid seclusion' (khalwah sahiha) means seclusion without any legal impediment to intercourse, such as fasting during Ramadan or ihram. The discussion then addresses why the matn mentions both 'before intercourse' and 'before valid seclusion' – to cover cases where intercourse occurs without valid seclusion (e.g., during a haram time), meaning the divorce could be before valid seclusion but not before intercourse. The commentator also examines the grammatical point that the preposition 'ba' in 'bi-talaq' indicates accompaniment, not causation, because the obligation of half dower arises from the contract itself, not the divorce. The ruling is expanded to include other forms of separation like apostasy or zinā. The author refutes the objection that mentioning both is redundant by providing the counterexample of intercourse during a fast. The relied-upon position is that both conditions must be established, and valid seclusion is a separate condition from intercourse.

Key Terms
خلوة صحيحة (khalwah sahiha): Valid seclusion between spouses without any legal impediment to intercourse (e.g., not fasting Ramadan or in ihram).
نصف ما فرضتم (nisfu ma faradtum): Half of the prescribed dower; the obligatory payment upon divorce before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the matn mention both 'before intercourse' and 'before valid seclusion' for the half-dower ruling?
A) Because valid seclusion is always accompanied by intercourse.
B) To cover cases where intercourse occurs without valid seclusion, such as during Ramadan fast.
C) Because the author wanted to emphasize both conditions.
D) To distinguish between real and constructive intercourse.

Key Takeaway
Half dower becomes wajib upon divorce only when both consummation and valid seclusion are absent; valid seclusion is a separate legal condition equivalent to intercourse for dower obligations.

Marriage Valid Without Dower or with Invalid Dower
Explaining that marriage is valid even without a dower or with an invalid dower such as wine or pig.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a marriage contract is valid without a dower or with a non-valuable dower, and determine the wife's entitlement to mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid even without dower; the wife receives proper dower instead.

Many assume that a marriage contract requires a dower, or that if the dower is something forbidden, the marriage itself becomes invalid. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi view: the dower is not a condition for validity. Even if the dower is omitted, denied, or specified as something worthless like wine or pig, the marriage remains valid. The wife's right to a proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is preserved. Let's explore the proof from the Quran and its application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the three scenarios covered: marriage without mentioning dower, with explicit negation, and with an invalid dower (e.g., wine, pig). The marriage is sahih in all.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse (Al-Baqarah 2:236) cited in the passage. Understand that it permits divorce before fixing a dower, implying the marriage contract can exist without a fixed dower.
The verse is qat'i in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse proves the ruling: if divorce is allowed before fixing a dower, then the marriage must be valid without a fixed dower. This covers both non-mention and negation.
4
Extend to invalid dower
Apply the same principle to cases where the specified dower has no legal value (e.g., wine, pig, carrion). Since the dower is not a condition, the marriage remains valid, but the specified item is void.
The wife gets mahr al-mithl instead.
5
Identify the consequence
The consequence of an invalid or missing dower is the obligation to pay mahr al-mithl (proper dower based on the wife's status). This ensures justice for the wife.
Note the exception for dhimmi specifying wine, mentioned but not detailed here.

وصح النكاح بلا ذكر مهر، ومع نفيه، وبخمر، أو خنزير. قوله : بلا ذكر مهر؛ أي عند العقد، وإنما يصح النكاح في هذه الصورة، وفي صورة نفي المهر بأن يصرح عند العقد بعدم إعطاء المهر؛ لأن ذكر المهر ليس بشرط في انعقاده، يدل عليه قوله تعالى: {لا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِن طَلقَهُمُ النِّسَاءَ مَا لَمْ تَمَسُّوهُنَّ أَوْ تَفْرِضُوا لَهُنَّ فَرِيضَةٌ}، فإنه يدل على جواز الطلاق قبل فرض الفريضة: أي المهر، وهو لا يمكن بدون انعقاد النكاح، فدل ذلك على جوازه بدون ذكره وتعيينه، وهو يشمل عدم الذكر مطلقاً ونفيه. ولما صح النكاح في هاتين الصورتين صح في صورة ما إذا ذكر في المهر ما لا قيمة له كالخمر والخنزير ونحوهما مما هو ليس بمتقوم شرعاً، وكذا في ذكر مجهول القيمة: كمطلق الثوب، والدابة، وذكر ما لا يصلح جعله مهراً لتعليم القرآن مما ليس بمال. [0] قوله : وبخمر؛ أي إذا سماه المسلم، وأما إن سماه الذمي فسيجيء ذكره في موضعه، ومثله التسمية بالميتة والدم، فإنه ليس بمال أصلاً.
(And the marriage contract is valid without mentioning a dower, and with its negation, and with wine or pig). His statement: without mentioning a dower; i.e., at the time of contract, and the marriage is valid in this case and in the case of negating the dower by explicitly stating at the contract that no dower will be given, because mentioning the dower is not a condition for its validity. This is indicated by His statement: {There is no sin upon you if you divorce women when you have not touched them nor specified for them an obligation}, for it indicates the permissibility of divorce before specifying the obligation, i.e., the dower, and that is not possible without the validity of the marriage contract; thus it indicates its validity without its mention and specification, and that includes absolute non-mention and negation. Since the marriage is valid in these two cases, it is valid in the case where something of no value is mentioned as dower, like wine, pig, and the like which are not legally valuable; likewise for mentioning something of unknown value, like an unspecified cloth or animal, and mentioning something unsuitable as dower like teaching Quran, which is not property. [0] His statement: 'and with wine'; i.e., if a Muslim specifies it, but if a dhimmi specifies it, its mention will come in its place; similarly, specification of carrion and blood, for they are not property at all.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage establishes that the validity of a marriage contract does not depend on the mention or fixation of a dower. The commentator explains that marriage is valid even if the dower is not mentioned at all, or even if it is explicitly negated (e.g., saying 'I marry you with no dower'). The proof is from Quran 2:236, which permits divorce before fixing a dower—since divorce presupposes a valid marriage, the marriage must be valid without a dower. This principle is extended to cases where the dower is something that has no legal value in Islamic law, such as wine, pig, carrion, or blood—items that are not considered property (mal). In such cases, the marriage remains valid, but the wife is entitled to the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) because the specified item is not legally effective. Similarly, if the dower is something of unknown value (e.g., an unspecified cloth) or something that cannot be dower (like teaching the Quran), the marriage is valid and proper dower is due. The commentator also notes that if a non-Muslim (dhimmi) specifies wine, the ruling may differ and will be discussed elsewhere.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): Dower or bridal gift; a financial obligation of the husband to the wife upon marriage.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Proper dower determined by the dower of women of similar status when no dower is specified or the specified dower is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because wine is considered wealth in Islamic law.
B) Because the marriage contract is independent of the dower; the invalid dower is replaced by mahr al-mithl.
C) Because wine is not prohibited for Muslims.
D) Because the dower is not required at all for validity.

Key Takeaway
Marriage is valid without dower or with an invalid dower; the wife is entitled to the proper dower (mahr al-mithl).

Validity of Marriage Without Dower or with Invalid Dower
Ruling and commentary on marriage validity without dower or with impermissible dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that marriage is valid without mentioning a dower or with an impermissible dower, and apply the proof from Quran 2:236 to distinguish the dower's obligation from the contract's validity.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, marriage is valid without a dower; the dower is a financial obligation, not a contractual condition.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition addresses a common concern: does a marriage contract need to include a dower (mahr) to be valid? The answer is clear: the marriage is valid even without mentioning a dower, even if the dower is explicitly negated, and even if something impermissible like wine or pig is named as dower. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Quran, and the practical consequences for the wife's right to a suitable dower (mahr al-mithl).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the marriage contract (nikah). The ruling is that it is sahih (valid) in all three scenarios: without mentioning a dower, with explicit negation of a dower, and with a dower that is non-property like wine or pig.
The Hanafi position is that mentioning a dower is not a condition (shart) of the contract.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:236, which permits divorce before specifying a dower. The commentary argues that divorce logically requires a valid marriage, so the verse implies the marriage itself is valid without a specified dower.
The dalil is naqli (Quranic) with qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'or have not specified for them an obligation (fariḍah)' shows that the marriage contract can exist without specifying the dower. Since divorce is contingent upon a valid marriage, the marriage must be valid ab initio.
This uses the principle that a necessary condition of a valid act is itself valid.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
In the case where the husband points to an object (e.g., a jar of vinegar) but it turns out to be wine, or points to a slave who is free, there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa holds the marriage valid; the two disagree in the slave example. The 'asahh' view is that the wife gets the indicated slave if it is actually a slave.
This shows that even when the specified dower is invalid, the marriage remains valid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that marriage is valid in all these cases, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl when the specified dower is invalid.
This is consistent with the statement in al-Wiqayah and confirmed by later authorities.

The Book of Marriage, Chapter of the Dower. And the marriage is valid without mentioning a dower, and with its negation, and with wine or a pig. I say: we do not concede, because it can be before a valid seclusion, and it is not before intercourse by having intercourse without valid seclusion, like if he had intercourse with the presence of a legal barrier such as fasting Ramadan and the like. [4] (And the marriage is valid without mentioning a dower, and with its negation, and with wine or a pig.) [1] He said: I say we do not concede; meaning that divorce before intercourse is binding because it is before valid seclusion; therefore it needed to be mentioned and one was not sufficient. [2] He said: without valid seclusion; even if absolute seclusion existed, for valid seclusion is more specific because it is restricted by the absence of a legal barrier to intercourse, as will be detailed. (3) He said: and the like; it is either a conjunction to fasting Ramadan, and its pronoun refers to it: meaning like fasting Ramadan such as the ihram of Hajj, or a conjunction to the legal barrier: meaning with the presence of the legal barrier and its like: such as a physical barrier, and its detail will come soon if Allah wills. [4] He said: without mentioning a dower; meaning at the contract. The marriage is valid in this case and in the case of negating the dower by explicitly stating at the contract that no dower is given, because mentioning the dower is not a condition for its validity. The proof for this is His saying: 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women when you have not touched them nor specified for them an obligation' (Quran 2:236). For it indicates the permissibility of divorce before specifying the obligation, i.e., the dower, and that is not possible without the marriage being valid. So that indicates its permissibility without mentioning and specifying it, and it includes absolute omission and negation. And since marriage is valid in these two cases, it is valid in the case where one mentions as dower something that has no value, like wine and pig and the like, which are not legally valuable, and likewise in mentioning something of unknown value, like an absolute garment or animal, and mentioning something that cannot be made a dower, like teaching the Quran, which is not property. And with this jar of vinegar, and it is wine, and with this slave, and he is free, and with a garment and an animal whose type is not specified, and with teaching the Quran, and with the service of a free husband to her for one year. And in marrying his daughter with this jar of vinegar, and it is wine, and with this slave, and he is free, and with a garment and an animal whose type is not specified, and with teaching the Quran, and with the service of a free husband to her for one year: He restricted it to the free because if he were a slave, service would be obligatory, and it will come. (And in marrying his daughter) [1] He said: and with this jar; it is - with a fatha on the dāl, and shadda on the nūn - meaning the earthenware jar. Its mention is incidental. The summary: that the marriage is valid when the dower is mentioned, and he pointed to something unlawful. If he mentioned something that cannot be made a dower, and pointed to something that can be made a dower, like this free (slave), and he is a slave, then she gets the indicated slave in the most correct view. The division is fourfold: for either both the mentioned and the indicated are unlawful, or both are lawful and different, or the mentioned is unlawful and the indicated is unlawful, or the opposite. The dower of the like is obligatory when both are unlawful or the indicated is unlawful, and the specification is valid in the remaining cases. As stated in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Nahr'. [2] He said: and with a garment; meaning the marriage is valid when he mentions the dower and makes it an absolute garment or an animal or a house or the like, and does not specify what removes the ignorance. [3] He said: he did not specify their type; the type according to the jurists and usul scholars is what applies to many different things with different purposes; garments are different types, and likewise the animal, the living being, and the house. [4] He said: and with teaching the Quran; meaning the husband teaching his wife the Quran. [0] He said: and in marrying; this is the marriage called shighār - with a kasra on the shīn - emptiness.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the validity of marriage (nikah) in various cases concerning the dower (mahr). The author begins by stating that marriage is valid (sahih) without mentioning a dower, even if the dower is explicitly negated, and even if the dower is something impermissible by Islamic law, such as wine or a pig. The commentary explains that this is because mentioning a dower is not a condition for the validity of the marriage contract, according to the Hanafi school. The proof is from Quran 2:236, which permits divorce before specifying a dower, implying that the marriage contract itself was valid without it. This verse covers both absolute omission and explicit negation of the dower. The passage then extends the ruling: if a dower is mentioned but is something without value in Islamic law (like wine, pig, carrion, or blood), the marriage is still valid, but the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers). Similarly, if the dower is something unknown in value, like an unspecified garment or animal, or non-property like teaching Quran, the marriage is valid, and mahr al-mithl is due. The commentary also addresses cases where the dower is specified by pointing to an object, e.g., 'this jar of vinegar' but it is actually wine, or 'this slave' but he is free. The Hanafi position is that the marriage is valid, and the wife gets the indicated object if it can be suitable, otherwise mahr al-mithl. There is a difference of opinion with the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in some of these cases, as noted. The passage also touches on shighār marriage (exchanging daughters without mahr), which is invalid in the Hanafi school. Throughout, the commentary follows the order of the matn, clarifying each phrase and providing legal principles.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridewealth given by the husband to the wife as a matrimonial gift.
خمر (khamr): Wine or any intoxicating beverage that is not considered property (mal mutaqawwim) in Islamic law.
خلوة صحيحة (khalwah sahihah): A valid private seclusion between a married couple, free from any legal or physical barrier to intercourse.
شغار (shighar): A marriage where two men exchange their daughters or sisters without any dower, each marrying the other's female relative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a marriage is contracted without mentioning any dower?
A) The marriage is invalid.
B) The marriage is valid, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
C) The marriage is valid, but no dower is owed.
D) The marriage is valid only if the wife agrees to forgo the dower.

Key Takeaway
Marriage is valid without a dower; the dower is a wajib financial right, not a condition of the contract.

Validity of Marriage with Ambiguous or Haram Mahr
Explaining cases where mahr is valid despite ambiguity or haram mention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which mahr specifications in marriage lead to a valid marriage with mahr al-mithl versus those where the specification stands, and apply the Hanafi rule that marriage is not invalidated by mahr ambiguity.

Core Idea
Marriage remains sahih even if mahr is ambiguous or haram; mahr al-mithl becomes due when specification fails.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya illustrates a key Hanafi principle: the validity of a marriage contract does not depend on the mahr being perfectly specified or halal. Several examples show that even if the mahr points to something haram or is left ambiguous, the marriage is sahih, and the mahr is resolved either by giving the actual pointed item or by wajib mahr al-mithl. Understanding this prevents the mistaken belief that such defects nullify the marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching ruling
The passage repeatedly states that the marriage is valid (sahih) in all given scenarios. Identify that the ruling is about the validity of the marriage itself, not about the mahr's per se.
The marriage is not invalidated by a defective mahr.
2
List the examples of problematic mahr
Go through each example: ‘with this jar of vinegar’ (but it's wine), ‘with this slave’ (but he is free), ‘with a garment’ (unspecified genus), ‘with an animal’ (unspecified genus), ‘with teaching the Quran’, ‘with service for a year’. Note that some involve pointing to an object, others are purely verbal mentions.
Some examples have a ‘mentioned’ and a ‘pointed’ item; others have only a mention.
3
Understand the fourfold division
The commentary classifies cases with both a mentioned and a pointed item into four groups: (a) both haram, (b) both halal but different, (c) mentioned haram, pointed haram, (d) mentioned halal, pointed haram (or the opposite). The consequence: if both are haram or the pointed is haram, mahr al-mithl is wajib; otherwise the specification (pointed item) stands.
The division applies only when there is a specific pointing.
4
Determine when mahr al-mithl applies
Extract the rule: whenever the mahr as specified is invalid (e.g., haram, impossible, or excessively ambiguous), the marriage remains sahih but mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. For purely verbal ambiguous mentions (like ‘garment’ without genus), the ambiguity is considered excessive, so mahr al-mithl is due.
The passage confirms marriage is valid even in those cases, and by Hanafi law, mahr al-mithl fills the gap.
5
Examine the special case of the slave
If the husband points to a person whom he believes is free (making it impossible as mahr) but the person turns out to be a slave (valid mahr), the wife receives that slave. The commentary says this is al-asahh (the most correct view).
This shows that if the pointed item is actually valid, it becomes the mahr even if the husband's description was wrong.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا الدَّنّ من الخلّ ، فإذا هو خمرٌ وبهذا العبد فهو حرّ، وبثوب وبدابة لم يبين جنسهما، وبتعليم القرآن، وبخدمة الزوج الحر لها سنة. (1) وبهذا الدنا. من الخل، فإذا هو خمر (1)، وبهذا العبدِ فهو حرّ ، وبثوب" [٢] وبداية لم يبين جنسهما " ، وبتعليم القرآن ، وبخدمة الزوج الحر لها سنة) (۲) : وإنما قيد بالحر ؛ لأنه لو كان عبداً تَجِبُ الخدمة وسيجيء. [١] قوله : وبهذا الدن؛ هو - بفتح الدال المهملة، وتشديد النون - : أي الجرة من الخزف والطين، وذكره اتفاقي حاصله : أن يصح النكاح فيما ذكر المهر، وأشار إلى شيء حرام، فلو ذكر ما لا يمكن جعله مهراً، وأشار إلى ما يمكن جعله مهراً كهذا الحرّ، فإذا هو عبد يكون لها العبد المشار إليه في الأصح. والقسمة رباعية ؛ لأنه إما أن يكون كل من المذكور والمشار إليه حرامين، أو يكون كل منهما حلالين مختلفين، وإما أن يكون المذكور حراماً والمشار إليه حراماً، وإما أن يكون بالعكس، فيجب مهر المثل فيما إذا كانا حرامين، أو المشار إليه حراماً، وتصح التسمية في الباقين. كذا في «البحر» و «النهر) [٢] قوله : وبثوب ؛ أي يصحُ النكاحُ فيما إذا ذكر المهر وجعله مطلق ثوب أو دابة (ر) (٤) أو دار أو نحو ذلك ولم يبين ما يرتفع به الجهالة.
