[٤]قوله : وبتعليم القرآن ؛ أي تعليم الزوج امرأته القرآن.
And with this jar of vinegar, and it is wine, and with this slave, and he is free, and with a garment and an animal without specifying their genus, and with teaching the Quran, and with the service of a free husband for her for a year. (1) And with this jar of vinegar, and it is wine (1), and with this slave, and he is free, and with a garment [2] and an animal without specifying their genus, and with teaching the Quran, and with the service of the free husband for her for a year (2): and he only restricted with 'free' because if he were a slave, service would be obligatory, and it will come. [1] He said: and with this jar; it is - with fath of the unimportant dal and tashdid of nun - meaning the earthenware jar of clay and pottery, and its mention is accidental. Summary: that the marriage is valid when he mentions the mahr and points to something haram; if he mentions what cannot be made a mahr and points to what can be made a mahr like this free person, and he turns out to be a slave, then she gets the slave pointed to in the most correct view. And the division is fourfold: either both the mentioned and the pointed are haram, or both are halal but different, or the mentioned is haram and the pointed is haram, or the opposite. In the case where both are haram or the pointed is haram, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, and the specification is valid in the remaining cases. Thus in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. [2] He said: and with a garment; meaning the marriage is valid when he mentions the mahr and makes it an absolute garment or animal (r) (4) or house or similar, and does not specify what removes the ambiguity. [3] He said: he did not specify their genus; genus according to the jurists and usul scholars is that which applies to many different things with different purposes; thus garments are different genera, and similarly the animal, the living creature, and the house. [4] He said: and teaching the Quran; meaning the husband teaching his wife the Quran.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on the ruling of mahr specification in marriage. The matn lists several examples: mahr is mentioned as a jar of vinegar (but points to wine), a slave (but points to free), an unspecified garment or animal, teaching Quran, or service for a year. The commentary explains that the marriage is valid in all these cases, and the mahr is determined based on the actual pointed object or by mahr al-mithl if the mentioned mahr is invalid. The fourfold division classifies the combination of mentioned and pointed items (both haram, both halal but different, etc.). The definition of 'jins' is given to clarify when ambiguity is removed.

Key Terms
الدَّنّ (al-dann): A large earthenware jar used for storing liquids like vinegar or wine.
الجنس (al-jins): A genus that encompasses many sub-types; used here to indicate that specifying only 'garment' or 'animal' is too ambiguous due to multiple genera.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a husband specifies the mahr as 'with this jar of vinegar' but it turns out to be wine, what is the ruling?
A) Marriage is invalid because the mahr is haram.
B) Marriage is valid and the wife gets the jar of wine.
C) Marriage is valid and the wife gets mahr al-mithl.
D) Marriage is valid and the wife gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law upholds the validity of marriage even when the mahr is ambiguous, haram, or improperly specified; the mahr is resolved through mahr al-mithl or by the actual pointed object.

Shighar Marriage: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute resolving shighar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shighar marriage, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
In shighar marriage, the prohibition targets the absence of mahr, not the contract itself—marriage is valid, mahr al-mithl is wajib.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over shighar, an exchange marriage where two men marry each other's female relatives without any additional mahr. Understanding how the Hanafis maintain the validity of the marriage while nullifying the mahr specification reveals a key principle: prohibitions affecting a condition do not necessarily invalidate the underlying contract. We will walk through the proofs and counter-proofs to grasp the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that a shighar marriage is sahih (valid) but the specification of mahr (the exchange itself) is invalid, so mahr al-mithl (comparable dowry) becomes wajib for each woman. Identify what the matn states and how Fath al-Qadir expands it.
The marriage contract is not corrupted by the invalid mahr term.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues the marriage is batil (void) based on the hadith of Ibn Umar (six collections) where the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade shighar. He also uses a logical argument: each woman is both a mahr and a married object, leading to a conflict. Note the two prongs: transmitted (naqli) and rational (aqli).
The opposing dalil is the apparent generality of the prohibition.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the prohibition (and negation) in the hadith applies to the 'name' of shighar, i.e., the absence of mahr, not to the marriage contract itself. By obligating mahr al-mithl, the defective condition is removed, and the marriage stands valid. The prohibition is interpreted as karahah (dislike), not tahrim affecting validity. Also, qiyas is made on cases where mahr is invalid but marriage remains valid.
The hadith is understood through the principle that al-amr wa al-nahy relate to the supplementary condition, not the essence.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis treat the marriage as fully valid (inheritance, iddah, etc.) with an obligation to pay mahr al-mithl. Shafi'is require annulment if not yet consummated. This difference affects the rights of the women and the stability of the union.
This is a live ikhtilaf with real-world implications.
5
Note the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) opinion in the school, as explained by al-Kamal ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir. The text shows that the Hanafi response refutes both the transmitted and rational arguments of the opponent.
Tarjih is based on the strength of the Hanafi reading of the hadith and the supporting qiyas.

And regarding marrying his daughter or his sister to him on condition that he marries his daughter or sister to him in exchange for the two contracts. It is said: a empty land if it lacks authority, and it is that a man marries his precious one: his daughter or sister or others to another man on condition that the other marries his precious one to him, and there is no mahr except this. Thus in al-Mughrib. [11] He said: meaning the marriage is valid... etc.; he said in Fath al-Qadir: the ruling of this contract in our view is its validity and corruption of the specification, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i said: the contract is invalid according to transmitted and rational evidence. As for transmitted: the hadith of Ibn Umar reported by the six: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ forbade shighar, and it is that a man marries on condition that he marries his daughter or sister, and there is no dowry between them.' And prohibition implies corruption of the prohibited. And from him he said: 'There is no shighar in Islam,' and negation removes its existence in the Shariah. As for the second: because each pudendum is at that time a dowry and a married object, so it becomes shared between the two husbands, and the mahr is claimed, and this is invalid. The answer: Regarding the first, the subject of the prohibition and negation is the named shighar, and its meaning includes its being free from (1) al-Mughrib (p. 252). (2) It is an indication that the prohibition is for the naming of the mahr, not for the marriage itself, so the marriage remains valid. And the prohibition is for karahah, so the Shariah obligates two things: karahah and mahr al-mithl. The first is taken from the prohibition, and the second from the evidences indicating that when something unsuitable as mahr is named, the contract obligates mahr al-mithl. This second evidence is a proof to interpret the prohibition as karahah not corruption. See al-Bada'i (2:278), Radd al-Muhtar (3:106), al-Tabyin (2:145), etc. (3) In Sahih al-Bukhari (5:1966) etc. (4) Meaning the linguistic meaning: in the marriage free of mahr, and by obligating mahr al-mithl for each, this shighar is removed, so the prohibition in the hadith ceases. See al-Mabsut (15:155), Fath al-Qadir (3:249), etc. (0) In Sahih Muslim (2:1035) and Sahih Ibn Hibban (7:416), etc.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning shighar marriage (exchange marriage). The matn states the Hanafi ruling: marriage is sahih but the mahr specification is null, so mahr al-mithl is wajib. Al-Shafi'i argues that the marriage is batil based on hadith prohibiting shighar and the logical argument that each woman is both a mahr and a married object, causing conflict. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the prohibition applies to the lack of mahr, not the marriage itself, so the marriage remains valid but mahr al-mithl is due. The hadith prohibition is interpreted as karahah (dislike), not tahrim (prohibition) affecting validity.

Key Terms
الشغار (al-shighar): A marriage where two men exchange female relatives (daughters or sisters) without any other mahr; each woman is the dowry for the other.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The comparable dowry given to a woman of similar status in her family; paid when the specified mahr is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of shighar marriage?
A) The marriage is batil (invalid).
B) The marriage is sahih (valid) but with no mahr.
C) The marriage is sahih and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
D) The marriage is sahih and the specified exchange is valid as mahr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates shighar marriage but obligates mahr al-mithl because the prohibitory hadith targets the absence of mahr, not the marriage itself.

Nikah — Marriage

Ruling on Shighar Marriage: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i Dispute
Presents Hanafi position on Shighar and refutes Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Shighar marriage, identify the Shafi'i objection and its dalil, and explain how the Hanafis refute each objection using usul principles.

Core Idea
Shighar marriage is valid in the Hanafi madhhab but requires mahr al-mithl, not the reciprocal marriage.

Shighar marriage—where two men marry each other's female relatives without any dower except the exchange itself—seems prohibited by a clear hadith. Yet the Hanafi school upholds the validity of the contract, a position that appears to contradict the primary text. In this lesson, we will unpack the Hanafi reasoning, compare it to the Shafi'i critique, and see how the school applies its usul methodology to reconcile the hadith with general principles of contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
State what Shighar is and the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i proof: the hadith of Ibn Umar
Examine the explicit prohibition and the logical structure that leads to invalidity.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith
See how Hanafis argue that the prohibition targets the essence (absence of mahr) not the contract itself, and that the contract remains valid by qiyas.
4
Analyze the second Shafi'i proof: shared ownership argument
Understand the rational objection and the Hanafi rebuttal denying co-ownership.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Contrast the legal outcomes for couples in each madhhab.

And from him that he said: 'There is no shighar in Islam,' and negation removes its existence in the law. As for the second: because each sexual organ then is a dowry and a married object, so it becomes shared between the two spouses, and the mahr is claimed, and that is invalid. The answer: Regarding the first: the object of the prohibition and negation is the essence of shighar, and what is in its concept: its being devoid of the dowry and making the sexual organ a dowry, and we affirm the negation of this essence, and what is legally applicable to it, so the marriage is not established like that, but rather it invalidates it, so it remains a marriage in which something that is not suitable as a mahr is named, so it is contracted obligating mahr al-mithl like a marriage in which wine or pork is named. And what is the object of the prohibition we did not affirm, and what we affirmed is not connected to it, rather general proofs necessitate its validity, meaning what effects the contract with mahr al-mithl when no mahr is named, or when what is not suitable is named. And regarding the second: by conceding the invalidity of co-ownership in this chapter, and we did not affirm it, since there is no co-ownership without entitlement, and we have nullified it being a dowry. [1] He said: 'meaning the case of being... etc.'; this is included in the meaning of shighar, which is that the marriage is devoid of mahr, and the mahr from both sides is the marriage of his noble daughter to the other. So if this is not the case, it is not shighar, such as mentioning the mahr with the condition that he marries his client or not mentioning the mahr, and not making his marriage the mahr, but rather stipulating separately. Likewise in al-Nahr. [2] He said: 'in all'; i.e., all the mentioned cases. As for the obligation of mahr al-mithl in the case of not mentioning or negating the mahr, it is due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: A man married a woman and did not fix a dowry for her and died before consummating, so Ibn Mas'ud was asked and said: She has the mahr of her peers. Allah? So Ma'qil ibn Sinan testified that he had seen the Messenger of Allah adjudicate likewise. It was narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and authenticated by al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, al-Hakim, and others.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling of Shighar marriage. The Hanafi school holds that the marriage contract in Shighar is valid, but the specified mahr (which is the exchange of women) is invalid; therefore, mahr al-mithl (dower of the like) becomes obligatory. The Shafi'i school holds that the contract is invalid based on two proofs: (1) the hadith of Ibn Umar in which the Prophet forbade Shighar, and prohibition implies corruption of the prohibited act; and (2) rational argument that each woman is both a mahr and a wife, creating a shared ownership. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the essence of Shighar (which the prohibition targets) and the marriage contract itself. They argue that the prohibited Shighar is the form where the marriage is devoid of any mahr and the mahr is the act of marrying the other woman. In the Hanafi view, when a marriage contract includes an invalid mahr, the contract remains valid and mahr al-mithl is due, analogous to a marriage where wine or pork is stipulated as mahr. The prohibition is thus interpreted as makruh (disliked) rather than invalid. The second objection is answered by denying that any shared ownership occurs: since the mahr specification is void, no actual sharing of the women as property takes place. The commentary further clarifies that Shighar only applies when the mahr is solely the reciprocal marriage; if additional conditions or a different mahr are mentioned, it is not Shighar. The obligation of mahr al-mithl for marriages without a specified mahr is supported by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.

Key Terms
شغار (shighār): A marriage where two men marry each other's female relatives (daughters or sisters) with no mahr except the reciprocal marriage. The text also defines it as a marriage devoid of mahr where the mahr is the marriage of the other's relative.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of women similar to the bride in social status, family, and other relevant factors. It is mandatory when no mahr is specified or when the specified mahr is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on a Shighar marriage (where the mahr is the reciprocal marriage of a relative)?
A) The marriage is invalid and must be annulled immediately.
B) The marriage is valid but the specified mahr is void, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory.
C) The marriage is valid with the specified mahr as agreed.
D) The marriage is valid only if the mahr is mentioned separately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates Shighar marriage but obligates mahr al-mithl, reconciling the prohibition with general contract principles.

Mahr al-Mithl When Mahr is Invalid or Omitted: Ruling and Dispute on Teaching Quran
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on mahr al-mithl and teaching Quran as mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr al-mithl when mahr is omitted or invalid, identify the dalil from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and evaluate the Shafi'i argument regarding teaching Quran as mahr with the Hanafi response and later fatwa.

Core Idea
Omitting or invalidating mahr triggers mahr al-mithl; teaching Quran as mahr is disputed but later Hanafi fatwa allows it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains that when no mahr is named or an invalid mahr is named, mahr al-mithl becomes wajib upon intercourse or death. The author supports this with the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and addresses the Shafi'i objection based on the hadith of marriage for teaching Quran. The lesson will walk through the ruling, the proof, and the inter-madhhab dispute, including the evolution of the Hanafi position on teaching Quran as mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on marriages where the mahr is omitted or an invalid mahr is named (e.g., wine, teaching Quran). The author states that mahr al-mithl becomes wajib (obligatory) in all such cases upon intercourse or death.
The ruling applies whether the mahr is omitted entirely, explicitly negated, or named something unsuitable.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof for the ruling when no mahr is mentioned is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet judged a woman to have mahr al-mithl when her husband died without fixing a dower.
This hadith is extended by analogy (qiyas) to cases where an invalid mahr is named, treating the naming as void.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly gives the ruling of mahr al-mithl when no dower is fixed. The Hanafi school extends this to invalid named mahr because the naming is considered non-existent (laghw).
The hadith's thubut is zanni (ahad) but its dalala is considered qati (definitive) by the Hanafis regarding the ruling.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school argues that teaching Quran can be a valid mahr, citing the hadith where the Prophet married a man to a woman 'bima ma'aka min al-Quran'. The Hanafi response is that the preposition 'ba' indicates causation (sababiyya), not exchange.
This ikhtilaf leads to a practical difference: Shafi'i validates the marriage with teaching Quran as mahr; classical Hanafi invalidates the naming and imposes mahr al-mithl.
5
Evaluate the later Hanafi fatwa
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Bahr, Fath al-Qadir) note that since ijarah (hiring) for teaching Quran is now permissible, naming it as mahr becomes valid. The mufta bihi (operative position) aligns with the Shafi'i view in this regard.
This shows that Hanafi fiqh can evolve with changes in mu'amalat (transactions) and custom ('urf).

ولزم مهر مثلها في الجميع عند وطء، أو موت وقوله : معاوضة ؛ يمكن أن يكون تمييزاً ، أو حالا عن التزويج : أي حال كون التزويج تعويضاً لهذا العقد بذلك العقد، ولذلك العقد بهذا.
(ولزِمَ مهر مثلها في الجميع" عند وطء، أو موت)
الصداق وكون البضع صداقاً، ونحن قائلون بنفي هذه الماهية، وما يصدق عليها شرعاً، فلا يثبت النكاح كذلك، بل يبطله ، فيبقى نكاحاً سمى فيه ما لا يصلح مهراً، فينعقد موجباً لمهر المثل كالنكاح المسمى فيه خمر أو خنزير. وما هو متعلّق النهي لم نثبته وما أثبتناه لم يتعلّق بـه ، بل اقتضت العمومات صحته أعني ما يفيد الانعقاد بمهر المثل عند عدم تسميته المهر، وتسميته ما لا يصلح
وعن الثاني : بتسليم بطلان الشركة في هذا الباب، ونحن لم نثبته إذ لا شركة بدون الاستحقاق، وقد أبطلنا كونه صداقاً.
[١] قوله : أي حال كون ... الخ ؛ هذا داخل في مسمى الشغار، وهو أن يخلو النكاح عن المهر، ويكون المهر من الطرفين هو إنكاح كريمته الآخر، فلو لم يكن هذا فليس بشغار ، كأن يذكر المهر مع شرط أن يزوجه موليّته أو لا يذكر المهر، ولا يجعلُ إنكاحه مهراً ، بل يشترط على حدة. كذا في «النهر».
[٢] قوله : في الجميع؛ أي جميع الصور المذكورة، أما وجوب مهر المثل في صورة عدم الذكر، أو نفي المهر ؛ فلحديث ابن مسعود : إن رجلاً تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقاً ومات قبل أن يدخل بها فسئل ابن مسعود ، فقال : لها مهر مثل نسائها ، طالله (۱) فشهد معقل بن سنان له أنه كذلك قضى رسول الله ) ، أخرجه أبو داود والترْمِذِيُّ وصححه النسائي وابن ماجة والحاكم وصححه وغيرهم.
ويلحق بها لو ذكر ما لا يصلح مهراً : إما لعدم المالية : كتعليم القرآن، وإما لعدم المالية المتقدمة كما في ذكر الخمر ونحوه، ومثله ما لو أشار إلى ما لا يصلح مهراً، وهو
للجهالة الفاحشة، كما في صورة ذكر الثوب والدابة.
وبالجملة فالصور التي سُمِّي فيها شيء من الصور المذكورة التسمية فيها لغو،
فيجعلُ الذكرُ كعدم الذكرِ فيجبُ مهر المثل كما في صورة عدم الذكر. وأما حديث البخاري وغيره : إنه قال لرجل : «التمس ولو خاتماً من حديد، فالتمس فلم يجد شيئاً ، فقال : هل معك شيء من القرآن ، قال : نعم ؛ سورة كذا وكذا ، فقال : قد ملكتها بما معك من القرآن» (١) ، وهو الذي استدل به الشافعي له على أن المهر قد يكون غير المال.
فأجاب أصحابنا عنه : بأن الباء هنا ليست للمعوض، بل للسببية أو التعليل، وذكر في «فتح القدير»: إنه لَمَّا جوز الشافعي له أخذ الأجرة على تعليم القرآن صحح تسميته مهرا ـراً(۳) ، فكذا نقول : يلزم على المفتي بـه صـحة تسميته صداقاً ، ولم أر من
تعرض له. انتهى.
وفي «البحر»: سيأتي في «كتاب الاجارات»: إن الفتوى على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن والفقه، فينبغي أن يصح تسميته مهراً ؛ لأن ما أجاز أخذ الأجرة في مقابلتِهِ من المنافع جاز تسميته صداقاً كما قدمنا نقله عن «البدائع»(4). انتهى
And mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory in all cases upon intercourse or death. And his statement 'mu'awada' (exchange) can be a specification or a condition of the marriage: meaning that the marriage is a compensation for this contract with that contract, and for that contract with this. (And mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory in all cases upon intercourse or death). The dower and that the vulva is a dower, and we maintain the negation of this essence and what is legally true of it, so marriage is not established like that, rather it invalidates it. So it remains a marriage in which something unsuitable as dower is named, so it is contracted necessitating mahr al-mithl, like a marriage in which wine or pig is named. And what is the object of the prohibition we do not affirm, and what we have affirmed is not connected to it, rather the general evidences require its validity, meaning that which benefits the conclusion (of the contract) with mahr al-mithl when the dower is not named, and naming something unsuitable. And concerning the second (objection): by admitting the nullity of partnership in this chapter, and we have not affirmed it, since there is no partnership without entitlement, and we have nullified its being a dower. [1] His statement: 'meaning that it is...' etc.; this is included in the definition of shighar, which is that the marriage is free from dower, and the dower from both sides is the marriage of each one's female ward to the other. If this is not the case, it is not shighar, such as mentioning the dower with the condition that he marry his ward, or not mentioning the dower and not making his marriage the dower, but rather stipulating separately. This is in 'al-Nahr'. [2] His statement: 'in all cases'; i.e., all the mentioned forms. As for the obligation of mahr al-mithl in the case of not mentioning (the dower) or negating it, it is due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: A man married a woman and did not fix a dower for her, and died before consummating the marriage. Ibn Mas'ud was asked and said: She has the mahr of women like her. Then Ma'qil ibn Sinan testified that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) had judged likewise. It was narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and authenticated by al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, and al-Hakim, and others. And it is attached to it (the same ruling) if he mentions something unsuitable as dower: either due to lack of property (mal), like teaching the Quran, or due to lack of the mentioned property, as in mentioning wine and the like, and similarly if he indicates something unsuitable as dower due to gross ignorance, as in the case of mentioning a garment or an animal. In summary, the forms in which something from the mentioned forms is named, the naming is void, so the mention is treated as non-mention, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory as in the case of non-mention. As for the hadith of al-Bukhari and others: He (ﷺ) said to a man: 'Seek (something to give), even if it is an iron ring.' He sought but found nothing. He said: 'Do you have anything of the Quran?' He said: 'Yes, Surah such-and-such.' He said: 'I have married her to you for what you have of the Quran.' This is what al-Shafi'i used as evidence that the dower can be other than property. Our scholars responded that the 'ba' here is not for exchange, but for causation or reason. And it is mentioned in 'Fath al-Qadir': When al-Shafi'i permitted taking a wage for teaching the Quran, he validated its naming as dower. So we say: The mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion necessitates the validity of naming it as dower, and I have not seen anyone addressing it. End. And in 'al-Bahr': It will come in the Book of Ijarat (hire) that the fatwa is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran and fiqh, so it should be valid to name it as dower, because whatever permits taking a wage in exchange for benefits allows its naming as dower, as we previously quoted from 'al-Bada'i'. End.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory in all cases of invalid or omitted mahr upon intercourse or death. The author first discusses shighar (exchange marriage) where no mahr is specified, and explains that such a marriage is not valid because the vulva cannot be a mahr. However, if the marriage is contracted with an invalid mahr (like wine or pig), the marriage is valid but mahr al-mithl is due, as the invalid naming is treated as void. The proof for mahr al-mithl when no mahr is mentioned is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet judged a woman to have mahr al-mithl when her husband died before consummation without fixing a dower. The same ruling applies when an invalid mahr is mentioned, such as teaching Quran (which is not property) or wine. The passage then addresses a Shafi'i objection based on the hadith where the Prophet married a man to a woman for teaching Quran. The Hanafi response is that the preposition 'ba' in 'bima ma'aka min al-Quran' indicates causation, not exchange, so the hadith does not prove that teaching Quran is a valid mahr. However, later Hanafi fatwa from 'Fath al-Qadir' and 'al-Bahr' notes that since hiring for teaching Quran is now permissible, naming it as mahr becomes valid. This shows the evolution of the Hanafi position from classical to later practice.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what women of similar status receive, determined by consideration of family, beauty, wealth, etc.
شغار (shighar): A marriage where the dower for each bride is the marriage of the other bride to the other groom, i.e., exchange marriage with no separate mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument about the hadith of teaching Quran as mahr, what is the meaning of the preposition 'ba' in 'bima ma'aka min al-Quran'?
A) For exchange (mu'awada)
B) For causation or reason (sababiyya or ta'lil)
C) For accompaniment (ma'iyya)
D) For instrumentality (istishhad)

Key Takeaway
When mahr is omitted or invalid, mahr al-mithl is wajib; teaching Quran as mahr is accepted in later Hanafi fatwa due to ijarah permissibility.

Teaching Quran as Mahr: Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute and Fatwa Evolution
Hanafi commentary on invalid mahr and the hadith about teaching Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on teaching Quran as mahr, state the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the later Hanafi fatwa that permits it.

Core Idea
Teaching Quran cannot be mahr originally; later fatwa permits it when hiring for teaching is allowed.

This passage from a Hanafi sharh addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: can teaching the Quran be validly named as the dower? The Shafi'i school cites a hadith where the Prophet accepted teaching Quran as mahr. The Hanafi school originally rejects this because mahr must be property. However, later Hanafi fatwas, under necessity, permit hiring for teaching, making teaching Quran a valuable benefit and thus valid as mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage first states that mentioning something invalid as mahr (e.g., teaching Quran, wine) makes the naming void, and the husband must pay mahr al-mithl.
This is the general Hanafi rule from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Locate the Shafi'i proof
The hadith from al-Bukhari is presented: the Prophet accepted teaching Quran as mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i uses this to argue that mahr can be non-property.
The hadith is sahih but its interpretation differs.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret the preposition 'ba' in the hadith as sababiyya (causation) not badal (compensation). Also, teaching Quran is not considered property because it is an act of worship and cannot be sold or rented.
This argument relies on usul al-fiqh principles of amr and nahy.
4
Trace the later fatwa evolution
Later Hanafi scholars (al-Bada'i, al-Bahr, Fath al-Qadir) permitted ijara for teaching Quran due to necessity. Since ijara is valid, teaching becomes a valuable benefit, thus valid as mahr.
This is a shift from the original position, based on istihsan and necessity.
5
Evaluate the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Shafi'i, any teaching suffices; under original Hanafi, mahr al-mithl is wajib; under later Hanafi fatwa, teaching is valid if ijara is permitted, but not automatically.
The later fatwa aligns Hanafis closer to the Shafi'i position in practice.

ويلحق بها لو ذكر ما لا يصلح مهراً : إما لعدم المالية : كتعليم القرآن، وإما لعدم المالية المتقدمة كما في ذكر الخمر ونحوه، ومثله ما لو أشار إلى ما لا يصلح مهراً، وهو للجهالة الفاحشة، كما في صورة ذكر الثوب والدابة. وبالجملة فالصور التي سُمِّي فيها شيء من الصور المذكورة التسمية فيها لغو، فيجعلُ الذكرُ كعدم الذكرِ فيجبُ مهر المثل كما في صورة عدم الذكر. وأما حديث البخاري وغيره : إنه قال لرجل : «التمس ولو خاتماً من حديد، فالتمس فلم يجد شيئاً ، فقال : هل معك شيء من القرآن ، قال : نعم ؛ سورة كذا وكذا ، فقال : قد ملكتها بما معك من القرآن» (١) ، وهو الذي استدل به الشافعي له على أن المهر قد يكون غير المال. فأجاب أصحابنا عنه : بأن الباء هنا ليست للمعوض، بل للسببية أو التعليل، وذكر في «فتح القدير»: إنه لَمَّا جوز الشافعي له أخذ الأجرة على تعليم القرآن صحح تسميته مهراً، فكذا نقول : يلزم على المفتي بـه صـحة تسميته صداقاً ، ولم أر من تعرض له. انتهى. وفي «البحر»: سيأتي في «كتاب الاجارات»: إن الفتوى على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن والفقه، فينبغي أن يصح تسميته مهراً ؛ لأن ما أجاز أخذ الأجرة في مقابلتِهِ من المنافع جاز تسميته صداقاً كما قدمنا نقله عن «البدائع». انتهى

اكتفى بذكر الوطء، ولم يذكر الخلوة ؛ لأنه أراد الوطء حقيقة، أو دلالة، ففى الخلوة دلالة الوطء إقامة للداعى مقام المدعو.
وقوله : أو موت ؛ أي موتُ الزَّوج، أو الزوجة.

[١]قوله : اكتفى ؛ دفع دخل مقدر ، تقرير الدخل : أنّ وجوب مهر المثل كما هو عند الوطء والموت كذلك عند الخلوة الصحيحة ؛ لقيامها مقام الوطء في مسائل المهر، فلم لم يذكر المصنف له الخلوة هاهنا كما ذكرها سابقاً، وحاصل الدفع : أنه أراد بالوطء هاهنا أعم من أن يكون حقيقة أو دلالة فاكتفى بذكر الوطء.
وفي رد المحتار (۱ : ۱۰۸) بعد نقل الكلام السابق ذكر: واعترضه المقدسي : بأنه لا ضرورة تلجئ إلى صحة تسميته بل تسمية غيره تغني بخلاف الحاجة إلى تعليم القرآن فإنها تحققت للتكاسل عن الخيرات في هذا الزمان اهـ.
وفيه أن المتأخرين أفتوا بجواز الاستئجار على التعليم للضرورة كما صرحوا به ، ولهذا لم يجز على ما لا ضرورة فيه كالتلاوة ونحوها، ثم الضرورة إنما هي علة لأصل جواز الاستئجار ، ولا يلزم وجودها في كل فرد من أفراده، وحيث جاز على التعليم للضرورة صحت تسميته مهراً ؛ لأنه منفعة تقابل بالمال كسكني الدار، ولم يشترط أحد وجود الضرورة في المسمى، إذ يلزم أن يقال مثله في تسمية السكني مثلا أن تسمية غيرها تغني عنها مع أن الزوجة قد تكون محتاجة إلى التعليم دون السكنى والمال.
واعتراض أيضا في «الشرنبلالية»: بأنه لا يصح تسمية التعليم لأنه خدمة لها وليست من مشترك مصالحها : أي بخلاف رعي غنمها وزراعة أرضها، فإنه وإن كان خدمة لها لكنه من المصالح المشتركة بينه وبينها. وأجاب تلميذه الشيخ عبد الحي بأن الظاهر عدم تسليم كون التعليم خدمة لها ، فليس كل خدمة لا تجوز، وإنما يمتنع لو كانت الخدمة للترذيل. قال الطحطاوي : وهو حسن ؛ لأن معلم القرآن لا يعد خادما للمتعلم شرعاً ولا عرفاً .اهـ. قلت : ويؤيده أنهم لم يجعلوا استئجار الابن أباه لرعي الغنم والزراعة خدمة ، ولو كان رعي الغنم خدمة أو رذيلة لم يفعله نبينا وموسى عليهما الصلاة والسلام بل هو حرفة كباقي الحرف الغير المسترذلة يقصد بها الاكتساب فكذا التعليم لا يسمى خدمة بالأولى.
And joins to it if one mentions what is not suitable as a dower: either due to lack of financial value, like teaching the Quran, or due to lack of preexisting financial value as in mentioning wine and the like, and similarly if one points to what is not suitable as a dower, and it is for gross ignorance, as in the case of mentioning a garment or an animal. In summary, the cases in which something among the mentioned types is named, the naming therein is void, so the mention is made like no mention, and the dower of the like becomes obligatory as in the case of no mention. As for the hadith of al-Bukhari and others: He said to a man: 'Seek, even if it is an iron ring.' He sought but found nothing. He said: 'Do you have anything of the Quran?' He said: 'Yes, such and such a surah.' He said: 'I have given her to you in marriage for what you have of the Quran.' And this is what al-Shafi'i used as evidence that the dower can be other than property. Our companions answered about it: The preposition 'ba' here is not for compensation, but for causation or reason. It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir: When al-Shafi'i permitted taking wages for teaching the Quran, he validated naming it as dower. So we say: The one who gives fatwa with it is obliged to validate naming it as a dower. I have not seen anyone who addressed it. End. In al-Bahr: It will come in the Book of Ijarah that the fatwa is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran and fiqh, so it should be valid to name it as dower, because whatever benefit for which taking wages is permitted, it is permitted to name it as a dower, as we previously quoted from al-Bada'i. End.

He sufficed with mentioning intercourse, and did not mention seclusion, because he intended intercourse literally or figuratively, for in seclusion there is an indication of intercourse, making the caller stand in place of the called.
And his statement: 'or death' i.e., death of the husband or the wife.

[1] His statement: 'sufficed' is a repelling of a presumed objection. The explanation of the objection: The obligation of the dower of the like as it is at intercourse and death, similarly at valid seclusion, because it stands in the place of intercourse in matters of dower. So why did the author not mention seclusion here as he mentioned it previously? The summary of the repelling: He intended by intercourse here to be more general, whether literally or figuratively, so he sufficed with mentioning intercourse.

In Radd al-Muhtar (1:108) after quoting the previous statement: Al-Maqdisi objected: There is no necessity that compels the validity of naming it, rather naming something else suffices, unlike the need for teaching the Quran which was realized due to laziness in good deeds in this time. End.

And in it: The later scholars gave fatwa on the permissibility of hiring for teaching due to necessity, as they stated, and for this reason it is not permitted for what has no necessity like recitation and the like. Then necessity is only a cause for the original permissibility of hiring, and its existence is not required in every individual instance. And since it is permitted for teaching due to necessity, its naming as dower is valid, because it is a benefit that is exchanged for property like dwelling in a house. No one stipulated the existence of necessity in the named thing, for it would be necessary to say the like in naming dwelling, for example, that naming something else suffices while the wife may be in need of teaching without dwelling and property.

Also an objection in al-Sharnablaliyya: It is not valid to name teaching because it is a service to her and not among her common interests, i.e., unlike herding her sheep and farming her land, for although it is a service to her, it is among the common interests between him and her. His student Sheikh Abd al-Hayy answered: The apparent is that teaching is not conceded to be a service to her, for not every service is prohibited; it is only prohibited if the service is for abasement. Al-Tahtawi said: This is good, because the teacher of the Quran is not considered a servant of the student legally or customarily. End. I say: And it is supported by the fact that they did not consider the son hiring his father for herding sheep and farming as a service. If herding sheep were a service or abasement, our Prophet and Moses (peace be upon them) would not have done it; rather it is a profession like other non-abasing professions aimed at earning. So likewise teaching is not called a service, a fortiori.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi commentary (sharh) on the text of al-Wiqaya, addressing the ruling when something unsuitable is mentioned as mahr (dower). The author first states that if something without financial value (like teaching the Quran) or something that lacks preexisting financial value (like wine) is named as mahr, the naming is void and the husband must pay mahr al-mithl (dower of the like). This is because such items cannot be valid consideration in a marriage contract. The discussion then turns to a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ accepted teaching Quran as mahr. Imam al-Shafi'i used this as evidence that mahr can be non-property. The Hanafi scholars respond that the preposition 'ba' in the hadith indicates causation (sababiyya) rather than compensation; i.e., the marriage was for the cause of teaching, not as an exchange. They further note that al-Shafi'i permits taking wages for teaching Quran, so he considers it property. However, the Hanafi school (until later fatwas) generally did not permit hiring for teaching Quran due to the prohibition of taking wages for acts of worship. But later Hanafi scholars, citing necessity, permitted ijara (hiring) for teaching Quran and fiqh, and thus it becomes a valuable benefit. Consequently, naming teaching Quran as mahr becomes valid according to the fatwa, as quoted from al-Bahr and al-Bada'i. The passage then continues with commentary on the author's phrase 'sufficed with mentioning intercourse,' explaining that the author intended intercourse in both literal and figurative senses, thus covering valid khalwa (seclusion) as well. Further objections from al-Maqdisi and al-Sharnablali are addressed: al-Maqdisi argued there is no necessity making teaching Quran valid as mahr, but the response is that later scholars allowed ijara for teaching due to necessity, and the existence of necessity in each case is not required. Al-Sharnablali objected that teaching is a service, but the response is that teaching is not considered a servile act; it is a respectable profession. Thus, teaching Quran can validly be named as mahr under the later fatwa.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of marriage.
الباء (al-ba): The Arabic preposition bi, interpreted here as either compensatory (li al-mu'awad) or causative (li al-sababiyya).
الاستئجار (al-isti'jar): Hiring someone for a service, here specifically for teaching Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi fatwa mentioned in al-Bahr, when does teaching Quran become valid as mahr?
A) In all cases, because it is a benefit.
B) Only when the husband is unable to pay any other dower.
C) When hiring for teaching Quran is permitted due to necessity.
D) Never, because it is not property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school evolved from invalidating teaching Quran as mahr to permitting it via the permissibility of ijara for teaching under necessity.

Nikah — Marriage

Validity of Marriage Without Specifying Dower
Ruling on marriage validity despite dower defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage validity when no dower is specified and explain the obligation of mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A marriage is valid without a dower; the wife receives mahr al-mithl.

In Hanafi marriage law, the dower (mahr) is a right of the wife but not a condition for the validity of the contract. This lesson examines the ruling from al-Mukhtasar that a marriage is valid even when no dower is mentioned or when the dower is invalid. Understanding this principle is crucial for ensuring that marriages are not unjustly invalidated due to omission or defect in the dower term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the marriage contract (nikah). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) even without a dower.
This is the foundational point: dower is not a condition of validity.
2
List the scenarios of defective dower
The text mentions four cases: no dower mentioned, dower denied, dower is non-valuable property, dower is unknown in type or description.
In all these, marriage remains valid.
3
Determine the compensation mechanism
When the dower is not specified or invalid, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the equivalent dower of a woman of her status). If the dower is vaguely described, the average value is due.
Mahr al-mithl is determined by factors like family, beauty, and wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعبارة «المختصر» هذا : وصح النكاح بلا ذكر مهر، ومع نفيه وبشيء غير مال متقوم، وبمجهول جنسه، ويجب مهر المثل، كما مر، أو صفته، فالوسط أو قيمته : أي صح النكاح بمجهول صفته، فيجب الوسط، أو قيمته.
And the expression of al-Mukhtasar is this: 'And the marriage is valid without mentioning a dower, and with its negation, and with something that is not a valuable property, and with an unknown type, and the dower of the like is obligatory, as has passed, or with an unknown description, then the middle [value] or its value.' That is: the marriage is valid with an unknown description of the dower, so the middle [value] or its value becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Mukhtasar and its commentary. It establishes that a marriage contract is valid even if no dower (mahr) is explicitly mentioned, even if the husband denies any dower, even if the dower is specified as something that is not legally considered valuable property (such as wine or pig, which are impure and have no value in Islamic law), and even if the type or description of the dower is unknown (e.g., saying 'a horse' without specifying which horse). In all these cases, the marriage is valid, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of a woman of similar status). When the dower is specified with an unknown description (like a generic type), the obligatory amount is the average value (al-wasat) of that type.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what women of similar status to the wife would receive, considering factors like family, beauty, wealth, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a man marries a woman without specifying any dower?
A) The marriage is invalid.
B) The marriage is valid but no dower is due.
C) The marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory.
D) The marriage is suspended until a dower is agreed.

Key Takeaway
A marriage is valid without a dower; the wife must receive the equivalent dower (mahr al-mithl).

Mut'ah: Obligation, Limits, and Assessment Criteria
Explains when mut'ah is obligatory, its limits, and the assessment method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the single scenario in which mut'ah is wajib, identify its minimum and maximum amounts, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on how to assess the amount.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is obligatory only when divorce occurs before consummation and no valid dower was specified.

Mut'ah is a consolatory gift for a divorced woman in specific circumstances. This lesson clarifies when it becomes obligatory, its limits in value, and the varying opinions within the Hanafi school on how to determine the appropriate amount. Understanding this ruling protects one from sin and ensures justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajib scenario
Read the passage to find the one case where mut'ah is obligatory. Note the conditions: divorce before consummation and absence of a valid dower specification.
The verse 2:236 is cited as proof.
2
Determine the limits of mut'ah
The passage states that mut'ah cannot exceed half of mahr al-mithl nor be less than five dirhams. Understand the reasoning behind each limit.
The limit of half is derived from analogy with specified dower halved upon pre-consummatory divorce.
3
Analyze the assessment dispute
Three opinions are mentioned: al-Sarakhsi (husband's status only), al-Karkhi (wife's status only), al-Khassaf (both). Compare how each applies to a given scenario.
The mufta bihi is al-Khassaf's view, as preferred by later authorities.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a case where husband is rich and wife is poor. Under each opinion, the amount differs. This practical difference shows why the correct opinion matters.
The middle path (al-Khassaf) is considered most equitable.
5
Apply the ruling to a new case
Given a scenario with specific facts, determine whether mut'ah is wajib, its range, and the recommended assessment method.
Use the mufta bihi opinion for fatwa purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومتعة عطف على قوله : مهر مثلها : أي ولزم متعة في الصور المذكورة عند الطلاق قبل الوطء والخلوة. والحاصل : أن في صورة تسمية المهر الصحيحة يجب بالموت وبالوطء دلالة وحقيقة كل المسمى، وعند الطلاق قبل الوطء يجب نصفه. وفي صور عدم التسمية وفسادها، بأن يسمى ما لا يصلح مهراً : الواجب مهر المثل عند الوطء أو الموت، وعند الطلاق قبل الدخول : الواجب المتعة، وعليه حُمِلَ قوله تعالى : «وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتِ مَتَاعٌ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ» (البقرة ٢٤١)، وقوله : «لا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِن طَلَقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ مَا لَمْ تَمَسُّوهُنَّ أَوْ تَعْرِضُوا لَهُنَّ فَرِيضَةً وَمَتُّموهُنَّ عَلَى الْمُوسِعِ قَدَرُهُ وَعَلَى الْمُقْتِرِ قَدَرُهُ» (البقرة ٢٣٦). وبالجملة وجوب المتعة خاص بصورةٍ واحدة، وهي ما إذا طلقها قبل الدخول ولم يسم لها مهراً، أو كانت التسمية فاسدة من كل وجه، وباقي الصور تستحب المتعة فيها إلا في مطلقة قبل الدخول، وقد سمى لها مهراً. وهو بالضم اسم لما تمتع به المرأة وتنشط به حالاً. لا تزيد على نصفه ولا تنقص عن خمسة. وتعتبر بحاله في الصحيح لا تزيد على نصف مهر المثل، ولا تنقص عن خمسة دراهم. وتعتبر بحاله في الصحيح : لقوله تعالى : «عَلَى الْمُوسِعِ قَدَرُهُ وَعَلَى الْمُقْتِرِ قَدَرُهُ». قوله : لا تزيد ; الجملة صفة للمتعة : يعني أنه يشترط في المتعة أن لا تزيد على نصف مهر المثل ; وذلك لأن المسمّى أقوى من مهر المثل ; لوجوبه بالعقد والتسمية، ومهر المثل يجب بالعقد فقط، ولا تجوز الزيادة على نصف المسمى في الطلاق قبل الدخول بنص القرآن في نكاح فيه تسمية، فلأن لا يزاد على نصف مهر المثل الواجب في صورة عدم التسمية أو فسادها أولى. كذا في «الكافي». قوله : ولا تنقص ; لأن المتعة وجبت عوضاً عن البضع، وكل العوض لا يجوز أن يكون أقل من عشرة ; إذ لا مهر أقل منه، فنصفه لا يجوز أن يكون أقل من نصفه، وهو خمسة دراهم. قوله : وتعتبر ; أي تعتبر المتعة بحال الزوج : أي غناه وفقره هذا أحد الأقوال الثلاثة في المسألة ذكره السرخسي وغيره، وصححه في «الهداية». واعتبر الكرخي حالها. واعتبر الخصّاف له حالهما، فإن كانا غنيين فلها الأعلى من الثياب أو فقيرين فالأدنى، أو مختلفين فالوسط، وصحّحه الولوالجي في «فتاواه»، ورجحه ابن الهمام في «الفتح». قوله : على الموسع ; - بضم الميم وكسر السين – : أي الغني، ومقابله المذكور في القرآن المقتر، وهو الفقير أي يجب على الغني مقدار يناسب حاله، وعلى الفقير ما يوافقه.
And mut'ah is a conjunction to his saying 'the dower of her like': meaning that mut'ah becomes obligatory in the mentioned cases upon divorce before intercourse and seclusion. The summary: In the case of a valid dower specification, the entire specified dower is obligated upon death and upon intercourse by dalalah and by haqiqah, and upon divorce before intercourse half of it is obligated. In cases of no specification or invalid specification, such as specifying something not suitable as a dower: the obligatory is mahr al-mithl upon intercourse or death, and upon divorce before consummation the obligatory is mut'ah. Upon this is carried His statement, the Exalted: 'And divorced women shall have a provision in kindness' (2:241), and His statement: 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women while you have not touched them or specified for them an obligation. And provide for them – on the wealthy a sum and on the poor a sum' (2:236). In short, the obligation of mut'ah is specific to one scenario: when he divorces her before consummation and did not specify a dower for her, or the specification was invalid from every aspect. In the remaining scenarios, mut'ah is recommended except for a woman divorced before consummation and he had specified a dower for her. And mut'ah is a noun with a dammah for what a woman is given as a gift and benefits from at the time. It does not exceed half of it and does not fall short of five. And it is considered based on his condition in the correct view: it does not exceed half of mahr al-mithl and does not fall short of five dirhams. And it is considered based on his condition in the correct view: due to His statement, the Exalted: 'On the wealthy a sum and on the poor a sum'. He said: 'It does not exceed' – the sentence is a description of mut'ah: meaning that it is a condition for mut'ah that it does not exceed half of mahr al-mithl; because the specified dower is stronger than mahr al-mithl due to its obligation by contract and specification, whereas mahr al-mithl is obligated by contract only, and increase over half of the specified is not permitted in divorce before consummation by the text of the Quran in a marriage with specification. So it is more appropriate that it should not be increased over half of mahr al-mithl obligated in the case of no specification or its invalidity. Thus in al-Kafi. He said: 'And does not fall short' – because mut'ah is obligated as compensation for the vulva, and every compensation cannot be less than ten, for there is no dower less than that, so its half cannot be less than its half, which is five dirhams. He said: 'And it is considered' – i.e., mut'ah is considered based on the husband's condition: his wealth and poverty. This is one of three opinions on the issue, mentioned by al-Sarakhsi and others, and he corrected it in al-Hidayah. Al-Karkhi considered her condition. Al-Khassaf considered their condition: if both are wealthy, then she gets the highest of garments, if both are poor then the lowest, if different then the middle. Al-Walwaliji corrected this in his Fatawa, and Ibn al-Humam preferred it in al-Fath. He said: 'On the wealthy' – with dammah on the meem and kasrah on the seen: i.e., the rich, and its opposite mentioned in the Quran is 'al-muqtir' which is the poor, meaning that on the rich an amount suitable to his condition is obligatory, and on the poor what suits him.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of mut'ah (a consolatory gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no dower was specified). It first clarifies that mut'ah is obligatory only in one specific scenario: when divorce occurs before consummation and the dower was either not specified at all or the specification was completely invalid (e.g., specifying something not legally considered property). In all other cases, mut'ah is merely recommended (mustahabb). The passage then sets the limits for mut'ah: it cannot exceed half of mahr al-mithl (the dower of the like) and cannot be less than five dirhams. The reasoning is that the specified dower is stronger than mahr al-mithl, so if the specified dower is halved upon pre-consummatory divorce, then mut'ah, which is less than a specified dower, should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl. The minimum of five dirhams is derived from the principle that no dower is less than ten dirhams, so its half is five. The passage also discusses how to determine the amount of mut'ah based on the financial status of the husband (whether wealthy or poor), citing the Quranic verse that the provision is according to the means of the giver. There is a disagreement among Hanafi scholars: al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Hidayah consider only the husband's status; al-Karkhi considers the wife's status; and al-Khassaf considers both, giving the wife the higher or lower according to their combined status. The preferred opinion (mufta bihi) is that of al-Khassaf, as chosen by later scholars like al-Walwaliji and Ibn al-Humam.

Key Terms
متعة (mutʿah): A gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no dower was specified or the specification was invalid.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower that women of similar status to the wife would receive, used as a benchmark when no valid dower is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is mut'ah obligatory according to this passage?
A) Whenever a woman is divorced before consummation.
B) Only when the husband is wealthy.
C) When divorce occurs before consummation and no valid dower was specified.
D) Always when a dower is not paid in full.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is wajib only in the case of pre-consummatory divorce without a valid mahr; its amount is between half of mahr al-mithl and 5 dirhams, and the mufta bihi opinion considers both spouses' financial status for assessment.

intermediate

Amount of Mut'ah and Consideration of Husband's Status
Ruling on the limits of mut'ah and whose financial status is considered

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum and maximum amounts of mut'ah and identify whose financial status is considered according to the Hanafi school, using the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib, capped at half the proper dower and floored at five dirhams, determined by the husband's wealth.

In this lesson, we examine the specific rules governing the amount of mut'ah — the consolatory gift given to a wife divorced before consummation when no dower was specified. The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah establishes two clear boundaries and then enters into an important intra-madhhab discussion about whether to consider the husband's or wife's financial status. You will trace how the Hanafi school uses Quranic proof (2:236) to ground its position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the act is mut'ah (consolatory gift) and that it is wajib in Hanafi law in the specific scenario of divorce before consummation without dower or with invalid dower.
Mut'ah is wajib, not mustahabb as in some other schools.
2
Understand the maximum limit
The mut'ah must not exceed half of the woman's mahr al-mithl (proper dower). Trace the reasoning: if a named dower cannot be exceeded by half in divorce before consummation, then the weaker mahr al-mithl is even more deserving of this cap.
The analogy is based on the strength of the named dower (by contract and naming) versus mahr al-mithl (by contract only).
3
Understand the minimum limit
The mut'ah must not be less than five dirhams. This stems from the minimum mahr being ten dirhams; mut'ah as compensation cannot be less than half of that minimum.
The minimum mahr in Hanafi law is ten dirhams.
4
Identify the three opinions on whose condition is considered
There are three views: (1) the husband's condition (sahih view, mufta bihi), (2) the wife's condition (al-Karkhi), (3) both conditions with gradation (al-Khasaf). The text cites the Quranic verse 'upon the affluent his capacity and upon the straitened his capacity' as proof for the husband's condition.
The Quranic address is to the giver (the husband), which supports considering his capacity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is considering the husband's condition, as authenticated by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and preferred by later authorities like al-Walwaliji and Ibn al-Humam.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا تزيد على نصفه ولا تنقص عن خمسة. وتعتبر بحاله في الصحيح لا تزيد على نصفه ولا تنقص عن خمسة : أي لا تزيد على نصف مهر المثل، ولا تنقص عن خمسة دراهم. وتعتبر بحاله في الصحيح : لقوله تعالى : على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره قوله : لا تزيد ; الجملة صفة للمتعة : يعني أنه يشترط في المتعة أن لا تزيد على نصفه مهر المثل ; وذلك لأن المسمى أقوى من مهر المثل ; لوجوبه بالعقد والتسمية، ومهر المثل يجب بالعقد فقط ، ولا تجوز الزيادة على نصف المسمى في الطلاق قبل الدخول بنص القرآن في نكاح فيه تسمية ، فلأن لا يزاد على نصف مهر المثل الواجب في صورة عدم التسمية أو فسادها أولى. كذا في «الكافي». قوله : ولا تنقص ; لأن المتعة وجبت عوضاً عن البضع، وكل العوض لا يجوز أن يكون أقل من عشرة ; إذ لا مهر أقل منه، فنصفه لا يجوز أن يكون أقل من نصفه، وهو خمسة دراهم. قوله : وتعتبر ; أي تعتبر المتعة بحال الزوج : أي غناه وفقره هذا أحد الأقوال الثلاثة في المسألة ذكره السرخسي وغيره، وصححه في «الهداية». واعتبر الكرخي له حالها. واعتبر الخصاف له حالهما، فإن كانا غنيين فلها الأعلى من الثياب أو فقيرين فالأدنى، أو مختلفين فالوسط ، وصححه الولوالجي في «فتاواه»، ورجحه ابن الهمام في «الفتح» قوله : على الموسع ; - بضم الميم وكسر السين – : أي الغني، ومقابله المذكور في القرآن المقتر، وهو الفقير أي يجب على الغني مقدار يناسب حاله، وعلى الفقير ما يوافقه.
It should not exceed half of it nor fall short of five. And it is considered according to his condition in the correct view. (It should not exceed half of it nor fall short of five): meaning it should not exceed half of the mahr al-mithl (proper dower), nor fall short of five dirhams. (And it is considered according to his condition in the correct view): due to His statement, may He be exalted: 'Upon the affluent his capacity, and upon the straitened his capacity.' (His statement: 'should not exceed': the clause is an adjective for mut'ah: meaning it is stipulated in mut'ah that it should not exceed half of the mahr al-mithl; this is because the named (mahr) is stronger than the mahr al-mithl, being obligatory by both contract and naming, while mahr al-mithl is obligatory by contract alone, and it is not permissible to exceed half of the named mahr in divorce before consummation by the text of the Quran in a marriage with naming, so it is even more fitting that it should not be exceeded over half of the mahr al-mithl which is obligatory in the case of absence of naming or its invalidity. Thus in al-Kafi. (His statement: 'nor fall short': because mut'ah is compensatory for the marital bond, and every compensation is not permissible to be less than ten, since there is no mahr less than it, so its half is not permissible to be less than its half, which is five dirhams. (His statement: 'and it is considered': meaning the mut'ah is considered according to the husband's condition: i.e., his wealth and poverty. This is one of the three opinions in the matter, mentioned by al-Sarakhsi and others, and he authenticated it in al-Hidayah. Al-Karkhi considered it according to her (the wife's) condition. Al-Khasaf considered it according to the condition of both: if both are wealthy, she gets the highest of garments; if both poor, the lowest; if differing, the middle. Al-Walwaliji authenticated it in his Fatawa, and Ibn al-Humam preferred it in al-Fath. (His statement: 'upon the affluent': with damm on the meem and kasr on the seen: i.e., the wealthy; its counterpart mentioned in the Quran is 'the straitened', which is the poor, meaning that upon the wealthy is an amount suitable to his condition, and upon the poor what corresponds to it.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the amount of mut'ah (consolatory gift) due to a woman divorced before consummation when no dower was specified or the specification was invalid. The commentary explains two conditions: first, mut'ah must not exceed half the woman's proper dower (mahr al-mithl), reasoning that since the named dower is stronger and cannot be exceeded by half of the named amount, then half of the mahr al-mithl cannot be exceeded either. Second, mut'ah must not be less than five dirhams, because compensation for marital rights cannot be less than ten dirhams (the minimum mahr), so its half is five. The third part discusses whose financial status is considered: the correct view (as in al-Hidayah) is that it is based on the husband's condition (wealth or poverty), citing the Quranic verse (2:236). Al-Karkhi based it on the wife's condition, and al-Khasaf based it on both, with a middle option if they differ. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the husband's status, as authenticated by al-Marghinani and preferred by later scholars.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given by the husband to his wife upon divorce before consummation when no dower was specified or the specification was invalid.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower for a woman of similar status (age, beauty, family, etc.) in her father's family, used when no dower is specified or the specified dower is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ten dirhams
B) Five dirhams
C) Half a dirham
D) One dirham

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is wajib, bounded between five dirhams and half the proper dower, and the husband's financial condition determines the amount.

Minimum Items of Mut'ah and Regional Variation
Definition of minimum mut'ah and regional adjustment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum components of mut'ah and explain how regional custom can increase this minimum.

Core Idea
The minimum mut'ah is three garments, but local custom may require more.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the minimum items of mut'ah (consolation gift) in a divorce before consummation. It specifies three garments but, through al-Birjandi's commentary, introduces a crucial principle: the minimum is not absolute but tied to local custom. Understanding this helps us apply Hanafi rulings flexibly across different societies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Mut'ah is wajib in certain divorces (e.g., when no mahr was fixed and before intercourse). The passage applies to that context.
The phrase 'بطلاق قبل الوطء والخلوة' indicates the condition.
2
List the three minimum items
The text explicitly names dir' (shift), khimar (headcover), and milhafah (wrap). Memorise these as the baseline.
These are the absolute minimum according to the report from Ibn Abbas.
3
Understand the regional exception
Al-Birjandi states that in lands where women wear more than three garments, the mut'ah must include additional items like izar and ka'b to match local custom.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle of considering 'urf (custom) in financial obligations.
4
Apply to a scenario
If a woman in a cold region typically wears four layers, the mut'ah should include at least those four. The mufti must ascertain local practice.
The minimum is floor, not ceiling; 'urf can raise it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي درع، وخمار، ومِلْحَفة بطلاق قبل الوطء والخلوة : أي في الصور المذكورة، وهي قوله بلا ذكر المهر إلى آخره. قوله : درع ; الدرع : - بالكسر - قميص المرأة. والخمار - بالكسر - ما تُغطي به رأسها. والملحفة : - بكسر الميم وفتح الحاء بينهما لام ساكنة - : ما تلتحف به المرأة من قرنها إلى قدمها. وهذا أدنى المتعة، وهو مروي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه أخرجه البيهقي، قال البرجندي : قالوا : هذا في ديارهم ، أما في ديارنا فيجب أكثر من ذلك ; لأن النساء في ديارنا تلبس أكثر من ثلاثة أثواب، فيزاد على ذلك إزار وكعب.
It is a shift, a headcover, and a wrap in divorce before intercourse and seclusion: i.e., in the mentioned cases, namely his statement 'without mention of the dower' etc. His statement: 'shift'; the shift: with kasra (i.e., the vowel i) – the woman's chemise. And the headcover: with kasra – that which she covers her head with. And the wrap: with kasr of the meem and fatha of the haa, with a silent laam between them – that which the woman wraps herself with from her head to her feet. This is the minimum of mut'ah, and it is reported from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, recorded by al-Bayhaqi. Al-Birjandi said: They said: This is in their lands; but in our lands, more than that is obligatory because women in our lands wear more than three garments, so a waist-wrapper and a pair of socks are added.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage defines the minimum items of mut'ah as three specific garments: a dir' (a shift or chemise), a khimar (head covering), and a milhafah (a large wrap covering head to feet). This is the minimum and is narrated from Ibn Abbas. However, the commentator al-Birjandi notes that this depends on regional custom: if women in a given region typically wear more than three garments, the mut'ah must be increased accordingly, adding for example an izar (waist-wrapper) and ka'b (socks) to meet the local standard. Thus, the minimum is not absolute but relative to what is considered adequate clothing for the woman in her society.

Key Terms
درع (dir'): A woman's chemise or shift, an undergarment covering the upper body.
خمار (khimar): A head covering that women drape over their heads, also known as a scarf.
ملحفة (milhafah): A large outer wrap that covers the woman from head to feet, like a cloak or sheet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Three garments: dir', khimar, milhafah; may increase if local custom requires more
C) Half the mahr al-mithl; always fixed
D) A shift and a headcover only

Key Takeaway
The minimum mut'ah is three garments, but it must be adjusted upward to match regional custom, demonstrating the Hanafi integration of 'urf.

Stipulating the Husband's Service as Dower: Free vs. Slave
Ruling on validity of service as dower: free vs. slave husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating a free husband's service as dower (invalid) and a slave husband's service (valid with permission), and explain the proof from Quran 4:34.

Core Idea
A free husband's service cannot be dower because it reverses the divinely ordained marital hierarchy; a slave's service can be dower because his labor is owned.

In this lesson, we examine a specific but instructive case: a man marries a woman and stipulates that he will serve her, e.g., for a year, as the entire dower. Is this valid? The Hanafi answer depends on whether the husband is free or a slave. We will explore the rule, the Quranic proof, and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for a free husband
The dower specification (tasmiyyah) is fasid (invalid) regardless of the wife's status; she is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
The marriage contract itself remains valid.
2
State the ruling for a slave husband
The service specification is sahih (valid) as dower, but only if the slave has his master's permission; without it, the contract is invalid.
The slave's service is considered property (mal) because his person is owned.
3
Identify the dalil
The proof is Quran 4:34: 'Men are in charge over women.'
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah, allowing interpretation.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse establishes that men are qawwamun (managers/protectors) over women, implying that the wife is the one who serves or is under authority. Stipulating the husband's service reverses this order, so it is prohibited.
This reasoning applies only to free men; slaves are not qawwamun.
5
Understand the distinction
Marriage is a contract seeking financial benefit (al-ibtigha' bil-mal). A free man's service is not property; a slave's service is property because his person is owned. Hence the different rulings.
The principle of qawama overrides general permissibility of conditions for free husbands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : في خدمة ; يعني إذا تزوج على أن يخدم الزوج لها مقداراً معلوماً كسنة مثلاً فإن كان الزوج حراً ، فالتسمية فاسدة سواء كانت الزوجة أمة أو حرّة، والواجب مهر المثل كما مر ; لأن خدمة الزوج لها واستخدامه حرام; لكونه قلباً للموضوع، فإن وضع النكاح أن تكون الزوجة خادمة كما يدل عليه قوله تعالى : الرجال قوامون على النساء [النساء:34] وإن كان الزوج عبد وجبت هي : أي الخدمة، ويشترط فيه أن يكون العبد مأذوناً من مولاه بالتزوج على هذا، فإنه إن لم يأذن له مولاه لم يصح العقد. ووجه الفرق : أن الشرط في النكاح : هو الابتغاء بالمال، وخدمة الحر ليست كذلك لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، وخدمة العبد ابتغاء بالمال لتضمن تسليم رقبته.
His statement: 'with service'; meaning if he marries on the condition that the husband serves her for a known amount, e.g., a year, then if the husband is free, the specification is invalid whether the wife is a slave or free, and the obligatory (dower) is the proper dower (mahr al-mithl), as previously mentioned; because the husband's serving her and his being used (by her) is prohibited, as it is a reversal of the matter, for the disposition of marriage is that the wife is the servant, as indicated by His statement: 'Men are in charge over women' [4:34]. And if the husband is a slave, the service is valid, with the condition that the slave is permitted by his master to marry on this basis; if his master does not permit him, the contract is not valid. The point of distinction is that the condition in marriage is the seeking of wealth (al-ibtigha' bil-mal), and the service of a free man is not so, neither in reality nor in legal effect, while the service of a slave is considered seeking of wealth because it involves the surrender of his person (for the benefit of the master?).
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage rules on the validity of stipulating the husband's service to the wife as the dower. For a free husband, such a stipulation is invalid (fasid) regardless of whether the wife is free or a slave, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl instead. The reasoning is that it reverses the natural order of marriage, where the wife is the one who serves or is under the husband's authority, as per Quran 4:34. For a slave husband, however, the stipulation is valid and the service becomes the dower, provided the slave has his master's permission to marry on that basis. The difference is that marriage is a contract seeking financial benefit (al-ibtigha' bil-mal); a free man's service is not considered property, but a slave's service is because his person is owned.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): Service; here it refers to the husband performing labor for the wife as a condition of the dower.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower; when the specified dower is invalid, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because service is difficult to quantify
B) Because it reverses the natural order of marriage as established in the Quran
C) Because free men cannot be hired
D) Because the wife must serve the husband

Key Takeaway
A free husband's service cannot be dower because it contradicts the qawama principle; a slave's service can be dower because it is property.

Minimum Mut'ah: Garments for a Divorced Woman Before Consummation
Defines minimum obligatory mut'ah for mufawwidah divorced before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum mut'ah gifts for a mufawwidah divorced before consummation and explain how custom affects the amount.

Core Idea
Mut'ah for a divorced mufawwidah requires at least a chemise, headcover, and wrap, but custom may demand more.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the matn of al-Wiqayah on the minimum compensation (mut'ah) owed to a woman whose marriage ended before consummation without a specified dower. The text provides a concrete list of garments based on a prophetic practice, but the commentary by al-Birjandi introduces an important principle: the minimum is not absolute; it adjusts to local custom. You will learn both the rule and its flexible application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Determine the situation that obligates mut'ah: a woman married without a specified mahr (mufawwidah) and divorced before consummation and valid seclusion.
If the mahr was specified, half of it is due instead of mut'ah.
2
List the minimum items
The text specifies three garments as the minimum: dir' (chemise), khimar (headcover), and milhafah (wrap).
These are the basic coverings for a woman.
3
Note the dalil
The minimum is supported by a narration from Ibn Abbas (ra) recorded by al-Bayhaqi, indicating the Prophet (saw) gave these three garments as mut'ah.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni evidence.
4
Apply the expansion
Al-Birjandi explains that this minimum applies to the Arabian context; in other lands where women wear more garments, additional items (e.g., izār and ka'b) become obligatory.
The principle is that mut'ah should be sufficient to console the woman according to local custom.
5
Derive the principle
The ruling shows that 'urf (custom) plays a role in determining the scope of a wajib obligation in Hanafi fiqh.
This flexibility preserves the objective of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي درع، وخمار، ومِلْحَفة بطلاق قبل الوطء والخلوة. وهذا أدنى المتعة، وهو مروي عن ابن عباس له أخرجه البيهقي، قال البِرْجَندِيُّ : قالوا : هذا في ديارهم ، أما في ديارنا فيجب أكثر من ذلك ؛ لأنّ النِّساء في ديارنا تلبس أكثر من ثلاثة أثواب، فيزادُ على ذلك إزار وكعب.
And it is (i.e., the minimum mut'ah) a chemise, a headcover, and a wrap by divorce before intercourse and seclusion. And this is the lowest of mut'ah, and it is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) recorded by al-Bayhaqi. Al-Birjandi said: They said: This is in their lands. As for our lands, more than that is obligatory because women in our lands wear more than three garments, so an izār (waist-wrapper) and a ka'b (ankle-covering?) are added.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn, expanded by the commentary. It specifies the minimum obligatory mut'ah for a mufawwidah (woman married without specified mahr) who is divorced before consummation and valid seclusion. The minimum is three garments: a dir' (chemise), a khimār (headcover), and a milḥafah (large wrap covering from head to feet). This minimum is based on a narration from Ibn Abbas (ra) reported by al-Bayhaqi, indicating it is a sunnah-based minimum. Al-Birjandi notes that this minimum applies to women in the Arabian context; in other lands where women typically wear more garments, the mut'ah should be increased to include additional items like an izār and ka'b. This is because the purpose of mut'ah is to console the woman and remove the distress of separation, which is better achieved by providing what is customary. The commentary thus adapts the ruling to different cultural contexts while preserving the underlying principle.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A gift or compensation given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified, to console her.
درع (dir'): A woman's chemise or shift that covers the upper body.
خمار (khimar): A head covering worn by women to cover the hair and neck.
ملحفة (milhafah): A large wrap or cloak used by women to cover from head to feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage
