The Ruling on Stipulating Husband's Service in Marriage
Distinguishes free vs slave husband regarding service condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating the husband's service in the marriage contract, distinguish between free and slave husband, and apply the underlying principle of mal (property).

Core Idea
A free husband's personal service is not mal; a slave's service is mal because it entails his person.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains a nuanced rule in Hanafi nikah: if a husband agrees to serve his wife for a specified period, the validity depends on his status. The key is whether the service constitutes property (mal). Let's see how the text unpacks this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between a free husband and a slave husband who stipulates to serve his wife for a known period (e.g., one year).
The condition is the same in both cases, but the ruling differs.
2
State the ruling for a free husband
For a free husband, the condition is fasid (corrupt), and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (equitable dower), not the specified service.
This applies whether the wife is free or a slave.
3
State the ruling for a slave husband
For a slave husband, the condition is valid and the service becomes obligatory, provided the slave has permission (idhn) from his master to marry on that condition.
If the master does not permit, the contract is invalid.
4
Understand the proof
The distinction is based on whether the service is considered mal (property). A free man's service is not mal in reality or by legal effect; a slave's service is mal because it entails delivery of his person (raqabah). Additionally, the Quranic verse (4:34) indicates men are caretakers, implying the wife is normally the server.
The condition in marriage must involve seeking property (ibtighā' bi al-māl).
5
Note exceptions
The passage mentions that other non-monetary conditions like providing housing, riding animals, or cultivating land are valid because they involve benefits of specific property (manafi' al-a'yān) which are considered mal or assimilated to it due to need.
The invalidity is specific to personal service of a free husband.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : في خدمة ؛ يعني إذا تزوج على أن يخدم الزوج لها مقداراً معلوماً كسنة مثلاً فإن كان الزوج حراً ، فالتسمية فاسدة سواء كانت الزوجة أمة أو حرّة، والواجب مهر المثل كما مر ؛ لأن خدمة الزوج لها واستخدامه حرام؛ لكونه قلباً للموضوع، فإن وضع النكاح أن تكون الزوجة خادمة كما يدلُّ عليه قوله : الرِّجَالُ قَوَّامُونَ عَلَى النِّسَاءِ وإن كان الزوج عبد تجب هي : أي الخدمة، ويشترط فيه أن يكون العبد مأذوناً من مولاه بالتزوج على هذا، فإنه إن لم يأذن له مولاه لم يصح العقد. ووجه الفرق : أن الشرط في النكاح : هو الابتغاء بالمال، وخدمة الحر ليست كذلك لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، وخدمة العبد ابتغاء بالمال لتضمن تسليم رقبته، وذكر في البدائع وغيره : إنه لو تزوج الحرُّ على سكنى داره، أو ركوب دابته ، أو الحمل عليها ، أو على أن تزرع أرضه، ونحو ذلك من منافع الأعيان مدة معلومة صحت التسمية ؛ لأن هذه المنافع مال، أو أُلْحِقَتْ به للحاجة.
His saying: 'in service' means if he marries on the condition that the husband serves her for a known amount such as a year, then if the husband is free, the specification (of such a condition) is corrupt, whether the wife is a slave or free, and the obligatory is mahr al-mithl as has passed; because the service of the husband to her and his utilizing her is haram, as it is an inversion of the matter, for the nature of marriage is that the wife is the servant as indicated by His saying: 'Men are caretakers of women.' And if the husband is a slave, it (service) is obligatory, and it is required that the slave be authorized by his master to marry on this condition; for if his master did not permit him, the contract is not valid. And the explanation of the difference is that the condition in marriage is the seeking of property (mal), and the service of a free man is not that, neither in reality nor in legal effect, whereas the service of a slave is seeking property because it entails delivery of his person. And it is mentioned in al-Bada'i' and elsewhere that if a free man marries on condition of living in his house, or riding his animal, or carrying on it, or that she cultivates his land, and similar benefits of specific property for a known period, the specification is valid because these benefits are property or are attached to it due to need.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase 'in service' (fi khidmah). It discusses a condition in the marriage contract whereby the husband agrees to serve the wife for a specified period (e.g., one year). The ruling distinguishes between a free husband and a slave husband. For a free husband, the condition is invalid (fasid) and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (equitable dower) instead of the specified service. The reason is that service of a free man is not considered property (mal); moreover, it reverses the natural order of marriage, as indicated by the Qur'anic verse that men are caretakers (qawwamun) over women, implying that the wife is normally the one who serves. For a slave husband, however, the condition is valid and the service becomes obligatory, provided the slave is authorized (ma'dhun) by his master to marry on such terms. The rationale is that the service of a slave effectively involves the delivery of his person, which is a form of property (since a slave is owned). The commentary also notes an exception from al-Bada'i' and other sources: if a free man marries on condition of providing specific benefits like lodging, riding, or agricultural use of his land for a known duration, that condition is valid because those are recognized forms of property or are assimilated to property due to necessity. Thus, the invalidity is specific to personal service of a free husband, not to all non-monetary conditions.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): Personal service rendered by the husband to the wife, as opposed to providing property or specific benefits.
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in a specific transaction, here to marry on condition of service.
ابتغاء بالمال (ibtighā' bi al-māl): The seeking or exchange of property, which is the proper subject of a condition in marriage according to Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key principle that determines whether a condition in a marriage contract is valid in Hanafi law, according to this passage?
A) The condition must be mutual and agreed upon.
B) The condition must involve property (mal) or be assimilated to property.
C) The condition must be permitted by the wife's guardian.
D) The condition must be for a limited duration.

Key Takeaway
A free husband's personal service cannot be a valid condition in marriage because it is not considered property, whereas a slave's service is valid due to his status as owned property.

The Mufawwidah's Entitlement and the Dispute on Half of Later-Agreed Mahr
Commentary on the matn's ruling for mufawwidah with dispute on half of later-agreed mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the entitlements of a mufawwidah in three scenarios (consummation, death, divorce before consummation) and explain why Abu Hanifa holds she receives only mut'ah, not half of any later-agreed mahr, citing the principle that mahr al-mithl is not halved.

Core Idea
For a mufawwidah divorced before consummation, the later-agreed mahr does not halve; she receives only mut'ah, because the underlying obligation is mahr al-mithl.

This passage defines the mufawwidah and clarifies her entitlements. It then presents a key intra-madhhab dispute: if the couple later agrees on a specific mahr and divorces before consummation, does she get half? The commentary defends Abu Hanifa's view that only mut'ah is due, based on the nature of mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufawwidah and her rulings
First, understand who a mufawwidah is: a woman who marries without specifying a mahr. The primary ruling: she receives mahr al-mithl upon consummation or death of the husband; if divorced before consummation, she receives mut'ah (consolation gift).
The passage also notes that the matn's phrase 'or if he dies' should be read as 'or if one of them dies' because the ruling is symmetrical.
2
Pinpoint the dispute
The dispute arises when the couple later agrees on a specific mahr and then divorces before consummation. Abu Yusuf (and al-Shafi'i) argue that she gets half of that agreed amount, analogizing it to a mahr specified at the time of the contract.
Abu Yusuf's view is based on qiyas: just as a specified mahr is halved, so is a later-agreed mahr.
3
Trace Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa argues that the real obligation from the contract is mahr al-mithl. The later agreement merely determines that mahr al-mithl; it does not create a new mahr. Since mahr al-mithl is not halved upon divorce before consummation, the later-agreed amount cannot be halved either.
This is a clear qiyas jaliy: the effective cause is that the obligation is not a fixed sum at contract.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, the wife receives a set of garments (mut'ah), which is minimal. Under Abu Yusuf's view, she would receive half of the agreed amount, which could be substantial. The Hanafi school adopts Abu Hanifa's position as mufta bihi.
This ikhtilaf highlights how a difference in usul (classification of the later agreement) leads to different outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمفوضة بكسر الواو ما فُرِضَ لها إن وُطِئت، أو مات عنها، والمتعة إن طلّقت قبل الوطء. قوله : وللمفوضة ؛ هو إما على وزن اسم الفاعل من التفويض : أي التي فوَّضَت نفسها بلا مهر، وإما على وزن اسم المفعول : أي التي فوضها دليلها إلى زوجها بلا مهر. قوله : ما فُرض ؛ بصيغة المجهول أو المعلوم، والضمير إلى الزوج، والمراد به ما تراضيا عليه بعد العقد. قوله : أو مات عنها ؛ لو قال : «أو مات أحدهما» لكان أولى، فإن حكم موتها كحكم موته. كذا في «التبيين». قوله : لها نصف المفروض ؛ أي للمفوضة في صورة الطلاق قبل الوطء نصف الذي تراضيا عليه بعد العقد ؛ لأنّ المفروض بعده كالمسمى عنده ، فكما يتنصفُ المسمى عند الطلاق قبل الوطء، كذلك المفروض. ولنا : إن الواجب في مثل هذه الصورة بالعقدِ هو مهر المثل ؛ ولهذا يجب هو عند الموت والوطء إن لم يفرض شيء، فالمفروض بعد العقدِ قائم مقامه، ومن المعلوم أن مهر المثل لا يتنصف شرعاً ، فكذا ما ينوب منابه.
And for the mufawwidah (with kasra on the waw) is what was prescribed (as mahr) for her if she was consummated, or if he dies from her, and the mut'ah if she is divorced before intercourse. His saying: 'for the mufawwidah': it is either on the pattern of the active participle from tafwid — i.e., she who delegated herself without mahr, or on the pattern of the passive participle: i.e., she whose guardian delegated her to her husband without mahr. His saying: 'what was prescribed' (ma furida): either in the passive or active voice, and the pronoun refers to the husband, and what is meant is what they mutually agree upon after the contract. His saying: 'or if he dies from her': it would have been better to say 'or if one of them dies' because the ruling of her death is like the ruling of his death. Thus in al-Tabyin. His saying: 'for her is half of the prescribed': i.e., for the mufawwidah in the case of divorce before intercourse, half of what they mutually agreed upon after the contract; because the prescribed after it is like the specified at him (Abu Yusuf), so just as the specified (mahr) is halved at divorce before intercourse, so is the prescribed. And for us (Abu Hanifa): The obligation in such a case by the contract is mahr al-mithl; for this reason it is obligatory at death and intercourse if nothing was prescribed, so the prescribed after the contract stands in its place, and it is known that mahr al-mithl is not halved legally, so likewise what acts in its stead.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling for the mufawwidah. It first defines the term: a mufawwidah is a woman who marries without specifying a mahr, either by delegating herself (active sense) or by being delegated by her guardian (passive sense). The ruling: she gets the mahr that is later agreed upon if consummation or death of the husband occurs; if divorced before consummation, she gets only mut'ah, not the agreed amount. The commentary then addresses a significant intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab dispute. Abu Yusuf (and also al-Shafi'i) hold that if the couple later agrees on a specific mahr and then divorces before consummation, she is entitled to half of that agreed amount, analogizing it to the case where the mahr was specified at the time of the contract. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that she gets only mut'ah, because the true obligation arising from the contract is mahr al-mithl (equitable dower), and the later agreement merely determines that, not a new mahr. Since mahr al-mithl is not halved upon divorce before consummation (as it is not a specified sum), the later agreement cannot create a half right. The commentary from al-Tabyin also notes a textual point: the matn says 'or he dies from her' but it should include 'or she dies' because the ruling is symmetrical. Thus, the lesson clarifies the correct Hanafi ruling and the rationale behind it.

Key Terms
مفوضة (mufawwidah): A woman who marries without specifying a mahr in the contract, either by her own delegation or by her guardian's delegation.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable dower determined by considering the dower of similar women (by family, status, etc.), owed when no specific mahr was mentioned.
متعة (mut'ah): A consolation gift given to the mufawwidah upon divorce before consummation, consisting of a minimum of three garments, adjusted by custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what does a mufawwidah receive if she is divorced before consummation after the couple agreed on a specific mahr?
A) Half of the agreed mahr
B) The full agreed mahr
C) Only mut'ah (minimum garments)
D) Mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
For a mufawwidah, the underlying obligation is mahr al-mithl; any later agreement determines it but does not create a new mahr subject to half.

The Mufawwidah's Dower: Half or Gift? An Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Defines mufawwidah and dispute over half-dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the mufawwidah's entitlement upon pre-consummation divorce, distinguish the opposing view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, and apply the Hanafi rebuttal to the qiyas argument.

Core Idea
The mufawwidah's agreed dower substitutes for mahr al-mithl, which never halves — so she gets only mut'ah, not half.

This lesson examines a key scenario in marriage contracts: what happens when a woman is married without specifying a dower (mufawwidah), the couple later agrees on an amount, but then divorce occurs before consummation? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, holds that she does not get half of that agreed amount — only a consolation gift (mut'ah). Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i disagree, drawing an analogy to a specified dower. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and shows why the Hanafi view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Define the Mufawwidah
Identify who is considered mufawwidah: a woman married without mentioning the dower, or on condition of no dower, who later agrees on an amount.
Mufawwidah is from tafwid (delegation) — she delegated the dower.
2
State the Normal Entitlements
If consummated or husband dies, she receives the full agreed dower. If divorced before consummation, she receives only a gift (mut'ah) according to Hanafi.
The agreed dower stands in for mahr al-mithl.
3
Present the Opposing View
Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue that the post-contract agreement is like a specified dower (musamma), so it should be halved in pre-consummation divorce.
They use qiyas to a standard specified dower.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the agreed dower substitutes for mahr al-mithl, which is not halved by law. Therefore, the analogy fails, and only mut'ah is due.
Mahr al-mithl is the default obligation from the contract itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمفوضة بكسر الواو ما فُرِضَ لها إن وُطِئت، أو مات عنها، والمتعة إن طلقت قبل الوطء. والمفوضة هي التي نكحت بلا ذِكْرِ المهر، أو على أن لا مَهْرَ لها، ثُمَّ إن تراضيا على مقدار، فلها ذلك المفروض إِن وَطِئَها، أو مات عنها، والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الوطء. وعند أبي يوسف الله، وهو قولُ الشَّافِعِي لها نصف المفروض. «البدائع» وغيره: إنه لو تزوجها الحرُّ على سكنى داره، أو ركوب دابته، أو الحمل عليها، أو على أن تزرع أرضه، ونحو ذلك من منافع الأعيان مدة معلومة صحت التسمية؛ لأن هذه المنافع مال، أو أُلْحِقَتْ به للحاجة. قوله: وللمفوضة؛ هو إما على وزن اسم الفاعل من التفويض: أي التي فوَّضَت نفسها بلا مهر، وإما على وزن اسم المفعول: أي التي فوضها دليلها إلى زوجها بلا مهر. قوله: ما فُرض؛ بصيغة المجهول أو المعلوم، والضمير إلى الزوج، والمراد به ما تراضيا عليه بعد العقد. قوله: أو مات عنها؛ لو قال: «أو مات أحدهما» لكان أولى، فإن حكم موتها كحكم موته. كذا في «التبيين». قوله: لها نصف المفروض؛ أي للمفوضة في صورة الطلاق قبل الوطء نصف الذي تراضيا عليه بعد العقد؛ لأنّ المفروض بعده كالمسمى عنده، فكما يتنصفُ المسمى عند الطلاق قبل الوطء، كذلك المفروض. ولنا: إن الواجب في مثل هذه الصورة بالعقدِ هو مهر المثل؛ ولهذا يجب هو عند الموت والوطء إن لم يفرض شيء، فالمفروض بعد العقدِ قائم مقامه، ومن المعلوم أن مهر المثل لا يتنصف شرعاً، فكذا ما ينوب منابه.
And for the mufawwidah (with kasra on the waw) is what was prescribed for her if she is consummated, or if he dies, and a gift if she is divorced before consummation. The mufawwidah is the one who married without mentioning the dower, or on condition that there is no dower for her, then if they mutually agree on an amount, she has that prescribed amount if he consummated with her, or if he dies, and a gift if he divorces her before consummation. According to Abu Yusuf, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i, she has half of the prescribed amount. Al-Bada'i' and others: If a free man married her on condition of residing in his house, or riding his animal, or carrying on it, or that she plant his land, and similar benefits of properties for a known period, the specification is valid because these benefits are property or are attached to it due to need. His saying: 'And for the mufawwidah' – it is either on the pattern of the active participle from al-tafwid (delegation), meaning she who delegated herself without dower, or on the pattern of the passive participle, meaning she whose guardian delegated her to her husband without dower. His saying: 'what was prescribed' – in the passive or active voice, and the pronoun refers to the husband, and what is meant is what they mutually agree upon after the contract. His saying: 'or if he dies on her' – if he had said 'or if one of them dies' it would have been better, for the ruling of her death is like the ruling of his death. So in al-Tabyin. His saying: 'she has half of the prescribed' – meaning for the mufawwidah in the case of divorce before consummation, half of what they mutually agreed upon after the contract, because the prescribed after it is like the named in his view, so just as the named is halved at divorce before consummation, so too the prescribed. And our proof: the obligatory in such a case by the contract is the mahr al-mithl (dower of the like); therefore it is obligatory at death and consummation if nothing was prescribed. So what is prescribed after the contract stands in its place, and it is known that mahr al-mithl is not halved by law, so likewise what takes its place.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines the mufawwidah and outlines her rights. The mufawwidah is a woman married without specifying a dower at the time of the contract. If they later agree on a dower, she receives that agreed amount if the marriage is consummated or if the husband dies. If she is divorced before consummation, she receives only a ‘gift’ (mut‘ah), not half of the agreed dower. The passage then presents a disagreement: Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi‘i hold that she is entitled to half of the agreed dower, analogizing it to a specified dower (al-musamma) which is halved in pre-consummation divorce. The Hanafi position rebuts this by stating that the obligation at the time of contract is the mahr al-mithl, which is not halved by shari‘a; the post-contract agreement merely substitutes for the mahr al-mithl, so it also cannot be halved. The Hanafi stance is thus that the mufawwidah does not get half the agreed dower if divorced before consummation, but only the mut‘ah. The passage also clarifies that benefits of properties (like residence or riding) can be validly specified as dower, as they are considered wealth or analogous to it.

Key Terms
المفوضة (al-mufawwidah): A woman married without specifying a dower, or on condition of no dower, who later agrees on an amount with the husband.
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no dower was specified, as compensation.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to her in status, which is the default obligation when no dower is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The full dower agreed upon after the contract
C) A gift (mut'ah) only
D) Nothing at all

Key Takeaway
The mufawwidah's post-contract dower agreement substitutes for non-halvable mahr al-mithl, so she does not receive half upon pre-consummation divorce—only mut'ah.

Increase of Mahr After Contract
Ruling on increase of mahr with conditions and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increases to the dower made after the contract, explain why it is wajib, and apply the rule that such increases do not halve upon pre-consummation divorce.

Core Idea
Post-contract dower increases bind the husband fully and are not halved in pre-consummation divorce.

This lesson examines a specific Hanafi ruling on dower (mahr) increases made after the marriage contract. The passage establishes that any increase agreed upon after the contract is obligatory (wajib) on the husband, provided the wife accepts it in the same session. A key practical implication is that in case of divorce before consummation, only the originally prescribed dower is halved; the increase remains fully due. This ruling is supported by Quran and distinguishes the Hanafi position from internal disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the statement that an increase upon the dower is obligatory. Note that this is a post-contract act, not part of the original dower.
The text says 'وما زيد على المهر يجب' – 'And whatever is increased upon the dower is obligatory.'
2
List the conditions for obligation
The passage specifies conditions: the wife's acceptance in the council, knowledge of the increase amount, and the marriage continuing at the time of increase. Identify each.
Conditions: qabul al-zawja fi al-majlis, ma'rifat qadr al-ziyada, baqa' al-zawjiyya.
3
Analyze the proof from Quran
The text cites Quran 4:24 'in whatever you mutually agree after the prescribed obligation'. Explain how this verse establishes the obligation of the increase.
The verse is general; the Hanafi interpretation is that mutual agreement after the contract creates a binding obligation.
4
Examine the halving issue
Understand the rule: if divorce occurs before consummation, only the original dower (alfarida) is halved. The increase is not halved; it drops entirely.
The passage contrasts with Abu Yusuf's first opinion. The proof is Quran 2:237, where 'prescribed' is interpreted as the dower at contract.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreements
Identify Zufar's disagreement on the obligation itself and Abu Yusuf's initial view on halving. Understand why the relied-upon position rejects these.
The text calls Zufar's view 'no face' and rejects Abu Yusuf's first saying using the Quranic proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زيد على المهر يجب، ويسقط بالطلاق قبل الوطء، وصح حطها عنه. أي حطّ المرأة عن الزوج. قوله: زيد على المهر: أي المسمى عن العقد، ولو كان بلا شهود أو بعد هبة المهر والإبراء منه سواء كان من جنس المهر أو غير جنسه، وسواء كانت الزيادة من الزوج أو وليه، فقد صرحوا بأن الأب والجد لو زوج ابنَه ثم زاد في المهر صح. كذا في «النهر» و«البحر». ولا يشترط لفظ: الزيادة، بل تصح بلفظها، وبقوله: راجعتك بكذا إن قبلت، كذا في «أنفع الوسائل»، وذكر في «الخانية»: إنه لو وهبته مهرها، ثم أقر بكذا وقبلت صح، ويحمل على الزيادة. قوله: يجب؛ أي على الزوج لكن بشرط قبول الزوجة في المجلس أو ولي الصغيرة، ومعرفته قدر الزيادة، وبقاء الزوجية حين الزيادة. وكذا في «النهر»، وفي وجوب الزيادة خلاف زفر، ولا وجه له، ويدلُّ على قولنا قوله تعالى: فيما تراضيتم بِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ الْفَرِيضَةِ. قوله: بالطلاق؛ يعني إذا طلق قبل الوطء يجب نصف الأصل فقط ولا يتنصفُ الزائد، وفيه خلافُ أبي يوسف الله في قوله الأول، وحجتنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في سورة الطلاق قبل الدخول: فَيَصفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ، فإنَّ الظاهر أن الفرض محمول على الفرض المعتاد، وهو الفرضُ عند العقد فلا يتنصفُ ما زيد عليه بعده. قوله: حطها؛ - بالفتح وتشديد الطاء - بمعنى الإسقاط: يعني إذا أسقطت المرأة المهر عن الزوج بعد العقد صح ذلك، وسقط ذلك القدر المحطوط، وإن كان كل المهر عن ذمته؛ لقوله تعالى: فَإِن طِبْنَ لَكُمْ عَن شَيْءٍ مِنْهُ نَفْسًا فَكُلُوهُ هَنِتَا قَرِينَا ويرتد الحط وكذا الإبراء برد الزوج، كما في «القُنية» و«البحر».
And whatever is increased upon the dower is obligatory, and drops with divorce before consummation, and her remission of it is valid. That is the woman's remission from the husband. His saying: 'increased upon the dower' i.e. upon the named at the contract, even if without witnesses or after gifting the dower and discharging it, whether it is of the same type as the dower or another type, and whether the increase is from the husband or his guardian, for they have stated that if the father or grandfather married off his son and then increased the dower, it is valid. So in al-Nahr and al-Bahr. And the word 'increase' is not stipulated; rather it is valid with its wording, and with his saying: 'I return to you for such-and-such if you accept', so in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. And it is mentioned in al-Khaniyya: if she gifted him her dower, then he admitted to such-and-such and she accepted, it is valid, and it is interpreted as an increase. His saying: 'is obligatory' i.e. upon the husband but on condition of the wife's acceptance in the session or the guardian of the minor, and his knowledge of the amount of increase, and the marriage continuing at the time of increase. So in al-Nahr. And there is a disagreement of Zufar regarding the obligation of the increase, but it has no basis, and our saying is supported by His saying: 'In whatever you mutually agree after the prescribed obligation' (Quran 4:24). His saying: 'with divorce' means if he divorces before consummation, only half of the original is obligatory and the increase is not halved. And there is a disagreement of Abu Yusuf in his first saying. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the divorce before consummation: 'You shall give half of what you prescribed' (Quran 2:237), for evidently 'prescribed' is understood as the usual prescribed at the contract, so what is increased after it is not halved. His saying: 'her remission' - with fatha and tashdid on the taa - meaning cancellation: i.e. if the woman drops the dower from the husband after the contract, that is valid, and that dropped amount falls, even if it is all the dower from his liability, due to His saying: 'But if they willingly give up of it something, then consume it wholesome and palatable' (Quran 4:4). And the remission and likewise the discharge are revoked by the husband's refusal, as in al-Quniyah and al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage covers three interrelated rulings regarding the dower. First, any increase to the dower made after the contract is legally binding (wajib) upon the husband, provided the wife accepts it in the same session, knows the amount, and the marriage still exists. The increase is valid even if the original dower was already gifted or discharged. Zufar's disagreement on the obligation is rejected; the Quranic verse 'in whatever you mutually agree after the prescribed obligation' (al-Nisa 4:24) is cited as proof. Second, if divorce occurs before consummation, only the original dower is halved; the increase does not halve. Abu Yusuf initially disagreed, but the Hanafi position relies on the Quranic verse 'give half of what you prescribed' (al-Baqarah 2:237), where 'prescribed' refers to the dower fixed at the contract, not subsequent increases. Third, the wife may validly remit (hitt) the dower, whether in part or entirely, after the contract. Her remission is effective, based on Quran 4:4. However, the remission is revocable if the husband rejects it, similar to discharge (ibra'). The passage thus ensures clarity on how post-contract modifications affect the dower obligation.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): An increase to the dower made after the marriage contract, which becomes obligatory upon the husband.
الفريضة (al-faridah): The prescribed dower fixed at the time of the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on an increase to the dower if divorce occurs before consummation?
A) It is halved along with the original dower
B) It drops completely and is not paid
C) It remains fully obligatory
D) It is doubled

Key Takeaway
Post-contract dower increases are binding and not halved upon pre-consummation divorce; only the originally prescribed dower is halved.

Wife's Remission of Mahr (Hitt)
Ruling on wife's remission of dower with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the validity and conditions of the wife's remission (hitt) of the dower after the marriage contract, and state the effect of the husband's rejection.

Core Idea
A wife's remission of the mahr is valid but revocable if the husband rejects it.

This lesson focuses on the wife's right to remit the dower (hitt) after the marriage contract. The passage establishes that such remission is valid based on Quran 4:4, and once accepted by the husband, the dower obligation is discharged. However, if the husband rejects the remission, it is revoked, similar to the rule for ibra'. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the dynamics of post-contract adjustments to the dower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of remission (hitt)
The passage defines hitt as the woman dropping the dower from the husband's liability. Recognize that this is a post-contract act.
The text says 'حطها' meaning her remission.
2
State the ruling and its proof
The remission is valid and effective. The proof is Quran 4:4: 'if they willingly give up of it something'.
The verse supports the wife's voluntary remission.
3
Note the condition of husband's acceptance
Although the remission is valid, it is revocable in case of the husband's rejection. Understand that the act is like a gift that requires acceptance.
The text likens it to ibra' (discharge).
4
Understand the consequence of rejection
If the husband rejects the remission, it is revoked and the dower remains due. This is different from an unconditional gift.
The text says 'يرتد الحط برد الزوج' – the remission is revoked by the husband's refusal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage covers three interrelated rulings regarding the dower. First, any increase to the dower made after the contract is legally binding (wajib) upon the husband, provided the wife accepts it in the same session, knows the amount, and the marriage still exists. The increase is valid even if the original dower was already gifted or discharged. Zufar's disagreement on the obligation is rejected; the Quranic verse 'in whatever you mutually agree after the prescribed obligation' (al-Nisa 4:24) is cited as proof. Second, if divorce occurs before consummation, only the original dower is halved; the increase does not halve. Abu Yusuf initially disagreed, but the Hanafi position relies on the Quranic verse 'give half of what you prescribed' (al-Baqarah 2:237), where 'prescribed' refers to the dower fixed at the contract, not subsequent increases. Third, the wife may validly remit (hitt) the dower, whether in part or entirely, after the contract. Her remission is effective, based on Quran 4:4. However, the remission is revocable if the husband rejects it, similar to discharge (ibra'). The passage thus ensures clarity on how post-contract modifications affect the dower obligation.

Key Terms
الحط (al-hitt): The wife's remission of the dower (or part of it) from the husband's liability after the contract.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Discharge of a debt; in this context, similar to hitt but from the creditor's side. The same rule of revocation by rejection applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the husband rejects the wife's remission of the dower?
A) The remission is still valid and the dower is discharged
B) The remission is revoked and the dower remains due
C) The dower is halved
D) The wife must pay compensation

Key Takeaway
The wife's remission of the dower is valid but revocable upon the husband's rejection; acceptance is required for finality.

Increase of Mahr: Conditions and Obligation
Commentary on the obligation and conditions of mahr increase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid post-contract mahr increase and explain the Hanafi proof for its obligation.

Core Idea
A mahr increase after marriage is wajib upon the husband once accepted, validated by mutual agreement (Quran 4:24).

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on increasing the mahr after the marriage contract. The commentator clarifies that such an increase is valid and binding, provided certain conditions are met. We will explore the conditions, the proof from the Quran, and the disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is increasing the mahr after the contract. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) under conditions.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites Quran 4:24: 'except regarding what you mutually agree upon after the prescribed obligation.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'تراضيتم به من بعد الفريضة' indicates that mutual agreement after the prescribed mahr is permissible, thus validating the increase.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Zufar disagreed on obligation; the Hanafi response dismisses his view as baseless.
Intra-Hanafi difference.
5
State the conditions
The increase is obligatory only if: wife accepts in the session, husband knows the amount, and marriage continues at that time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : زيد على المهر: أي المسمى عن العقد، ولو كان بلا شهود أو بعد هبة المهر والإبراء منه سواء كان من جنس المهر أو غير جنسه ، وسواء كانت الزيادة من الزوج أو وليه، فقد صرحوا بأن الأب والجد لو زوج ابنَه ثم زاد في المهر صح. كذا في «النهر» و«البحر»(۱). ولا يشترط لفظ : الزيادة، بل تصح بلفظها ، وبقوله : راجعتك بكذا إن قبلت، كذا في «أنفع الوسائل»، وذكر في «الخانية»: إنه لو وهبته مهرها، ثم أقر بكذا وقبلت صح، ويحمل على الزيادة. [٢] قوله : يجب ؛ أي على الزوج لكن بشرط قبول الزوجة في المجلس أو ولي الصغيرة، ومعرفته قدر الزيادة، وبقاء الزوجية حين الزيادة. وكذا في «النهر»، وفي وجوب الزيادة خلاف زفر ، ولا وجه له، ويدلُّ على قولنا قوله الا : فيما تراضيتُم بِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ الْفَرِيضَةِ (٢). [٣] قوله : بالطلاق ؛ يعني إذا طلق قبل الوطء يجب نصف الأصل فقط ولا يتنصفُ الزائد، وفيه خلافُ أبي يوسف الله في قوله الأول، وحجتنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في سورة الطلاق قبل الدخول : فَيَصفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ (٣) ، فإنَّ الظاهر أن الفرض محمول على الفرض المعتاد، وهو الفرضُ عند العقد فلا يتنصفُ ما زيد عليه بعده. (۳) [٤] قوله : حطها ; - بالفتح وتشديد الطاء :- بمعنى الإسقاط : يعني إذا أسقطت المرأة المهر عن الزوج بعد العقد صح ذلك، وسقط ذلك القدر المحطوط، وإن كان كل المهر عن ذمته ؛ لقوله ال: فَإِن طِبْنَ لَكُمْ عَن شَيْءٍ مِنْهُ نَفْسًا فَكُلُوهُ هَنِتَا قَرِينَا ويرتد الحط وكذا الإبراء برد الزوج، كما في «القُنية» و«البحر». (۱) «البحر الرائق (٣: ١٦٠). (۲) النساء: من الآية ٢٤ . (۳) البقرة : من الآية ۲۳۷ (٤) النساء : من الآية . (٤)  ١٢٤ وخلوة بلا مانع وطء عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية [1] ولم يذكر " مفعول الحطّ ليدل على العموم، كما في قوله : فلانٌ يُعطي ويمنع ، ، فيدلُّ على حطّ كل المهر وبعضه ، والزيادة" في صورة زاد على المهر عنه. وخلوة بلا مانع وطء [١] قوله : ولم يُذكر : بصيغة المجهول فما بعده نائب مناب فاعله، أو بصيغة المعلوم ففاعله الضمير الراجع إلى المصنف له، وما بعده مفعول. [٢] قوله : ليدل على العموم ؛ فإن حذف المفعول قد يكون لإفادة التعميم والإطلاق كما في قولهم في مدح الأسخياء العقلاء : فلان يعطي ويمنع : أي يعطي كلَّ شيء نافع ويمنع كل ضار، فإنّه لو ذكر المفعول في أمثال هذا لإفادة التخصيص. [۳] قوله : والزيادة ؛ أي حط الزيادة التي زادها الزوج بعد العقد. [٤] قوله : وخلوة ؛ شروع في بيان ما يؤكد المهر غير الوطء، والأصل في هذا الباب قوله : وَإِن أَردتُمُ اسْتِبْدَالَ زَوْجٍ مَكَانَ زَوج وَمَاتَيْتُمْ إِحْدَتْهُنَّ قِنطَارًا فَلَا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا ) إلى أن قال : وَكَيْفَ تَأْخُذُونَهُ، وَقَدْ أَفْضَى بَعْضُكُمْ إِلَى بعض ) ، فإن الإفضاء مفسر بالخلوة. (۱) وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : «من كشف خمر امرأة ونظر إليها فقد وجب الصداق دخل بها أو لم يدخل) ، أخرجه الدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ بسند ضعيف ، وأبو داود في «مراسيله» بإسناد رجاله ثقات. (۲)
His statement: 'Increased upon the mahr' means the named (mahr) from the contract, even if it was without witnesses or after gifting the mahr and releasing from it, whether the increase is from the same type as the mahr or different, and whether the increase is from the husband or his guardian. They explicitly stated that if the father or grandfather married off his son and then increased the mahr, it is valid. Likewise in 'al-Nahr' and 'al-Bahr' (1). The wording 'increase' is not required; rather it is valid with its wording, and with his statement: 'I return to you for such-and-such if you accept,' as in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il'. And it is mentioned in 'al-Khaniyya': If she gifted him her mahr, then he acknowledged something and she accepted, it is valid, and it is interpreted as an increase. [2] His statement: 'It is obligatory' means upon the husband, but with the condition of the wife's acceptance in the session or the guardian of the minor, and his knowledge of the amount of the increase, and the continuation of the marriage at the time of the increase. Likewise in 'al-Nahr'. And there is a disagreement with Zufar regarding the obligation of the increase, and it has no basis. And what indicates our statement is His saying: 'except regarding what you mutually agree upon after the prescribed obligation' (2). [3] His statement: 'with divorce' means if he divorces before consummation, only half of the original is obligatory and the increase is not halved. And there is a disagreement of Abu Yusuf in his first statement. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the surah of divorce before consummation: 'then you give half of what you prescribed' (3). For the apparent meaning is that the prescribed (mahr) is interpreted as the usual prescribed, which is the prescribed at the contract, so what is increased after it is not halved. (3) [4] His statement: 'her remission' - with fatha and tashdid of ta - meaning cancellation: i.e., if the woman remits the mahr from the husband after the contract, that is valid, and that amount remitted falls off, even if it was the entire mahr from his liability; due to His saying: 'But if they give up willingly to you anything of it, then consume it with enjoyment and pleasure' (4). And the remission and likewise the release are revocable by the husband's rejection, as in 'al-Qunniya' and 'al-Bahr'. (1) 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' (3:160). (2) Women: from verse 24. (3) al-Baqara: from verse 237. (4) Women: from verse 4. And seclusion without a barrier to intercourse. 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. [1] His statement: 'And it was not mentioned' means the object of 'remission' is not mentioned to indicate generality, as in the saying: 'So-and-so gives and withholds' so it indicates the remission of all of the mahr or part of it, and the increase in the case where he increased upon the mahr. And seclusion without a barrier to intercourse. [1] His statement: 'And it was not mentioned' - in the passive voice, so what follows is a substitute for the doer, or in the active voice, so its agent is the pronoun referring to the author, and what follows is the object. [2] His statement: 'to indicate generality' - for the omission of the object may be for the purpose of generalization and absoluteness as in their praise of generous, intelligent people: 'So-and-so gives and withholds' i.e., he gives every beneficial thing and withholds every harmful thing, for if he mentioned the object in such examples it would indicate specification. [3] His statement: 'and the increase' i.e., the remission of the increase that the husband added after the contract. [4] His statement: 'and seclusion' - a beginning in explaining what confirms the mahr besides intercourse. The basis in this chapter is His saying: 'And if you wish to substitute one wife in place of another and you have given one of them a great amount, do not take anything from it' until He said: 'And how can you take it while you have gone in unto each other?' (1) For 'going in' is interpreted as seclusion. (2) And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever uncovered a woman and looked at her, then the bridal gift becomes obligatory, whether he entered upon her or did not enter' - narrated by al-Daraqutni with a weak chain, and by Abu Dawud in his 'Mursalat' with a chain whose narrators are trustworthy.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah regarding the rulings of the mahr (dower) in the chapter of marriage. The commentator explains the matn line by line. The matn states: 'Whatever is increased upon the mahr is obligatory, and it falls off by divorce before intercourse, and her remission of it is valid.' The commentary first defines 'increase upon the mahr' as an addition to the named mahr from the contract, regardless of whether witnesses were present, or after the wife has gifted the mahr or released the husband from it. The increase can be from the same type of mahr or a different type, and the person making the increase can be the husband or his guardian (such as the father or grandfather marrying off his son). The increase is valid even without using the word 'increase'; it can be expressed as 'I return to you for such-and-such if you accept.' The condition for the increase to be obligatory on the husband is the wife's acceptance in the same session (or the guardian's acceptance if she is a minor), the husband's knowledge of the amount, and the continuation of the marriage at the time of the increase. There is a disagreement with Zufar who denied the obligation of such an increase, but the commentator dismisses it as baseless and supports the Hanafi position with the verse from Surah al-Nisa' (4:24): 'except regarding what you mutually agree upon after the prescribed obligation.' The commentary then addresses the effect of divorce before consummation: the original mahr (the one fixed at the contract) is halved, but the increase added later is not halved—it falls off entirely. This is based on the Prophet's interpretation of the verse in Surah al-Baqarah (2:237) regarding divorce before consummation: 'then give half of what you prescribed.' The 'prescribed' is interpreted as the mahr fixed at the contract, so the increase is not subject to halving. Abu Yusuf initially differed but the Hanafi position is established. Next, the commentary explains the wife's remission (hatt) of the mahr: if she voluntarily remits all or part of the mahr after the contract, it is valid and the husband is released from that amount. The proof is the verse from Surah al-Nisa' (4:4): 'But if they give up willingly to you anything of it, then consume it with enjoyment and pleasure.' However, the remission is revocable if the husband rejects it, as mentioned in the sources. Finally, the commentary introduces the concept of khalwa (seclusion) as a factor that confirms the full mahr, even without intercourse. The basis is the verse in Surah al-Nisa' (4:20-21) where 'going in unto each other' is interpreted as seclusion. Additionally, a hadith narrated by al-Daraqutni and Abu Dawud states that if a man uncovers a woman (i.e., removes her head covering) and looks at her, the full bridal gift becomes obligatory, whether or not he actually entered upon her. The chain is considered weak but is supported by other narrations.

Key Terms
المهر المسمى (al-mahr al-musammā): The mahr that is explicitly named and agreed upon at the time of the marriage contract.
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An increase in the mahr offered by the husband or his guardian after the marriage contract has been concluded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for a post-contract mahr increase to be obligatory?
A) The increase must be in writing
B) The husband must have witnesses
C) The wife must accept in the same session
D) The increase must be equal to the original mahr

Key Takeaway
A post-contract mahr increase is wajib on the husband if the wife accepts in the session, he knows the amount, and the marriage continues.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Effect of Divorce on Increased Mahr
Commentary on the halving of mahr upon pre-consummation divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the mahr liability upon pre-consummation divorce when an increase has been made, and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Upon pre-consummation divorce, only the original mahr is halved; the post-contract increase drops entirely.

This lesson focuses on a specific consequence of mahr increase: what happens if the husband divorces before consummation? The Hanafi school holds that the increase is not subject to halving; it falls off completely. We will examine the evidence from the Prophet's interpretation of the Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Divorce before consummation after a mahr increase.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Only half of the original mahr is obligatory; the increase is not halved and drops entirely.
3
Identify the dalil
The Prophet's explanation of Quran 2:237: 'then give half of what you prescribed.'
4
Analyze the proof
The word 'فَرَضْتُمْ' (you prescribed) refers to the mahr fixed at the contract, not subsequent increases.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf initially held that the increase also halves, but the later view (mufta bihi) is that it does not.

Source Text

قوله : زيد على المهر: أي المسمى عن العقد، ولو كان بلا شهود أو بعد هبة المهر والإبراء منه سواء كان من جنس المهر أو غير جنسه ، وسواء كانت الزيادة من الزوج أو وليه، فقد صرحوا بأن الأب والجد لو زوج ابنَه ثم زاد في المهر صح. كذا في «النهر» و«البحر»(۱). ولا يشترط لفظ : الزيادة، بل تصح بلفظها ، وبقوله : راجعتك بكذا إن قبلت، كذا في «أنفع الوسائل»، وذكر في «الخانية»: إنه لو وهبته مهرها، ثم أقر بكذا وقبلت صح، ويحمل على الزيادة. [٢] قوله : يجب ؛ أي على الزوج لكن بشرط قبول الزوجة في المجلس أو ولي الصغيرة، ومعرفته قدر الزيادة، وبقاء الزوجية حين الزيادة. وكذا في «النهر»، وفي وجوب الزيادة خلاف زفر ، ولا وجه له، ويدلُّ على قولنا قوله الا : فيما تراضيتُم بِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِ الْفَرِيضَةِ (٢). His statement: 'Increased upon the mahr' means the named (mahr) from the contract, even if it was without witnesses or after gifting the mahr and releasing from it, whether the increase is from the same type as the mahr or different, and whether the increase is from the husband or his guardian. They explicitly stated that if the father or grandfather married off his son and then increased the mahr, it is valid. Likewise in 'al-Nahr' and 'al-Bahr' (1). The wording 'increase' is not required; rather it is valid with its wording, and with his statement: 'I return to you for such-and-such if you accept,' as in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il'. And it is mentioned in 'al-Khaniyya': If she gifted him her mahr, then he acknowledged something and she accepted, it is valid, and it is interpreted as an increase. [2] His statement: 'It is obligatory' means upon the husband, but with the condition of the wife's acceptance in the session or the guardian of the minor, and his knowledge of the amount of the increase, and the continuation of the marriage at the time of the increase. Likewise in 'al-Nahr'. And there is a disagreement with Zufar regarding the obligation of the increase, and it has no basis. And what indicates our statement is His saying: 'except regarding what you mutually agree upon after the prescribed obligation' (2). And there is a disagreement of Abu Yusuf in his first statement. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the surah of divorce before consummation: 'then you give half of what you prescribed' (3). For the apparent meaning is that the prescribed (mahr) is interpreted as the usual prescribed, which is the prescribed at the contract, so what is increased after it is not halved. (3) [4] His statement: 'her remission' - with fatha and tashdid of ta - meaning cancellation: i.e., if the woman remits the mahr from the husband after the contract, that is valid, and that amount remitted falls off, even if it was the entire mahr from his liability; due to His saying: 'But if they give up willingly to you anything of it, then consume it with enjoyment and pleasure' (4). [2] His statement: 'to indicate generality' - for the omission of the object may be for the purpose of generalization and absoluteness as in their praise of generous, intelligent people: 'So-and-so gives and withholds' i.e., he gives every beneficial thing and withholds every harmful thing, for if he mentioned the object in such examples it would indicate specification. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Wiqayah regarding the rulings of the mahr (dower) in the chapter of marriage. The commentator explains the matn line by line. The matn states: 'Whatever is increased upon the mahr is obligatory, and it falls off by divorce before intercourse, and her remission of it is valid.' The commentary first defines 'increase upon the mahr' as an addition to the named mahr from the contract, regardless of whether witnesses were present, or after the wife has gifted the mahr or released the husband from it. The increase can be from the same type of mahr or a different type, and the person making the increase can be the husband or his guardian (such as the father or grandfather marrying off his son). The increase is valid even without using the word 'increase'; it can be expressed as 'I return to you for such-and-such if you accept.' The condition for the increase to be obligatory on the husband is the wife's acceptance in the same session (or the guardian's acceptance if she is a minor), the husband's knowledge of the amount, and the continuation of the marriage at the time of the increase. There is a disagreement with Zufar who denied the obligation of such an increase, but the commentator dismisses it as baseless and supports the Hanafi position with the verse from Surah al-Nisa' (4:24): 'except regarding what you mutually agree upon after the prescribed obligation.' The 'prescribed' is interpreted as the mahr fixed at the contract, so the increase is not subject to halving. Abu Yusuf initially differed but the Hanafi position is established. Next, the commentary explains the wife's remission (hatt) of the mahr: if she voluntarily remits all or part of the mahr after the contract, it is valid and the husband is released from that amount. The proof is the verse from Surah al-Nisa' (4:4): 'But if they give up willingly to you anything of it, then consume it with enjoyment and pleasure.' However, the remission is revocable if the husband rejects it, as mentioned in the sources. Finally, the commentary introduces the concept of khalwa (seclusion) as a factor that confirms the full mahr, even without intercourse. The basis is the verse in Surah al-Nisa' (4:20-21) where 'going in unto each other' is interpreted as seclusion. The chain is considered weak but is supported by other narrations.

Key Terms
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An increase in the mahr offered by the husband after the marriage contract.
الطلاق قبل الدخول (al-ṭalāq qabl al-dukhūl): Divorce pronounced before consummation of the marriage.

Upon pre-consummation divorce, the husband must pay:
A) half of the increased mahr

Key Takeaway
Upon divorce before consummation, only the mahr prescribed at the contract is halved; any post-contract increase is dropped entirely.
